# Deep assessment — `causal-marketing-pymc`

> **Method.** A 19-way parallel review (one demanding reviewer per notebook, two extra
> adversarial-statistics lenses on the anchors, plus reviews of the `src/cmp` statistical
> core, the DGP/policy/plots layer, the tests/CI/reports infrastructure, the marimo apps,
> and a claim-by-claim check of the README). Every **critical** and **statistical/code
> major** finding was then routed to an independent adversarial verifier that re-read the
> artifact and, where possible, re-ran the DGP + estimator code to reproduce the numbers.
> **107 agents, 88 verifications, 0 findings refuted.** Reviewers graded statistical
> watertightness hardest (per the brief: *watertight stats, business-first presentation*).

**Totals (verified, survived refutation):** 27 critical · 95 major · 69 minor · 19 polish.

The two anchor notebooks were each read by two independent reviewers; their criticals
converge on the same defects, so the unique critical count is lower than the raw total —
that convergence is evidence the defects are real, not reviewer noise.

> **Status — P0 fixes applied (2026-07-08).** The pre-lecture "screen-refutes-speaker + wrong
> headline numbers" tier of the fix roadmap has been implemented and re-verified by re-executing
> the affected notebooks. Cells marked `→` in the scorecard changed. See
> **[P0 fixes applied — scorecard delta](#p0-fixes-applied--scorecard-delta)** below for the
> finding-by-finding record. P1–P3 findings are unchanged; a full re-grade awaits a workflow re-run.

---

## P0 fixes applied — scorecard delta

The first fix tier — the pre-lecture "screen-refutes-speaker + wrong headline numbers" set — is
**done and re-verified by re-executing the affected notebooks in FAST mode** (nb01 on `cmp-core`;
nb06/09/10 on `cmp-legacy`), regenerating their PDFs, and running the test suite green (22 package +
notebook tests, plus 2 new regression guards). The single most consequential outcome: **nb06's headline
budget call flipped.** The buggy probability compared brand_search's posterior draws against TV's *scalar
mean* and read **P = 0.96 → "reallocate toward TV"**; the correct draw-wise computation gives **P = 0.73**,
which is below the 0.8 action bar, so the honest call is now **"test before reallocating."**

| # | Finding (severity) | Artifact(s) | Before | After |
|---|---|---|:--:|:--:|
| 1 | Bake-off read-out names BCF the winner; table shows the opposite (**critical**) | nb01, Anchor-A lens | narrative ⊥ table | run-stable, number-free read-out that matches the table |
| 2 | E-value inverted fallback + computed on the planted truth → "5.76" (**critical**) | nb01, `metrics.py`, cmp-stats | fabricated 5.76 | VanderWeele `sd`-standardized on the AIPW *estimate* → **≈ 2.0**; fallback removed, `sd` now required |
| 3 | 2-D sensitivity contour hard-coded `τ̄ + G·D·0.9` (**major**) | nb01, Anchor-A lens | drawn-in surface | **genuinely refit** OVB surface (new independent `conf_t`/`conf_y` DGP channels); black cost line is real geometry |
| 4 | Policy table `round(0)` shows frac 1.0 / 0.0 (**major**) | nb01, Anchor-A lens | 1.0 / 0.0 | euros + `frac_contacted` as % (47%, 29%, …) |
| 5 | "random-50%" baseline coupled to the DGP RNG stream (**critical**) | `policy.py`, cmp-dgp | +1414 (a recency rule) | independent `SeedSequence` spawn → **−712 ≈ ½ treat-all**; regression test added |
| 6 | Segment truth stated as €3/€12 "at average engagement" (**critical**) | nb02 | contradicts €7/€16 output | corrected to €3/€12 at *zero* engagement, €7/€16 at average |
| 7 | `P(TV ROI > brand_search)` = point-vs-draws (**critical**) | nb06 | **0.96 → "reallocate"** | draw-wise **0.73 → "test first"**; narrative + README aligned |
| 8 | "TV's interval sits above break-even" (**critical**) | nb06 | false (CI [0.29, 8.02]) | states TV straddles 1×, brand_search entirely below |
| 9 | Placebo cutoffs hard-coded "(≈0)", no SE (**critical**) | nb09, `estimators` | eyeballed | **t-stats + 90% error bars**; €130 placebo shown as t = 0.90 (noise), not "≈0" |
| 10 | "Bandwidth-stable +12.0%" vs a curve that doubles (**major**) | nb09 | overstated | honest "+7.2%…+14.9%, drifts mildly but stays positive" |
| 11 | Residual ACF computed on a rolling mean (leaves the weekly cycle in) (**critical**) | nb10 | spurious 8/10 lags out of band | **model residuals** → 0/10 out of band, honest "≈ white" |
| 12 | Cell-9 validation figure never emitted (**critical**) | nb10 | no image in notebook/PDF | figure emitted (explicit `plt.show()`); PDF regenerated |
| 13 | Two marimo apps end plot cells on `fig.tight_layout()` → blank (**critical**) | apps | no chart renders | dedicated `fig` display cell added to both |

**What this changes in the scorecard:** watertightness rises on the five touched notebooks (nb01 2→3,
nb02 3→4, nb06 2→3, nb09 3→4, nb10 2→3), nb10's diagnostics rises (2→3, the ACF is now a *real* check),
and **nb06's grade moves weak→adequate** because its headline decision is now statistically correct.
Two new regression guards (`test_e_value_requires_sd`, `test_random_baseline_is_independent`) lock in
fixes 2 and 5.

## P1 fixes applied — the truth-recovery failures

The second tier — **pattern A, "recover the truth fails, unacknowledged"** — is done and re-verified by
re-execution. In every case the committed run had the planted truth sitting *outside* a nominally-90%
interval under a title claiming recovery; each is now honestly recovered, and the root cause was fixed in
the estimator or the fit, not papered over in prose.

| # | Notebook | Before (truth outside interval) | Root cause | After (truth recovered) |
|---|---|:--:|---|:--:|
| 1 | **00 Foundations** — estimator ladder | AIPW 90% CI [5.29, 5.89] excludes true €6 (seed 17); title says "converges on the truth" | single-seed figure sold as if it proved unbiasedness | **multi-seed** panel: naive stays biased (+3.4), regression/IPW/AIPW centre on €6 (bias ≈ −0.1), AIPW covers truth in ~80% of samples — the honest meaning of "unbiased." "Credible interval" relabelled a bootstrap CI. |
| 2 | **07 Geo-lift (Anchor B ⭐)** | total €305k, 90% CI [279, 333] excludes true €339k; per-week band covers only ~45% | `effect = target − W_post@donors` used **weight uncertainty only**, dropping the counterfactual's observation noise | band is now a **posterior predictive** (adds `Normal(0, sd)`): truth inside [272, 342], **per-week coverage ~86%**. A multi-seed check honestly exposes that the *total* interval still covers only ~40% (SC's sample variance ≫ any single posterior), so the calibrated inference is the **placebo permutation test** — which *reinforces* "confirm with a second geo test." |
| 3 | **08 Rollout DiD** | Bayesian €327, CI [302, 353] excludes true €400; labelled "priors mildly shrink it" | CausalPy 0.8.1 fixed priors `β~N(0,50), σ~HalfNormal(1)` mis-scaled for €1000 revenue → shrink + too-narrow | **standardize revenue** before the fit, back-transform → €389, CI [275, 515] covers €400 and now **agrees with the 2×2 (€390)**. |
| 4 | **11 Endogenous IV** | Bayesian IV €16.6, CI [15.5, 17.8] excludes true €15 (~3.3× too narrow) | CausalPy centres IV priors on the 2SLS point with σ=1 (overconfident) | **weakly-informative priors** `{mus:[0,0], sigmas:[50,50]}` → €18.1, CI [14.8, 22.2] covers €15, and its **width matches the frequentist Wald SE**. |

**Shared-code fixes:** `estimators.synthetic_control` now returns a posterior-predictive counterfactual
(with `counterfactual_mean` exposed separately); `estimators.iv` gained `priors=`/`binary_treatment=`
pass-through with a docstring warning about CausalPy's overconfident defaults. A `FAST` switch was added to
nb00 (it previously had none) so the multi-seed loop scales for CI. All re-verified: **20/20 package tests
green, the four notebooks re-execute clean, PDFs regenerated.**

**What this changes in the scorecard:** validation rises on nb00/07/08/11 (multi-seed recovery + honest
coverage now present), watertightness rises on the same four (the headline figures no longer contradict the
truth). **Anchor B is now genuinely watertight** on its core recovery claim, with the total-interval
limitation disclosed rather than hidden — arguably a stronger lecture than a clean pass.

## P2 fixes applied — sensitivity/diagnostics watertightness + business depth

The third tier: the remaining statistical-watertightness gaps (patterns C/D) and the thin business steps
(pattern F). Done and re-verified by re-execution (21/21 package tests, +1 new guard).

| # | Finding (severity) | Notebook | Fix |
|---|---|---|---|
| 1 | Incoherent confounding ρ-sweep — code contradicts its comment, freezes one lever, bakes in "ROBUST" (**critical**) | nb04 | **Coherent** M–Y sweep: bias propagated through *both* levers that share the engagement→converted edge, per posterior draw. It now reveals a *real* fragility (engagement's lead over activation flips at ~55% of the edge) instead of a manufactured robustness. |
| 2 | Lever ranking is unit-dependent, no cost model (**critical, business**) | nb04 | Show €/unit **and** €/SD (they *reverse*) and rank by **ROI on a stated cost-to-move**, with `P(ROI>1)`. |
| 3 | "100% mediated" forced by omitting the direct edge (**major**) | nb04 | Include the direct onboarding→converted edge and **test it** — NDE = 0.06 [−0.03, 0.15] includes 0, so 100%-mediated is now *discovered*. Also corrected the false "simulates through the graph" claim (it's product-of-coefficients). |
| 4 | Sensitivity contour can't cross zero (bias ≤ 1 vs a €6 effect) (**major**) | nb05 | Widen the γ·δ grid to (0,3)² so the zero-crossing line actually exists. |
| 5 | E-value bar mixes a €6 effect and a 3.3× risk-ratio on one "RR-scale" axis (**major**) | nb05 | Plot only RR-scale quantities (E-value vs the 1.0 no-confounding baseline). |
| 6 | "Decide in euros" had no euros (**major, business**) | nb05 | Price the control choice: budgeting on the naive €9.45 vs the correct €6.09 books **€168k** of phantom lift on a 50k campaign. |
| 7 | "Posterior predictive check" drawn from a grand-mean constant, not the model (**major**) | nb01 | `bcf(return_full=True)` now returns the fitted `mu`/`sd`; the PPC draws genuine replicates `Normal(mu_draw, sd_draw)`. |
| 8 | "McCrary test" is a two-bin count ratio with unit-dependent smoothing (**major**) | nb09 | Proper density-continuity **binomial z-test** (no-manip z=+0.2; injected sorting z≈+14), scale-invariant log-ratio; +2 tests. |
| 9 | Business-depth gaps (**major, several**) | nb00, nb03, nb07 | nb00 now makes the €8-cost go/no-go the confounding flips; nb03 computes a scale-free **+21% profit uplift** [13,30] and fixes the conditional/unconditional posterior mix; nb07 prices the confirmatory test — **VOI + sizing (~27 markets, a lower bound)**. |

*Deferred as minor:* nb02 / nb11 single-cost decisions could gain a cost sweep (low value). `estimators.bcf`
gained a `return_full` option and `mccrary_density` now returns a z-stat (both backward-compatible defaults).

### Still open after P0 + P1 + P2

- **FAST-mode convergence suppression (pattern E)** — the one remaining large job: `compute_convergence_checks=False`
  is still hard-set and committed outputs are FAST-mode; a FULL-mode reference run with r-hat/ESS reported is
  deliberately deferred as the slow dual-environment step.
- **Infrastructure (pattern G, P3)** — CI still cannot run (wrong directory + `main` vs `master`), test deps not
  installed by `uv sync`, notebook tests skip silently, no kernelspec-drift guard, `plots.py` mojibake.

---

## Seven systemic patterns

Almost every critical is an instance of one of these. Fix the pattern, fix the repo.

**A. "Recover the truth" fails, unacknowledged (00, 06, 07, 08, 11).** The repo's signature
move — plant a known effect, show the method recover it — silently fails on the committed
run, with the truth line outside the interval *on the projected figure*, under a title
claiming success. Root causes are structural (SC band omits observation noise;
CausalPy default priors mis-scaled for €1,000 revenue; IV fits a continuous model to binary
exposure) — not bad luck. For 07 (Anchor B) an honest band likely flips the headline
"TEST FURTHER" to "GO": the borderline decision is an artifact of undercoverage.

**B. The screen refutes the speaker (01, 02, 06, 07, 09).** Narrative claims contradicted
by the printed output on the same page/slide (e.g. Anchor A's read-out names BCF the winner
while the table above shows the T-learner ahead on all three cited metrics).

**C. Broken or fabricated sensitivity analyses (01, 04, 05, metrics.py).** The E-value
fallback is directionally inverted; Anchor A's 2-D contour is a hard-coded surface, not a
computation; nb04's confounding sweep bakes in "ROBUST" by construction.

**D. Probability / policy numbers computed wrong (01, 06, 07, policy.py).** P=0.96 in nb06
compares draws against a scalar mean; the "random-50%" baseline in Anchor A is coupled to
the DGP's RNG stream and is actually a recency-targeting rule; `go_no_go` labels net value
as "ROI".

**E. FAST-mode committed outputs with suppressed convergence evidence (01–11, cmp).**
`compute_convergence_checks=False` in every fitter; visible r-hat/ESS warnings (nb06 also
16 divergences) never addressed; the report generator strips the warnings that would
disclose it — awkward for a deck selling "honest uncertainty."

**F. The euro/business step is thinner than the README promises (00, 03, 04, 05, 07, 09).**
Missing VOI/sizing, missing profit computation, unit-dependent lever rankings, unanswered
decision questions.

**G. Infrastructure can't catch any of this (infra, apps).** CI has never run (wrong
directory + wrong branch); `uv sync` omits test deps; notebook tests skip silently and
contain zero asserts; two of three apps never render their figure.

---

## Recommended fix roadmap

**P0 — before any lecture (screen-refutes-speaker + wrong headline numbers).** Cheap, surgical edits:
- Rewrite the bake-off read-out to match the table (nb01); ideally generate it programmatically from `bake`.
- Fix the E-value call to use the `sd=` branch on an *estimate*, and fix/delete the inverted no-`sd` fallback in `metrics.e_value` (nb01, `src/cmp/metrics.py`).
- Replace the hard-coded 2-D "contour" with a real computed surface or delete it (nb01).
- Decouple the `policy_comparison` random-baseline RNG from the DGP stream (`src/cmp/policy.py`), re-run Anchor A's policy table.
- Compute `P(TV ROI > BS ROI)` draw-wise; update the number here and in the README (nb06).
- Correct the "TV interval sits above break-even" sentence (nb06).
- Add SEs to the placebo cutoffs and reword the hard-coded "(≈0)" (nb09).
- Fix the €3/€12-at-average-engagement misstatement (nb02).
- Emit cell 9's figure (nb10) and add a trailing `fig` display to the two silent marimo apps.

**P1 — watertightness (the five truth-recovery failures).** Requires re-execution:
- Add posterior-predictive observation noise to the synthetic-control counterfactual band, or explicitly state it is a mean-blend band and widen the decision interval (nb07, `src/cmp/estimators.py`).
- Demean/standardize revenue before the CausalPy DiD/ITS fits and back-transform (nb08, nb10); pass data-scaled or genuinely weak priors for IV, or use `binary_treatment=True` (nb11).
- Re-commit **FULL-mode** outputs with r-hat/ESS/divergences reported (stop hard-disabling `compute_convergence_checks`); regenerate PDFs.
- Add a multi-seed recovery + 90%-coverage loop to every notebook's validate step.

**P2 — depth vs the four-axes bar.** Real VOI/test-sizing in Anchor B (nb07); a cost-to-move model + per-euro lever ranking (nb04); an expected-profit computation in the decide step (nb03, nb05); an honest reading of the coverage-by-decile failure (nb01); a model-based (not rolling-mean) residual ACF (nb10); PPC drawn from the actual fitted model (nb01).

**P3 — infrastructure.** Relocate CI to the monorepo git root with a `master` trigger and `working-directory`; move `pytest`/`nbmake` into a dependency-group so `uv sync` installs them; fail (not skip) when a notebook kernel is missing; add a kernelspec-drift guard and a figure-presence check; lockfile the legacy env; fix the mojibake in `plots.py`.

---

## Per-artifact detail

### Notebook 00 — Foundations

**Grade: good** · 1 critical · 5 major · 10 findings total

| Diagnostics | Business | Narration | Validation | Watertight |
|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|
| 2 | 2 | 5 | 2 | 3 |

Notebook 00 is a conceptually excellent, fully reproducible vocabulary chapter: potential-outcomes missing-data table, randomized-vs-observational contrast, DAG gallery, and a 4-rung estimator ladder, all with correct formulas and honestly stated assumptions (every committed number re-derives exactly from the seeded DGPs). But it falls short of the cookbook's watertight bar in three verifiable places: the headline ladder figure claims convergence on the truth while its only displayed interval — reproduced as [5.29, 5.89] — excludes the known ATE of 6.0 with no acknowledgment; that interval is called a "credible interval" when it is a bootstrap confidence interval; and the cell-6 bars carry no uncertainty while the print labels a visibly-off €4.8 estimate "(unbiased)". The business axis is thin by design but leaves an obvious win on the table (COST=8.0 is defined, never used — true ATE €5.6 < €8 cost while the confounded naive €11.4 says profitable). The gated LaLonde section verifiably works (naive -$635, adjusted +$1,548, toward the ~$1,800 experimental truth) but the committed PDF only shows the skip message, so the real-data punchline never appears in the lecture artifact.

**Strengths.**
- Conceptual narration is flagship-grade: the three-customer missing-data table, precise unconfoundedness/positivity/SUTVA statements, the g-formula, do-operator vs conditioning, backdoor/mediator/collider distinctions, and the 'Bayes sharpens estimation, never identification' discipline callout are all correct, compact, and MBA-followable.
- Full reproducibility: every committed number was independently re-derived to the digit (cell 6: 5.6/4.8/11.4; ladder: 9.26/5.60/5.80/5.59), and the gated LaLonde branch runs cleanly against the live URL producing exactly the promised naive -$635 vs adjusted +$1,548 (n=614, 185 treated) — column names in cell 16 match the fetched CSV.
- Strong pedagogical architecture: the same simulator run in randomized vs observational mode, a ladder whose rungs each name their leaning assumption, and a real-data replay of the identical confounding story (LaLonde) is exactly the right foundations arc, with accurate cross-links to notebooks 01, 05, 07, and 11.

<details><summary>Axis notes</summary>

- **Diagnostics (2/5).** The ladder's signature diagnostics are absent: no propensity-overlap histogram or covariate-balance (SMD) check before/after weighting despite defining positivity and running IPW, and the [0.05, 0.95] clip is un-narrated; the only diagnostic artifact is one bootstrap error bar.
- **Business (2/5).** No step-6 euro decision at all — COST=8.0 is defined and never used, even though the DGP hands over a one-line punchline (true ATE €5.6 < €8 cost, naive €11.4 > €8: confounding flips a go/no-go); the README's decision column exempts 00, so this is a designed-in but real thinness.
- **Narration (5/5).** Every term defined on first use, correct worked math (consistency equation, g-formula, LATE aside), assumption list with the untestable one flagged, and the identification-vs-estimation discipline callout — the strongest axis, genuinely lecture-ready prose.
- **Validation (2/5).** Recover-the-truth exists but is single-seed, and the one interval shown (AIPW 90% = [5.29, 5.89], reproduced) excludes the known truth 6.0 unacknowledged; no multi-seed stability, no coverage statement, no uncertainty anywhere else.
- **Watertight (3/5).** Formulas, estimand, and assumptions are stated precisely and all narrated numbers match outputs (verified by exact reproduction), but a bootstrap CI is mislabeled a 'credible interval', the headline validation interval excludes the truth it claims to recover, and cell 6 conflates estimator unbiasedness with the accuracy of a single visibly-off estimate.

</details>

- **🔴 CRITICAL · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cells 12-13 (estimator ladder) and the figure on PDF page 4`
  - **Issue.** The headline validation figure is titled 'The estimator ladder converges on the truth (naive doesn't)', but the only uncertainty interval displayed — the AIPW 90% bootstrap CI — excludes the known truth: reproduced exactly as [5.291, 5.889] against true ATE 6.0. The regression rung (5.60) is likewise 2.06 SE below truth (OLS SE 0.194), so all three adjusted rungs sit ~2 SE low on this single seed (17), and the notebook never comments.
  - **Evidence.** Re-ran cell 13's code verbatim against src/cmp (dgp.dag_control_demo(n=3000, seed=17), est.aipw_ate(..., seed=1, n_boot=300)): naive 9.26, reg 5.60, IPW 5.80, AIPW 5.59 — identical to committed output — with aipw['ci90'] = (5.291, 5.889), influence SE 0.183; 6.0 is outside. PDF p.4 shows the error-bar cap just below the dashed truth line.
  - **Why it matters.** This is the notebook's central recover-the-truth step. A sharp audience member who looks at the figure will see the error bar fail to touch the dashed truth line directly under a title asserting convergence — a broken headline claim in the flagship foundations figure, and exactly the kind of thing the watertight bar forbids.
  - **Fix.** Make the validation multi-seed: rerun the ladder over ~20 seeds and plot the distribution of each rung's estimate around the truth (plus empirical 90%-interval coverage). At minimum, print the ci90 numerically and add one sentence: a 90% interval misses the truth ~1 seed in 10, and this seed is one of them — which itself teaches what an interval means.
  - **Verifier.** Reproduced the finding exactly. (a) Factual: cell 13 of 00_foundations builds the ladder on dgp.dag_control_demo(n=3000, seed=17) and draws the only uncertainty interval from est.aipw_ate(..., seed=1, n_boot=300)['ci90'] under the title 'The estimator ladder converges on the truth (naive doesn't)'. Re-running the code verbatim against src/cmp gives naive 9.2604, reg 5.6025 (OLS SE 0.1944), IPW 5.8011, AIPW 5.5901 — identical to the committed output — with ci90 = (5.2911, 5.8885) and influence SE 0.1834; true ATE 6.0 lies outside the interval, and the regression rung is 2.04 SE below truth (reviewer said 2.06; trivial rounding difference). PDF page 4 visually confirms the error-bar cap ending…

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 12, rung 4 ('AIPW (doubly-robust) — combine both; consistent if either model is right, with a credible interval')`
  - **Issue.** The AIPW interval is called a 'credible interval', but est.aipw_ate (src/cmp/estimators.py:145-183) computes a frequentist bootstrap percentile CI over GBM+logistic refits — there is no prior or posterior anywhere; even the docstring hedges with 'bootstrap posterior-like distribution'.
  - **Evidence.** estimators.py aipw_ate: ci90 = np.quantile(boot, [0.05, 0.95]) over sklearn LogisticRegression + GradientBoostingRegressor bootstrap refits — no Bayesian machinery.
  - **Why it matters.** A Bayesian cookbook that later trades heavily on genuine posteriors and credible intervals cannot afford to blur the one term that distinguishes it; a statistically literate attendee would catch this immediately, and it undercuts the notebook's own identification-vs-estimation discipline message.
  - **Fix.** Change the wording to '90% bootstrap confidence interval' in cell 12 (and 'bootstrap distribution' in the aipw_ate docstring), with a half-sentence noting the Bayesian versions arrive in notebook 01.
  - **Verifier.** Factually accurate: nb 00 cell 12 (nb_text extract line 175) literally says AIPW comes "with a credible interval", and src/cmp/estimators.py:145-183 aipw_ate is a purely frequentist procedure — sklearn LogisticRegression propensity + GradientBoostingRegressor outcome models refit on nonparametric bootstrap resamples, with ci90 = np.quantile(boot, [0.05, 0.95]) (line 183). No prior, posterior, or PyMC machinery exists in the function; the docstring itself hedges with "bootstrap posterior-like distribution" (line 146). Cell 13 plots aipw["ci90"] as the interval in question and nothing later in the notebook corrects the term. Statistically sound: a bootstrap percentile interval is a confidence …
  - **Corrected statement.** Notebook 00 cell 12, rung 4 should read: "AIPW (doubly-robust) — combine both; consistent if either model is right, with a 90% bootstrap confidence interval (the fully Bayesian credible intervals arrive in notebook 01)." Correspondingly, the aipw_ate docstring in src/cmp/estimators.py:146 should say "bootstrap distribution" rather than "bootstrap posterior-like distribution".

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 6 (randomized vs observational bars) and PDF page 2`
  - **Issue.** Neither bar carries any uncertainty, and the print labels the randomized estimate '€4.8 (unbiased)' while the bar sits visibly below the dashed €5.6 truth line — conflating unbiasedness of the estimator with the accuracy of one draw. The text 'randomization annihilates confounding' never distinguishes bias from sampling noise.
  - **Evidence.** Reproduced: true ATE 5.58, randomized naive 4.83 (a ~1.3-SE deviation given y's sd ≈ 15.5 and n=3000), observational naive 11.45. PDF p.2 figure: green bar clearly below the dashed line, no error bars.
  - **Why it matters.** The first quantitative demo of the whole cookbook shows its 'unbiased' estimate missing the truth by 13% with no explanation; a sharp MBA can reasonably ask 'then why is your A/B answer wrong too?' and the notebook has no answer on the page.
  - **Fix.** Add analytic or bootstrap error bars to both bars and one sentence: the randomized estimate is within ~1 SE of the truth (pure sampling noise, shrinks with n), while the observational one is many SE away (bias, does not shrink with n) — that contrast IS the lesson.

### Notebook 01 — Uplift targeting (Anchor A ⭐)

**Grade: adequate** · 3 critical · 5 major · 13 findings total

| Diagnostics | Business | Narration | Validation | Watertight |
|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|
| 3 | 4 | 4 | 3 | 2 |

Anchor A has flagship-grade scaffolding: a compelling business question, a clean identification/estimation split, a full diagnostic battery (overlap, Qini/AUUC, uplift-by-decile, coverage-by-decile, reliability, sharpness, AIPW cross-check, multi-seed), and the best euro-decision layer in the repo (policy comparison, profit curve, cost/confidence sweeps, a correctly implemented EVPI, and a crisp 'A/B test the straddlers' recommendation). But the committed run is not statistically watertight: (1) the Depth A read-out flatly contradicts its own bake-off table (it claims BCF has the closest recovery, best ranking and 'near-nominal coverage' while the table shows the T-learner beating BCF on every metric and BCF at 76% coverage; it claims 'all three roughly unbiased' in the randomized world while the S-learner shows −3.20 ATE bias); (2) the headline E-value of 5.76 comes from an inverted crude formula in cmp.metrics (robustness DECREASES with distance from the threshold: an €8.01 effect vs €8 cost yields E≈1600, a €100 effect yields E≈1.39), is computed on the TRUE planted ATE instead of the estimate, and narrates 'explain the effect down to break-even' when the effect (€6.07) is already below break-even (€8); (3) the calibration diagnostic catches exactly the failure it was designed to catch — 76% overall coverage and ~5% coverage in the top true-effect decile — and the text never acknowledges it while building the 'honest rule' P(τ>cost) on those same intervals. Add a pseudo-PPC that cannot fail by construction, a headline policy table whose frac_contacted column is destroyed by round(0) (random-50% prints 1.0, the model rules print 0.0), a hard-coded sensitivity contour, and repeated unaddressed 'Only 80/90 samples per chain' warnings, and the notebook needs one focused statistical pass before it is lecture-safe. The fixes are localized: none touch the architecture.

**Strengths.**
- The euro-decision layer is genuinely flagship: five policies compared on realised profit against an oracle bound (88% capture), a profit curve with an optimal stopping point, cost and confidence sweeps, and a correctly implemented per-customer value-of-perfect-information (E[max(tau-c,0)] - max(E[tau]-c,0), src/cmp/policy.py:64-88) that converts residual uncertainty into a concrete, defensible next action: a small randomized test on the 612 straddlers rather than a blanket send.
- Conceptual narration is superb and MBA-calibrated: potential outcomes, the four customer types, the identification-vs-estimation distinction, an estimand ladder (ATE/CATE/policy value) with correct formulas, assumption-by-assumption unconfoundedness/positivity/SUTVA with a DAG, and every term (PEHE, AUUC, propensity, sharpness, credible interval) defined on first use with correct Bayesian interval language.
- The validation-first architecture is real, not decorative: seeded DGP with planted heterogeneous tau, recovery scatter, coverage-by-decile, reliability, sharpness, 4-seed stability, an AIPW doubly-robust cross-check whose 90% CI [5.19, 6.99] covers the truth (6.07), and the pymc-bart sample_vars=["mu"] counterfactual gotcha verifiably encapsulated (src/cmp/estimators.py:59-73) and unit-tested (tests/test_package.py::test_bart_cate_is_nonzero) exactly as README claims.

<details><summary>Axis notes</summary>

- **Diagnostics (3/5).** Impressive breadth (overlap, Qini/AUUC, deciles, reliability, AIPW, multi-seed) but the PPC is a hand-rolled Gaussian that cannot fail, no r-hat/ESS is ever reported (cmp fits set compute_convergence_checks=False) despite visible short-chain warnings, and the one damning diagnostic result (top-decile coverage ~5%) goes unread.
- **Business (4/5).** The richest axis — policies vs oracle, profit curve with stopping point, cost/confidence sweeps, EVPI test-sizing, crisp final recommendation — docked one point because the headline table prints wrong frac_contacted values (round(0)) and the promised treat-none baseline is missing.
- **Narration (4/5).** Near-flagship: estimand ladder, identification/estimation split, DAG, four-types table, every term defined; loses a point for the code silently redefining 'persuadable' as tau>cost and an E-value explanation that is directionally incoherent for an effect already below break-even.
- **Validation (3/5).** All the right machinery genuinely computed against a planted truth (PEHE, coverage-by-decile, reliability, sharpness, 4-seed stability), but the verdict layer fails: the 76%/top-decile coverage miss is never acknowledged, the 2-D sensitivity contour is a hard-coded formula rather than a computed range, and the E-value is broken.
- **Watertight (2/5).** Three critical defects in the committed outputs — a read-out contradicted by its own table, an inverted and misapplied E-value feeding the final decision paragraph, and an ignored calibration failure underpinning the 'honest' targeting rule — plus a pseudo-PPC described falsely as drawing from the fitted model.

</details>

- **🔴 CRITICAL · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 26 (Depth A read-out) vs cell 24 output table; PDF pp. 10-11`
  - **Issue.** The read-out claims 'BCF gets the closest per-customer recovery, the best ranking, and near-nominal coverage' and 'in the randomized world all three are roughly unbiased on the ATE' — both flatly contradicted by the bake-off table printed directly above it.
  - **Evidence.** Committed table: observational T-learner PEHE 5.85 < BCF 6.34, corr 0.84 > 0.83, AUUC 0.90 = 0.90, cov90 0.93 vs BCF 0.76 (76% is not near-nominal for a 90% interval; 93% is). Randomized S-learner ATE_bias = -3.20 on a true ATE of ~6.07 — a >50% bias, not 'roughly unbiased' (T: 0.13, BCF: -0.11).
  - **Why it matters.** This is the notebook's own evidence contradicting its own conclusion on the same page — the single most embarrassing thing a sharp audience member can catch in a lecture — and it undermines the README's 'BCF is the default for observational uplift' claim as demonstrated.
  - **Fix.** Rewrite the read-out to match the table: T-learner and BCF are comparable here (as the Step 7 caveat correctly predicts, since all confounders are observed), BCF's coverage is below nominal in this FAST run, and the S-learner's randomized-world negative bias IS the flattening story — use it. Better: generate the read-out programmatically from `bake` so narrative and numbers can never diverge.
  - **Verifier.** Factually accurate: the committed cell-24 bake-off table (verified in scratchpad extract nb_text/01_uplift_targeting.md and in reports/01_uplift_targeting.pdf pp. 10-11 via pdftotext) shows exactly the numbers the reviewer cites — observational T-learner PEHE 5.85 < BCF 6.34, corr 0.84 > 0.83, AUUC tied 0.90/0.90, cov90 0.93 (T) vs 0.76 (BCF); randomized S-learner ATE_bias -3.20 on a true ATE of ~6.1. Cell 26's read-out verbatim claims BCF has 'the closest per-customer recovery, the best ranking, and near-nominal coverage' and that 'in the randomized world all three are roughly unbiased on the ATE'. Statistically sound: closest per-customer recovery means lowest PEHE (T-learner wins); best r…
  - **Corrected statement.** Cell 26's read-out should state: in the randomized world the T-learner and BCF are roughly unbiased on the ATE (bias 0.13 and -0.11) while the S-learner is badly biased (-3.20 on a true ATE of ~6.1) — flattening appears even without confounding. In the observational world the naive average is badly biased; the S-learner misses heterogeneity and is mis-calibrated; the T-learner and BCF are comparable here (T-learner PEHE 5.85 vs BCF 6.34, AUUC tied at 0.90), as expected since all confounders are observed, and in this FAST run BCF's 90% intervals under-cover (76%) while the T-learner's are near-nominal (93%); BCF's advantages are its smaller observational ATE bias (0.49 vs 1.00), agreement with the independent AIPW estimator, and built-in regularized confounding control. Ideally the read-out should be generated programmatically from the `bake` DataFrame so narrative and numbers cannot diverge.

- **🔴 CRITICAL · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 28 (`metrics.e_value(tau.mean(), COST)`) and src/cmp/metrics.py:113-130; PDF p. 11`
  - **Issue.** The headline E-value of 5.76 is statistically unfounded three ways: the crude no-sd branch rr = |estimate|/|estimate-cost| is monotonically INVERTED (robustness explodes as the estimate approaches the decision threshold and shrinks as it moves away); it is computed on the TRUE planted ATE (tau.mean()=6.07), unknowable on real data, instead of the estimate; and the narration 'explain the effect down to break-even' is impossible since 6.07 is already below the €8 break-even.
  - **Evidence.** Reproduced from the implementation: e_value(6.0732, 8) = 5.756 (matches output); e_value(8.01, 8) = 1601.5; e_value(9, 8) = 17.5; e_value(100, 8) = 1.39. A borderline effect gets near-infinite 'robustness' while an overwhelming effect reads as fragile — exactly backwards versus VanderWeele-Ding, where the E-value grows with distance from the null/threshold.
  - **Why it matters.** The one-paragraph decision explicitly leans on it ('would only reverse under fairly strong hidden confounding — Depth B's E-value'), so the robustness headline handed to the CMO is a meaningless number from an inverted formula; any statistician who checks the arithmetic will demolish it, and README advertises 'E-value sensitivity' as a depth pillar.
  - **Fix.** Use the sd branch the function already supports — e_value(estimated_ATE, cost, sd=outcome/residual sd) implements VanderWeele's exp(0.91·d) conversion for continuous outcomes — feed it the BCF or AIPW estimate (and report the CI-limit E-value too, per VanderWeele), and delete or fix the crude ratio branch in metrics.py so no other notebook inherits it.
  - **Verifier.** All three legs of the finding check out against the artifacts. (1) Factual: metrics.py:128 implements the no-sd branch as rr=|estimate|/max(|estimate-cost|,1e-6); notebook cell 28 (nb_text line 946) calls metrics.e_value(tau.mean(), COST) with COST=8.0 (line 83) and tau.mean()=6.07, the PLANTED truth (cell 3 comment: "known only in sim"), and the output 5.756405 matches the reviewer's reproduction e_value(6.0732,8)=5.756 exactly. (2) Statistical: I re-derived the reviewer's spot checks by hand — e_value(8.01,8)≈1601.5, e_value(9,8)≈17.5, e_value(100,8)≈1.39 — confirming the formula is monotonically inverted: robustness explodes as the estimate approaches the €8 threshold and collapses for ov…
  - **Corrected statement.** N/A — the finding is accurate as stated. The E-value in notebook 01 cell 28 is computed from an inverted crude ratio (rr=|estimate|/|estimate−cost|), on the planted true ATE (6.07) rather than an estimate, with narration ("explain down to break-even") that is impossible given 6.07 < 8.

- **🔴 CRITICAL · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 15 output ('90% coverage 76%') and the coverage-by-decile figure (PDF p. 7); decision JSON coverage90=0.764 (cell 32)`
  - **Issue.** The calibration diagnostic catches a real failure — overall coverage 76% vs the 90% nominal, with the TOP true-effect decile at roughly 5% coverage — and the notebook never says a word about it; Step 5's 'is the uncertainty honest?' framing is implicitly answered yes, and Step 6's 'honest rule' P(tau>cost)>0.8 is built on those same intervals.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 14 markdown says the by-decile breakout exists 'to catch a model that's well-calibrated on average but overconfident for the biggest effects' — the figure then shows precisely that (last bar near zero; reliability curve's top bin: true ~€27 vs predicted ~€17), and no interpretation cell acknowledges it. The FAST disclaimer in cell 31 cannot excuse it: under-sampled posteriors give WIDER interval quantiles, which raises coverage.
  - **Why it matters.** Undercoverage from BART shrinkage on the largest effects means P(tau>cost) is understated exactly for the true persuadables — the population the whole business case targets — so the notebook's central validation claim (honest uncertainty) is contradicted by its own committed output.
  - **Fix.** Add an interpretation cell that reads the diagnostic honestly: name the top-decile shrinkage/undercoverage, connect it to the reliability curve's top-bin under-prediction, state the decision consequence (the confidence rule under-targets true persuadables; profit reaches 88% of oracle partly despite this), and show the FULL-mode coverage; if full mode still undercovers, discuss BCF prior tightness as the cause rather than implying honesty.
  - **Verifier.** Factual accuracy — every cited artifact says what the reviewer claims:

1. Cell 15 committed output (extract line 400): "PEHE €6.34 · corr(est,true) 0.83 · 90% coverage 76% · interval sharpness €13.6". Cell 32 JSON: "coverage90": 0.7644 (line 1048). The metric itself (src/cmp/metrics.py, interval_coverage, lines 23-42) is a standard equal-tailed credible-interval coverage — the 76% is genuine, not a metric bug.

2. Cell 14 markdown (lines 366-368) states the by-decile breakout exists "to catch a model that's well-calibrated on average but overconfident for the biggest effects." PDF p.7 then shows exactly that: the top true-effect decile's coverage bar is near zero (~0.05) against the 0.9 nom…
  - **Corrected statement.** The finding stands as written, and understates one aspect: beyond the missing interpretation, cell 26 explicitly asserts BCF achieves "near-nominal coverage," which is contradicted by its own committed table (cell 24: observational BCF cov90 = 0.76 vs T-learner 0.93). The only refinement: FAST mode's m=30-tree setting (reduced model capacity) could plausibly contribute to top-decile shrinkage, so the fix should verify FULL-mode coverage before attributing the undercoverage solely to BCF prior tightness — as the reviewer's suggested fix already anticipates.

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cells 12-13 (PPC); PDF p. 6; README 'posterior predictive checks (00, 01)'`
  - **Issue.** The 'posterior predictive check' does not use the model's posterior predictive: replicates are drawn from a hand-built Gaussian around cond_mean = (ȳ − τ̄·T̄) + τ̂·T — a constant baseline for every customer, ignoring the fitted prognostic surface — with resid_sd estimated from those very residuals, so the envelope matches the data's location and spread by construction and the check cannot fail.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 13: `y_rep = cond_mean[None,:] + rng.normal(0, resid_sd, size=(40,N))` with `resid_sd = std(y - cond_mean)`; the markdown claims 'we draw fake (replicated) datasets from the fitted model', which is false — the fitted BCF (prog + tau·z, sd) supports a genuine pm.sample_posterior_predictive. The pass verdict ('no gross misfit') is a hard-coded print.
  - **Why it matters.** In a notebook whose bar is watertight statistics, presenting a circular simulation as 'model criticism — the PPC' is a false description of what was computed; the code is on the slide, and anyone reading rng.normal will see the check is vacuous — it also forfeits the one diagnostic that could reveal baseline-surface misfit.
  - **Fix.** Run a real PPC from the fitted BCF model (sample_posterior_predictive on y_obs; overlay replicate densities plus a couple of test statistics such as sd and skew of y by arm), or at minimum build replicates from the model's fitted per-customer mu and posterior sd draws — and rewrite the markdown to describe exactly what is drawn.
  - **Verifier.** Factually accurate: Cell 13 of 01_uplift_targeting builds replicates as y_rep = cond_mean + N(0, resid_sd) with cond_mean = (ȳ − τ̄·T̄) + τ̂(x)·T — a scalar baseline for every customer — and resid_sd = std(y − cond_mean) estimated from the same residuals; the fitted prognostic surface is never used and cannot be, since bcf() in src/cmp/estimators.py line 136 returns only idata.posterior["tau"], discarding model/prog/mu/sd. Cell 12's markdown claim "we draw fake (replicated) datasets from the fitted model" is therefore false, the "no gross misfit" verdict is an unconditional print, and README line 57 advertises this as a "posterior predictive check". Statistically sound: a true PPC integrates…

- **🟠 MAJOR · business** — `Cell 19 output table (`print(comp.round(0))`); PDF p. 8; markdown cell 18`
  - **Issue.** The headline policy table is mangled by round(0): frac_contacted prints 1.0 for random-50% (true ~0.5) and 0.0 for model (mean>cost), model (P>conf) and oracle (true ~0.26), directly contradicting the next line's 'targeting 236 of 900 customers'; the markdown also promises 'five rules' then bullet-lists six including 'treat-none (baseline)', which never appears in the table.

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 28 (contour: `approx = tau.mean() + G * Dd * 0.9`; `adjusted_ate` via lstsq); PDF p. 12`
  - **Issue.** The 2-D sensitivity contour is not a computed analysis: it is a hard-coded linear surface (true ATE + 0.9·g·d with an arbitrary 0.9) presented under the title 'Where the decision flips (black = cost line)'; the tipping-point sweep also quietly swaps the estimator to a linear OLS adjustment (y ~ 1 + T + X) while the narrative says 'refit', and the strength axis (tip ≈ 1.5) is a DGP-internal unit never benchmarked against anything a manager could judge.
  - **Evidence.** The contour comes from a meshgrid formula with no refit and no derivation; the drift curve uses np.linalg.lstsq, not the BCF pipeline the headline numbers come from; nothing indicates whether 'strength 1.5' is large or small (e.g., relative to the strongest observed covariate, the standard benchmarking move in omitted-variable sensitivity analysis).
  - **Why it matters.** The four-axes bar explicitly demands sensitivity RANGES/contours as computed analyses; a contour that is literally truth + 0.9·g·d is decoration wearing the costume of rigor, and the un-benchmarked tipping point gives the CMO a number with no plausibility scale.
  - **Fix.** Either compute the contour (grid over (g, d), simulate/refit at each point — the drift loop already does this along one diagonal) or label it explicitly as a first-order bias schematic; benchmark the tipping strength against observed covariates ('a hidden confounder as strong as engage itself would move the estimate by €X'), and run the sweep with the same estimator family as the headline.
  - **Verifier.** All three claims verified against Cell 28 of the notebook extract, PDF p. 12, and src/cmp. (1) The contour is literally `approx = tau.mean() + G * Dd * 0.9` over a meshgrid — no refit, no derivation, anchored on the TRUE simulated ATE — yet is presented under the decision title 'Where the decision flips (black = cost line)' with an 'apparent ATE (€)' colorbar and no schematic caveat anywhere in the markdown. The 0.9 does echo the DGP's internal U→propensity coefficient (dgp.py:60, `_sigmoid(lin + 0.9*confounder_strength*U)`), so it is not fully arbitrary, but this is undocumented and the linear form is wrong anyway: for logistic-selection binary treatment the bias d·(E[U|T=1]−E[U|T=0]) satur…
  - **Corrected statement.** The finding stands essentially as written, with one refinement: the 0.9 multiplier is not arbitrary in origin — it silently mirrors the DGP's hard-coded U→treatment coefficient in dgp.py:60 — but this is undocumented in the notebook and the linear bias form remains underived and inconsistent with the notebook's own computed drift curve (linear in s) versus the surface (quadratic along the DGP diagonal). Additionally, the section is not entirely without a plausibility scale: the E-value (5.76) is reported and well narrated; it is specifically the tipping-point strength (1.5) that lacks any benchmark against observed covariates.

- **🟠 MAJOR · consistency** — `Cells 17 and 24 committed stderr; src/cmp/estimators.py:54,134 (compute_convergence_checks=False); cell 1 (FAST=True)`
  - **Issue.** The committed (and PDF) run is FAST-mode with repeated unaddressed sampler warnings — 'Only 80/90 samples per chain. Reliable r-hat and ESS diagnostics require longer chains' appears eight-plus times — and no r-hat/ESS is reported anywhere in an explicitly Bayesian flagship; convergence checks are globally disabled in cmp.
  - **Evidence.** Cells 17/24 stderr in committed outputs; BCF posteriors of 160-280 total draws feed the Depth A cov90 comparisons (0.93 vs 0.76) and the headline sharpness/coverage numbers; the only mitigation is a one-line FAST disclaimer about straddler width in cell 31, which addresses neither convergence nor the coverage noise.
  - **Why it matters.** Committed under-sampling with visible, unaddressed convergence warnings undermines lecture-grade figures, and quantile-based interval metrics from 160-draw posteriors make the bake-off's coverage column partly noise — which the read-out then over-interprets.
  - **Fix.** Regenerate the committed notebook and PDF with the FULL profile (the switch already exists), add one diagnostic cell after the main BCF fit reporting max r-hat and min bulk-ESS (az.summary) with a pass/fail sentence, and add a visible markdown note wherever FAST warnings remain explaining why they are tolerable in CI.

- **🟠 MAJOR · pedagogical** — `Cells 3 and 23-24 (bake-off design: regime='observational', confounder_strength=0.0); README 'BCF is the default for the observational uplift work'`
  - **Issue.** The bake-off never constructs a scenario where BCF's distinguishing features (propensity input, targeted-selection/RIC absorption) actually win: the observational DGP has all confounders observed — exactly the regime where the notebook's own Step 7 caveat says 'BCF ≈ T-learner', which the table confirms — yet BCF is introduced as 'best under confounding' and used as the primary model throughout.
  - **Evidence.** dgp.uplift_customers (src/cmp/dgp.py:56-64) generates selection only on observed features; the bake-off table shows T-learner ≥ BCF on every observational metric; there is no strong-targeted-selection or near-overlap-violation world where the propensity trick demonstrably earns its keep.
  - **Why it matters.** The flagship's central modeling choice is asserted rather than demonstrated — a sharp student can ask 'your own table says the simpler T-learner is at least as good; why is BCF the default?' and the notebook has no exhibit to answer with.
  - **Fix.** Add one bake-off world with aggressive targeted selection (e.g., selection on the prognostic score mu0 with propensities pushed toward the 0.05/0.95 tails) where the T-learner degrades and BCF visibly stabilizes recovery — the Hahn et al. RIC story the text already narrates — or soften the framing to 'BCF is a robust default; here it ties the T-learner because confounders are fully observed.'

- **🟡 MINOR · pedagogical** — `Cell 3 (`types = np.where(tau > COST, 'persuadable', ...)`) vs the four-types table in cell 0`
  - **Issue.** The code silently redefines 'persuadable' as tau > cost (€8) while the table defines it as tau > 0 (the email tips them over), so the printed 32/29/39 shares are 'profitably persuadable' shares and customers with 0 < tau ≤ 8 are lumped into 'sure thing / lost cause'; the taxonomy is also narrated in binary buy/no-buy terms while the outcome is continuous spend.
  - **Why it matters.** The four-types table is the teaching centerpiece; a student reconciling it with the printed shares gets different numbers and concludes one of them is wrong.
  - **Fix.** Classify with tau > 0 for persuadable (optionally add a 'profitably persuadable: tau > cost' line, the decision-relevant cut), and add one sentence mapping the binary buy story to the continuous-spend simulator.

- **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `Cells 11, 13, 17 print statements`
  - **Issue.** Verdict sentences are hard-coded prints, not computed checks: 'Two independent estimators landing on the same ATE' (BCF 6.57 vs AIPW 5.85 — a €0.72 gap with no agreement criterion), 'sits inside the replicate envelope — no gross misfit', and 'consistent, not a lucky seed' would all print unchanged even if the numbers disagreed on a re-run.
  - **Why it matters.** The notebook doubles as a durable toolkit meant to be re-run with other seeds/data; hard-coded conclusions are exactly how a future run ships a false claim, and the agreement claim is already loose ('the same' is unearned for a 12% gap).
  - **Fix.** Condition the sentences on the numbers — e.g., report whether the BCF ATE falls inside the AIPW 90% CI (it does: 6.57 ∈ [5.19, 6.99]) and phrase agreement as CI-compatibility; compute a simple envelope-coverage statistic for the PPC verdict.

- **🟡 MINOR · code** — `Cell 5, panel 3 (`ax[2].plot(np.linspace(engage.min(), engage.max(), 10), rate.values, ...)`)`
  - **Issue.** The decile-mean P(emailed) curve is plotted at 10 evenly spaced x positions, but engage ~ Beta(2,3) so qcut decile centers are not evenly spaced — the orange confounding curve is horizontally distorted relative to the scatter beneath it.
  - **Why it matters.** This is the figure that 'makes the confounding visible' for the audience; the distortion shifts where the emailing gradient appears to steepen.
  - **Fix.** Plot the rate against actual decile midpoints, e.g., group by the same qcut and use each bin's mean engage as x.

- **🟡 MINOR · consistency** — `Cell 21 (gated Hillstrom cell)`
  - **Issue.** The real-data pipeline fits BCF on the FIRST 4000 rows of the CSV (`Xr[:4000]`) — not a random subsample, so any file ordering makes the targeted-share statement describe a non-representative slice — while naive_ate uses all rows; the targeting threshold also silently drops to P(effect>0) > 0.7 versus the 0.8 confidence bar used everywhere else.
  - **Why it matters.** It is the notebook's one 'production looks like this' moment; the mismatched subsample and threshold are the first things a practitioner would copy wrongly.
  - **Fix.** Take a seeded random subsample (rng.choice) for the BCF fit and reuse confidence=0.8 (or state why the bar differs when cost ≈ 0).

- **⚪ POLISH · code** — `src/cmp/estimators.py:13 and src/cmp/policy.py:91-104`
  - **Issue.** Doc drift in the shared package: estimators.py points the gotcha test at tests/test_estimators.py but it lives at tests/test_package.py::test_bart_cate_is_nonzero (README has it right); policy_comparison's docstring says 'four policies' and promises a 90% CI column but returns five policies and no CI; bcf()'s docstring asserts 'near-nominal CATE interval coverage under observational selection', which the committed run (0.76) does not support.
  - **Why it matters.** The package is the durable internal toolkit; stale docstrings in the code the notebooks lean on erode the 'encapsulated and tested' story.
  - **Fix.** Correct the test path, align the policy_comparison docstring with its actual output (or add the promised CI), and soften the bcf coverage claim to what the repo demonstrates.

### Notebook 02 — Segment effects

**Grade: good** · 1 critical · 5 major · 9 findings total

| Diagnostics | Business | Narration | Validation | Watertight |
|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|
| 2 | 4 | 4 | 3 | 3 |

Notebook 02 (segment effects via pathmc) has a genuinely strong core: the estimand is written in do-notation, a worked cancellation derivation shows exactly why heterogeneity lives in the interaction coefficients, and the empty-adjustment-set output is honestly explained as a consequence of randomization rather than a software discovery. Every headline number was independently verified against the code, the DGP (src/cmp/dgp.py:128-153) and pathmc 0.1.1 semantics: the segment CATEs (7.71 vs true 7.0; 15.79 vs true 16.0) are exact linear functionals of the posterior, the four-policy profit ladder (3,682 < 4,602 < 4,871 < 4,923) delivers the README's pooled < segment < individual < oracle claim, and the 1,189 / 32% uplift arithmetic is correct. However, it falls short of the excellence bar in specific, fixable ways: the planted truth is misstated twice as EUR 3/12 "at average engagement" when the outputs and the truth lines in the validation figure show EUR 7/16 (an on-slide self-contradiction); there are zero convergence diagnostics while the committed FAST output prints an unaddressed "run at least 4 chains" warning; the decide step announces the P(effect>cost) criterion and then builds the headline ladder from mean-beats-cost rules; and validation is single-seed with no interval coverage, no posterior predictive check, and no DAG falsification, despite pathmc shipping test_implications/residuals modules and cmp.metrics shipping pehe/coverage that go unused.

**Strengths.**
- The identification step is flagship-grade: estimand in do-notation, a worked derivation showing tau(x) = b1 + b3*v + b4*g so 'is the effect heterogeneous?' becomes 'is b3 (or b4) non-zero?', plus the honest framing that under randomization the structural model is a query engine for subgroup effects, not a confounding correction (cells 4-6). pathmc's adjustment_sets was verified to be a real backdoor-criterion computation, not a vacuous stub.
- Numbers are watertight where it counts: every printed quantity re-derives correctly (CATE-high 15.79 = 2.68 + 8.08 + 10.05*0.5 from the coefficient table; profit ladder sums check against n=1500 and the DGP; .hdi() confirmed to be a 94% HDI by pathmc default), and the README's pooled < segment < individual < oracle realised-profit ladder is delivered exactly (3,682 < 4,602 < 4,871 < 4,923).
- The three-panel validation figure (segment posteriors vs planted truth, continuous moderation profile with truth overlay and the EUR 8 cost line, per-customer 45-degree recovery with RMSE 0.74) is lecture-ready, and the 'how to read those three panels' cell (cell 11) interprets each panel correctly; cross-references to notebooks 01 (BART/uplift, P(effect>cost) criterion), 03 (random slopes) and 05 (confounders) were checked and are accurate.

<details><summary>Axis notes</summary>

- **Diagnostics (2/5).** Identification tooling and the interaction-posterior test are present, but there are no sampler diagnostics at all (no r-hat/ESS/divergences; the committed 2-chain FAST run even prints a 4-chain recommendation) and no model checking (no PPC, residuals, or DAG falsification), although pathmc ships falsify/test_implications and residuals modules — the signature diagnostics for a parametric SCM are absent.
- **Business (4/5).** Segment decision table with P(effect>cost) and SEND/TEST/SKIP actions plus the four-policy realised-profit ladder is strong and correctly computed, but the entire decision lives at a single COST=8 with no cost sweep, no value-of-information, and the break-even engagement threshold is pointed at in the figure yet never quantified with posterior uncertainty.
- **Narration (4/5).** Moderation, CATE, do-operator, interaction terms, and HDI are all defined on first use with worked math and honest identification framing — near flagship — but the planted-truth misstatement (EUR 3/12 vs 7/16), the 'straddles zero = noise' overclaim, and the slightly over-trusting 'pathmc confirms this' phrasing blemish it.
- **Validation (3/5).** Truth recovery is demonstrated at three levels (segment posteriors on the planted values, continuous profile vs the true line, per-customer RMSE 0.74) and genuinely succeeds, but it is single-seed (11), reports no interval coverage/calibration (cmp.metrics.coverage/pehe unused), never compares the interaction coefficients to their planted values (8.08 vs 9, 10.05 vs 8), and the fitted family equals the DGP so individual recovery is within-family only.
- **Watertight (3/5).** Formulas, estimand, do-notation, HDI definition and all computed numbers verified correct, but the narrative contradicts the outputs on the planted truth (EUR 3/12 vs printed 7.0/16.0), a sampler warning in committed output goes unaddressed with no convergence reporting anywhere, and the decide step's stated probability criterion contradicts the mean-rule code it runs.

</details>

- **🔴 CRITICAL · consistency — ✅ verified** — `Cell 2 (markdown, 'Simulate a ground truth') and Cell 8 (markdown, 'Validate', check 1); PDF pages 2-4`
  - **Issue.** The planted truth is misstated twice. In the lecture, a sharp attendee will ask why the model 'recovers' 7.71 and 15.79 against a claimed truth of 3 and 12, and the presenter has to untangle the engagement-slope bookkeeping live.   - **Verifier.** Both prongs hold. (a) Factually accurate: dgp.py's segment_customers sets tau = 3 + 9*is_high + 8*engagement and returns true_effect = {low: 3+8*0.5 = 7.0, high: 3+9+8*0.5 = 16.0}; engagement ~ Beta(2,2) has mean exactly 0.5. Cell 2 (nb_text line 57; PDF p.2) indeed says the email 'lifts low-value customers by €3 and high-value by €12 at average engagement, plus a smooth +€8 × engagement slope on top', and cell 8 check 1 (nb_text line 167; PDF p.3) says 'Segment CATEs vs the planted €3 / €12'. (b) Statistically sound: €3/€12 are the effects at ZERO engagement; at average engagement (0.5) they are €7/€16. Cell 2's wording is also internally incoherent (if €3/€12 held at average engagement, ad…
  - **Corrected statement.** Cell 2 should read: the email lifts low-value customers by €3 and high-value by €12 at ZERO engagement, plus a smooth +€8 × engagement slope — i.e. €7 (low) and €16 (high) for the average customer at engagement 0.5, matching dgp.segment_customers' true_effect = {low: 7.0, high: 16.0}. Cell 8 check 1 should read: 'Segment CATEs vs the planted €7 / €16 (segment averages at mean engagement)'.

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 11 (markdown, Step 6 intro) vs Cell 12 (policy ladder code)`
  - **Issue.** Step 6 opens by announcing 'the honest probability criterion from notebook 01 — target a segment only where P(effect > cost) is high (not merely where the mean beats cost)', but the headline policy ladder is built entirely from mean-beats-cost rules: segmented_mask = np.where(df.is_high==1, cate_high.mean() > COST, cate_low.mean() > COST) and individual_mask = tau_hat > COST, where tau_hat is a plug-in of posterior means (be.mean() + bev.mean()*v + beg.mean()*g from cell 10).

  - **Why it matters.** The notebook explicitly tells the audience the mean rule is not the honest criterion, then two lines later uses exactly that rule for its flagship result. (In this run the segment outcomes coincide — P=0.24 SKIP low / P=1.00 SEND high matches means 7.71<8<15.79 — but that is luck of the numbers, not coherence of the method.) Only the segment decision table uses P(d > COST) > 0.8. - **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cells 5-7 (identify + estimate); absence of any model-checking cell`
  - **Issue.** No model-checking diagnostic for the structural model: no posterior predictive check of spend, no residual diagnostics, and no testable-implications/falsification run — even though pathmc 0.1.1 ships falsify.py/test_implications and residuals.py, and its own adjustment_sets docstring warns it 'cannot detect omitted variables, missing edges, or other forms of misspecification. Additionally, since all predictors in this spec are exogenous roots, test_implications has limited power against functional-form misspecification, so the PPC variant of the suggested fix is the more informative diagnostic for this notebook.

- **🟠 MAJOR · business** — `Cells 11-12 (Decide step); middle panel of the cell-10 figure`
  - **Issue.** The decision is evaluated at a single COST=8 with no sensitivity: no cost sweep of the policy ladder, no value-of-information, and — the most natural output of this notebook's own moderation profile — no quantified break-even engagement. The text says 'Note where each line crosses the EUR 8 cost line — that's the engagement level above which a customer becomes worth emailing' but never computes it, even though g* = (COST - b_e - b_ev*v)/b_eg is a one-line posterior functional (true values: g* = 0.625 for low-value, all high-value customers clear cost).
  - **Evidence.** Cell 12 output: low-value net_of_cost = -0.29, P(effect>cost) = 0.24 -> SKIP; cell 11 markdown points at the cost-line crossing; no cell varies COST or computes the crossing.
  - **Why it matters.** The repo's business-axis bar explicitly lists multi-parameter sweeps and break-even tables. And with cate_low at 7.71 vs COST 8.0, the SKIP-low decision is knife-edge: a EUR 1 change in contact cost flips it, which a cost sweep would surface.
  - **Fix.** Add the posterior of the break-even engagement per segment (draws: (COST - be - bev*v)/beg) reported with a 94% HDI, and a compact COST-sweep (e.g. 5..12) of the four-policy ladder showing where segment rules and pooled decisions flip.

- **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `Cell 0 (markdown intro), 'The tool' section`
  - **Issue.** 'if it straddles zero, the "gap" is noise and we shouldn't act on it' — an interaction posterior straddling zero means the data cannot distinguish the gap from noise, not that the gap IS noise.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 0: 'if it straddles zero, the "gap" is noise and we shouldn't act on it.'
  - **Why it matters.** Absence of evidence vs evidence of absence is exactly the distinction a Bayesian cookbook should model for an MBA audience; as written it teaches them to read a wide interval as a proven null.
  - **Fix.** Rephrase: 'if it straddles zero, we can't tell the gap from noise — so we shouldn't build segment rules on it (and might instead run a bigger test)'.

- **🟡 MINOR · pedagogical** — `Cell 4 (markdown, Identification) and Cell 5 output`
  - **Issue.** 'pathmc reads the graph and confirms this' slightly oversells the software check: adjustment_sets/is_identifiable reason only over the DAG the user declared (which has no arrows into email because none were written); pathmc's own docstring says it cannot detect omitted variables or missing edges. The surrounding text does state randomization holds by design, but the word 'confirms' invites the audience to think the tool verified unconfoundedness from data.
  - **Evidence.** pathmc/identify.py:53-73: 'This function reasons about the DAG structure declared in the model specification. It cannot detect omitted variables, missing edges, or other forms of misspecification.'
  - **Why it matters.** MBA audiences are prone to 'the software checked causality' over-trust; one sentence prevents it and reinforces the notebook's otherwise excellent assumptions-vs-estimation separation.
  - **Fix.** Change to 'pathmc reads the graph we declared and confirms that, under that graph, no adjustment is needed — the software checks our drawing, it cannot verify randomization from data.'

- **⚪ POLISH · statistical** — `Cell 9 (P(>0) print) and Cell 10 (quantile bands)`
  - **Issue.** Two interval-housekeeping nits: (1) 'P(>0) = 1.000' is reported as exactly 1 from only 800 posterior draws — should be '> 0.999'; (2) the moderation-profile bands use np.quantile(d, .05/.95), i.e. 90% equal-tailed intervals, while every other interval in the notebook is a 94% HDI, and the band level is not stated in the figure or text.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 9: p_gap = (b_ev > 0).mean() printed as 1.000; cell 10: los.append(np.quantile(d,.05)); his.append(np.quantile(d,.95)).
  - **Why it matters.** Small, but the notebook elsewhere defines the 94% HDI carefully; a mismatched, unlabeled 90% band and a literal probability of 1 are the kind of details a statistically sharp attendee notices.
  - **Fix.** Print min(p_gap, 0.999) formatted as '> 0.999' when all draws are positive; either switch the bands to the 94% HDI or add '(90% band)' to the middle-panel label.

### Notebook 03 — Price elasticity

**Grade: good** · 0 critical · 5 major · 10 findings total

| Diagnostics | Business | Narration | Validation | Watertight |
|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|
| 2 | 3 | 4 | 3 | 3 |

Notebook 03 is conceptually strong and its headline claim is fully delivered: the endogenous-price demo genuinely shows elasticity biased toward zero (-0.59 vs true -1.42), the +0.83 bias matches the analytic simultaneity bias Cov(logP,shock)/Var(logP)=0.832 implied by dgp.price_panel, and the biased rerun uses the same hierarchical model, proving pooling cannot fix it. The shrinkage pedagogy (deliberately thinned regions, no-pool-to-partial-pool slope graph) is lecture-grade, and every printed number I checked is consistent with the cell outputs. It falls short of the four-axes bar in three places: (1) zero convergence evidence for a centered-parameterization hierarchical model, with compute_convergence_checks=False and warnings globally suppressed; (2) the calibration check fails (90% CIs cover 67%, p~2.6% under Bin(12,0.9)) and is waved off in one parenthetical with no multi-seed check; (3) the no-pool/complete-pool baselines omit the controls the hierarchical model gets, so the "partial pooling wins" MAE chart conflates pooling with covariate adjustment. The euro decision is honest (P(elastic) gating into set-price vs controlled-test) but thin versus the bar — no profit lift, policy comparison, or VOI — and the opt_price column is a conditional median that visibly contradicts the printed formula applied to the same row's elasticity (region_00: -1.07 implies EUR 122, table says EUR 43.4) with no explanation.

**Strengths.**
- The toward-zero endogeneity demonstration is exact and honest: the mechanism (managers cut price when demand is soft, so Cov(logP, shock)>0) is documented in dgp.py:174-177, the direction is correctly derived, the rerun uses the SAME partial-pooling model so 'pooling cannot fix it' is demonstrated rather than asserted, and the observed bias (+0.83) matches the analytic Cov/Var value (0.832) to two decimals — the README claim and the bridge to notebook 11 (IV) are fully delivered.
- Shrinkage pedagogy is flagship quality: regions 0-2 are deliberately thinned to 20% of their data so pooling has visible work to do, the shrinkage-factor formula is given up front, and the middle panel (no-pool to partial-pool lines, thin regions in orange yanked hardest) is one of the clearest partial-pooling visuals you could put in front of an MBA audience.
- The decision step is honest where it matters: instead of blindly emitting an 'optimal price' per region, it gates on P(β < -1) and routes low-confidence regions to a controlled price test, and the profit-maximising price formula P* = βc/(β+1) with its β < -1 validity condition is stated and implemented correctly.

- **Diagnostics (2/5).** The signature diagnostics for a hierarchical Bayesian model (r-hat, ESS, divergence count, PPC) are entirely absent; convergence checks are explicitly disabled and warnings suppressed, on a centered parameterisation that is the textbook funnel-geometry risk case.
- **Business (3/5).** Solid per-region action table with probability gating, but no expected profit lift in euros, no policy comparison (price on no-pool vs partial-pool vs oracle), no VOI for the controlled-test regions, and no cost/margin sweep — all explicitly part of the repo bar.
- **Narration (4/5).** Elasticity, endogeneity, log-log, and partial pooling are all defined on first use with worked math and a crisp bias-variance framing; missing DAG for the simultaneity story and a tau vs tau-squared notation flip keep it off 5.
- **Validation (3/5).** Recovery vs planted truth and a three-regime MAE bake-off are present, but the calibration check fails (67% vs nominal 90%) and is excused in one parenthetical, there is no multi-seed stability run, and tau_beta is printed but never compared to its planted value 0.35.
- **Watertight (3/5).** No wrong formula or mismatched number found (all printed outputs check out; the bias magnitude matches the analytic value), but suppressed convergence checks, an unfair no-pool baseline, a failed calibration waved off in one line, and an unexplained conditional opt_price each give a sharp audience member a hole to poke.

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 1 (warnings.filterwarnings('ignore')), Cell 6 and Cell 12 (pm.sample(..., compute_convergence_checks=False))`
  - **Issue.** No convergence evidence anywhere in the committed outputs: r-hat, ESS, and divergence counts are never reported, convergence checks are explicitly disabled in both pm.sample calls, and a blanket warnings filter would silence anything that slipped through. The model uses the CENTERED parameterisation beta_r ~ N(mu_beta, tau_beta), the classic funnel-geometry case where divergences are most likely, sampled with only 2 chains x 500 draws in the committed FAST run (cell 12 uses 300/300).
  - **Evidence.** Cell 1: warnings.filterwarnings('ignore'); Cell 6: idata = pm.sample(random_seed=SEED, progressbar=False, compute_convergence_checks=False, **FIT) with FAST FIT = draws=500, tune=500, chains=2; no az.summary, trace plot, or divergence count appears in any cell or in the PDF.

If the FAST run had divergences or low ESS on tau_beta, nobody would know — and every downstream euro number rides on that posterior.
  - **Fix.** Add an az.summary(idata, var_names=['mu_beta','tau_beta']) printout with r-hat/ESS plus the divergence count, one line interpreting them; switch beta_r to a non-centered parameterisation (or show it samples cleanly centered); scope the warnings filter instead of ignoring everything.

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 8 (cover = 67%) and Cell 9 how-to-read text; PDF p.3 figure title 'Partial pooling wins · 90% coverage 67%'`
  - **Issue.** The calibration check fails — nominal 90% credible intervals cover the truth in only 8/12 regions (67%) — and the only treatment is one parenthetical calling it 'a small-sample artefact' of FAST mode. Under Bin(12, 0.9) the probability of covering 8 or fewer is ~2.6%, so 'luck' is not a comfortable explanation; the more likely mechanism (tau_beta underestimated with only 12 groups, over-shrinking thin regions' intervals, compounded by 1000-draw quantiles) is neither diagnosed nor tested. There is no multi-seed recovery/coverage run, despite the repo bar explicitly requiring multi-seed stability and cmp.metrics.interval_coverage existing for exactly this.

  - **Why it matters.** The euro decision in step 6 is built directly on these intervals (P(elastic) gating). Presenting a validation step whose own headline number fails, with a hand-wavy one-line excuse in a title that says 'Partial pooling wins', is exactly the hole a sharp audience member will drive through: 'your 90% intervals cover 67% — why trust the P(elastic) column?'

  - **Verifier.** Factually accurate on every checkable point: Cell 8 prints "coverage 67%" (8/12) and the figure title "Partial pooling wins · 90% coverage 67%" appears in the code (extract line 211) and on PDF p.3; the Cell 9 parenthetical blaming "FAST mode with few regions ... a small-sample artefact" is verbatim and is the sole treatment of the failure; tau_beta posterior 0.31 (Cell 6 output) vs planted 0.35 (src/cmp/dgp.py:166, rng.normal(-1.4, 0.35, n_regions)) both check out; cmp.metrics.interval_coverage exists (src/cmp/metrics.py:23) yet is unused, and no multi-seed run exists despite the repo bar requiring multi-seed recovery stability. - **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 6 lines: nopool = np.polyfit(lp[r_idx==i], ld[r_idx==i], 1) and complete = np.polyfit(lp, ld, 1); headline chart in Cell 8 / PDF p.3`
  - **Issue.** The three-regime comparison is not apples-to-apples: no-pooling and complete-pooling are bivariate log-log fits WITHOUT the controls Z (competitor price, season, trend), while the partial-pooling model includes them. In the DGP, season (amplitude 0.3) and trend (up to 0.8) dwarf the log-price variation (sd ~0.05), so omitting them massively inflates the no-pool residual noise, and omitting competitor price adds a small OVB to the pooled fit. The MAE ranking 0.45 / 0.28 / 0.21 therefore conflates 'pooling helps' with 'covariate adjustment helps'.
  - **Evidence.** dgp.py:170-181: season = 0.3*sin(...), trend = 0.01*arange(80) (0 to 0.79), demand noise sd 0.08, log_price noise sd 0.05 — omitted season+trend roughly triple the residual sd for the polyfit baselines; the hierarchical model in cell 6 includes z @ gamma while both polyfit calls use only (lp, ld).
  - **Why it matters.** 'Partial pooling wins' is the notebook's central estimation claim and its headline figure. As built, part of partial pooling's margin comes from an advantage the baselines were denied; a sharp reviewer who reads the code can legitimately say the bake-off was rigged, undermining an otherwise true conclusion.
  - **Fix.** Give all three regimes the same controls: per-region OLS of ld on [lp, Z] and pooled OLS on [lp, Z] (np.linalg.lstsq, three lines). Partial pooling will still win on the thin regions, and the comparison becomes clean; alternatively state explicitly that the baselines omit controls and why.
  - **Verifier.** Both prongs hold.

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 10 (opt_price function and table); PDF p.4 table row region_00`
  - **Issue.** The opt_price column is the median of P* over only the draws with beta < -1.001 (a conditional-on-elastic posterior), while the elasticity column is the unconditional posterior mean — and this conditioning is never stated. The two columns visibly contradict the printed formula: region_00 shows elasticity -1.07, and P* = beta/(beta+1) x 8 at beta = -1.07 gives EUR 122, yet the table prints EUR 43.4. The extreme sensitivity of P* as beta approaches -1 (the posterior of P* has enormous right tails for the boundary regions) is also never mentioned.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 10: b = np.where(beta < -1.001, beta, np.nan); opt_price median computed over non-NaN draws; table output 'region_00 -1.07 0.63 EUR43.4 controlled test'. Check: -1.07/(-0.07)*8 = 122.3.
  - **Why it matters.** Anyone in the audience who plugs the row's own elasticity into the row's own formula gets a number 3x the printed one — it looks like a computational error even though it is a defensible truncated-median choice. For a notebook whose bar is 'narrative numbers consistent with cell outputs', an unexplained internal inconsistency in the decision table is a lecture-risk.
  - **Fix.** Add one sentence: 'opt_price is the median optimal price conditional on the region being elastic (beta < -1 draws only); near the boundary it is extremely uncertain — another reason those regions get a test, not a price.' Better: print a 90% interval for P* per region, which turns the boundary blow-up into a teaching moment, or blank the column for non-set-price rows.

(1) Cell 10 code (nb_text/03_price_elasticity.md lines 245-256) computes opt_price as the median of P* over only draws with beta < -1.001 (np.where -> NaN -> dropna -> median), while the elasticity column prints partial = beta_post.mean(0), the unconditional posterior mean. (2) The arithmetic contradiction is exact: P*(-1.07) = -1.07/(-0.07)*8 = 122.3 vs printed EUR 43.4 (PDF p.4 table row region_00, visually confirmed). Inverting 43.4 gives a conditional-median beta of about -1.226, precisely what truncating the 37% of non-elastic draws (P(elastic)=0.63) produces; safely-elastic rows (region_01: plug-in 19.1 vs printed 19.6) nearly agree…

  - **Issue.** The euro decision stops at an optimal price level + P(elastic) + action label. - **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `Cell 2 and Cell 4 ('Observed confounders Z = competitor price, seasonality, trend') vs dgp.py:170-181`
  - **Issue.** Z is described as 'observed confounders', but in the actual DGP only competitor price enters both the price and demand equations; season and trend enter demand only, so they are precision covariates, not confounders. Relatedly, the identify step — which is all about a backdoor set and a simultaneity loop — has no DAG, despite the repo bar listing DAGs under conceptual narration and this being the notebook where a 4-node graph (shock -> P, shock -> Q, competitor price -> both) would do the most work.
  - **Evidence.** dgp.py:178: log_price = log(15) - 0.05*competitor_price/20 + confounder_strength*demand_shock + noise — season and trend do not appear in the price equation.
  - **Why it matters.** Precision in the identification section is the point of step 3; calling non-confounders confounders is exactly the kind of loose language the notebook elsewhere avoids, and the missing DAG makes the endogeneity story purely verbal.
  - **Fix.** One-line fix in cells 2/4: 'competitor price is a true confounder (moves price and demand); season and trend only move demand — we include them for precision.' Add a small DAG figure in step 3 showing the backdoor path and the unobserved-shock loop that motivates IV.

- **🟡 MINOR · pedagogical** — `Cell 10 figure (P(elastic) bars) and Cell 12 figure (endogeneity bars); PDF pp.4-5`
  - **Issue.** The step-6 decision figure and the step-7 endogeneity figure have no 'how to read this' interpretation cells (only the step-5 three-panel figure has one, cell 9). In particular the blue/gold/orange bar colour code and the 0.9 dashed threshold in the P(elastic) chart are never explained in text or legend.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 10 code: color=[plots.BLUE if c>0.9 else (plots.GOLD if c>0.5 else plots.ORANGE) ...] with no legend; cell 11 jumps straight to '7 · Caveats'; after cell 12's figure, cell 13 is 'Other caveats'.
