- **🟡 MINOR · consistency** — `Cell 0 and Cell 5 (beta_r ~ N(mu_beta, tau_beta)) vs Cell 4 (beta_r ~ N(mu_beta, tau_beta^2)); shrinkage formula in Cell 4`
  - **Issue.** Notation flips between sections: cells 0 and 5 write the random-slope distribution with tau_beta as the second argument (sd convention, matching PyMC), while cell 4 writes tau_beta^2 (variance convention). Also the shrinkage factor 1 - tau^2/(tau^2 + sigma^2/n_r) is the random-INTERCEPT approximation; for a slope the effective sampling variance is sigma^2/(n_r Var(log P)). It is labelled 'approximately', but a purist could poke it.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 4: 'beta_r ~ N(mu_beta, tau_beta^2)' and '1 - tau_beta^2/(tau_beta^2 + sigma^2/n_r)'; cell 0/5: 'N(mu_beta, tau_beta)'.
  - **Why it matters.** Small notational drift in the one formula the audience is asked to internalise; a stats-literate attendee comparing sections will wonder which convention is meant.
  - **Fix.** Pick the sd convention everywhere (matching the PyMC code) and add '(per unit of log-price variance — exact form for a slope replaces n_r with n_r Var(log P))' after the shrinkage formula.

- **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `Cell 6 printout (tau_beta 0.31) vs dgp.py:166 (true between-region sd 0.35)`
  - **Issue.** tau_beta is promoted as the quantity that 'measures how much elasticity genuinely varies', and its posterior mean (0.31) is printed — but it is never compared to the planted truth (0.35), which the notebook text never states. mu_beta is likewise reported as a bare point (-1.36) with no credible interval.
  - **Evidence.** dgp.py:166: true_elasticity = rng.normal(-1.4, 0.35, n_regions); cell 6 output: 'between-region spread tau_beta 0.31' with no truth alongside.
  - **Why it matters.** The validate-the-truth step covers the beta_r but skips the two hyperparameters the narrative leans on; validating tau against 0.35 would also directly inform the coverage discussion (finding 2).
  - **Fix.** Print 'tau_beta 0.31 (true 0.35)' and give mu_beta with a 90% interval; one line noting tau is mildly underestimated with 12 groups ties directly into why coverage runs low.

- **⚪ POLISH · code** — `Cell 3 (thinned df used for the clean fit) vs Cell 12 (full df2 used for the endogenous fit)`
  - **Issue.** The clean-vs-endogenous fleet comparison is not perfectly matched: the clean run uses the panel with regions 0-2 thinned to 20%, the endogenous run uses the full 12x80 panel, so the two bars differ by more than just the endogeneity switch (negligibly, here).

### Notebook 04 — Funnel mediation

**Grade: adequate** · 2 critical · 4 major · 11 findings total

| Diagnostics | Business | Narration | Validation | Watertight |
|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|
| 2 | 2 | 4 | 3 | 2 |

Steps 1-5 are genuinely strong: the NDE/NIE estimand is stated correctly, the sequential-ignorability assumptions (including the treatment-induced-confounder condition) are stated honestly and kept separate from estimation, and the recover-the-truth validation is real and numerically clean (all three path/total estimates cover the planted truths from dgp.funnel). But Step 6 — the notebook's own headline — does not hold up to the watertight bar. The "invest in onboarding" leverage ranking compares euros-per-unit across variables on incommensurate scales (one unit of onboarding_score is its entire range, about 3.5 SD; one unit of engagement is about 1.2 SD); on a per-SD basis the ranking fully inverts (engagement ~ EUR 175 > activated ~ EUR 155 > onboarding ~ EUR 136), so the euro recommendation is an artifact of units, and no cost-to-move-a-unit model ever connects it to the "fixed budget to split" opening question. The signature sensitivity sweep is internally incoherent: the code contradicts its own comment on the bias direction, freezes onboarding's value even though onboarding's total effect flows through the same confounded edge with a ~2.15x larger loading, uses an uncalibrated rho, and by construction can never flip within the swept range — while pathmc ships a proper VanderWeele-Ding sensitivity() method the notebook ignores. Add an unaddressed r-hat warning in the committed sampling output, a direct effect that is assumed away rather than estimated, and a mischaracterization of pathmc path effects as "simulate-through-the-graph" when they are coefficient products, and the notebook lands at adequate: excellent mediation pedagogy up front, a decision step a sharp audience could take apart.

**Strengths.**
- Identification honesty is above the usual bar for mediation material: cell 4 states all three no-unmeasured-confounding conditions plus the no-treatment-induced-confounder condition, says explicitly that natural effects are NOT identified if it fails, singles out the M-Y link as the one most likely to break, and keeps identification cleanly separate from estimation — exactly what the artifact-specific review asked to verify.
- Truth recovery is genuine and numerically watertight: the printed truths match dgp.funnel exactly (2.2*1.6*0.9=3.17, 2.2*0.35=0.77, total 3.94), and the posterior recovers total 3.89 [3.74,4.04], via-activated 3.11 [2.95,3.28], via-engagement 0.78 [0.63,0.92] — every truth inside its 90% interval, with a clean estimated-vs-true bar chart.
- The conceptual narration is lecture-ready: correct Pearl NDE/NIE formulas with the TE = NDE + NIE decomposition, the product-of-coefficients bridge to classic a.b mediation, the cascade intuition for why total (not local) effects are the right lever metric, every figure with a how-to-read-this cell, and an accurate cross-link to notebook 05 on not controlling away the mechanism.

<details><summary>Axis notes</summary>

- **Diagnostics (2/5).** No PPC, no residuals, no r-hat/ESS table despite a visible r-hat warning in cell 6 output, and no DAG falsification even though pathmc provides falsify()/test_implications()/implied_independences(); only truth-recovery is shown.
- **Business (2/5).** One three-row lever table with trivially-1.0 P(>0) values; no cost-per-unit-lift, no budget allocation, no break-even or VOI, and the headline euro ranking is a variable-scaling artifact that inverts under standardization.
- **Narration (4/5).** Correct Pearl NDE/NIE formulas, honest assumption-by-assumption discussion, cascade intuition, and good how-to-read-this cells; docked for mischaracterizing what pathmc effect() computes and loosely naming the cross-world condition.
- **Validation (3/5).** Single-seed truth recovery is genuine and quantitative (3.89 vs 3.94, 3.11 vs 3.17, 0.78 vs 0.77, all within 90% intervals), but there is no multi-seed stability or coverage check, and the zero direct effect is imposed by the spec rather than validated.
- **Watertight (2/5).** All printed numbers are internally consistent and the estimand/assumptions are stated correctly, but the sensitivity formula behind the headline ROBUST claim is incoherent, the lever ranking is not scale-licensed, an r-hat warning sits unaddressed in committed output, and a caveat gives wrong guidance about the tool.

</details>

- **🔴 CRITICAL · business — ✅ verified** — `Cell 11 (Step 6 leverage ranking) and its printed table (onboarding 467 / engagement 217 / activated 107)`
  - **Issue.** The lever ranking compares posterior ATE per one-unit change times EUR 120 across variables measured on incommensurate scales, with no cost-to-move model. In the DGP, one unit of onboarding_score is the variable's entire range (~3.46 SD, sd=0.289), while one unit of engagement is ~1.23 SD (sd~0.815) and one unit of activated is ~0.70 SD (sd~1.44). Converting to per-SD euro values using the same posterior means gives engagement ~EUR 175 > activated ~EUR 155 > onboarding ~EUR 136 — the exact opposite ranking of the one the notebook headlines. The opening question ('fixed budget to split across the funnel') is never answered: a euros-per-unit table cannot allocate a budget without euros-per-unit-lift costs per stage, which are never stated.
  - **Evidence.** dgp.funnel (src/cmp/dgp.py:195-223): onboarding_score ~ U(0,1); engagement = 2.2*onb + 1.1*ch + N(0,0.4) so var = (2.2^2+1.1^2)/12 + 0.16 = 0.664. Per-SD effects: onboarding 3.94*0.289=1.14, engagement 1.79*0.815=1.46, activated 0.9*1.44=1.29. pathmc even ships model.standardized() ('coef * sd(X)/sd(Y)') for exactly this comparison and it is unused.
  - **Why it matters.** This is the notebook's answer to its own title question, and it flips under a different (equally arbitrary) choice of units. One question from a sharp MBA — 'is one unit of onboarding comparable to one unit of engagement?' — collapses the recommendation. It misleads the decision, which is the definition of critical under this repo's bar.
  - **Fix.** Introduce explicit cost assumptions (EUR spent buys delta-units of each stage's metric, stated as a table) and rank by euro return per euro spent, with a break-even cost per stage and P(ROI>0) from the posterior; at minimum, present the standardized ranking alongside the raw one and state plainly that per-unit rankings are unit-dependent. Also replace the uninformative all-1.0 P(>0) column with P(return > cost).
  - **Verifier.** Every factual claim verified against the artifacts. (1) Cell 11 of notebooks/04_funnel_mediation.ipynb ranks levers by raw per-unit posterior-mean ATE x EUR 120 and prints onboarding 467 / engagement 217 / activated 107 with an all-1.0 P(>0) column; no cost-per-unit-lift model appears anywhere, so the opening 'fixed budget to split' question is answered only under an unstated equal-cost-per-raw-unit assumption. - **🔴 CRITICAL · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 11, sensitivity block (rho sweep, 'gap' formula, and the printed 'call is ROBUST' conclusion; right panel of the Step 6 figure, PDF p.4)`
  - **Issue.** The confounding stress test is internally incoherent on three counts. (a) Direction: the comment says 'confounding inflates apparent engagement value', but the code ADDS r*|c_eng|*VALUE to engagement's value — modeling engagement's true value as HIGHER than estimated, the opposite scenario. (b) Propagation: any bias delta in the engagement->converted coefficient also biases onboarding's total effect by e_on*delta ~ 2.15*delta (onboarding's ATE flows through the same edge), so freezing onboarding while adjusting engagement is inconsistent with the fitted SCM — under either bias direction, coherent propagation moves the gap differently than coded (if c_eng is inflated, both levers deflate and the gap shrinks by (e_on-1)*delta*V; if c_eng is suppressed, the gap WIDENS with rho, not shrinks). (c) Calibration and design: rho is never defined (bias = rho*|c_eng| is arbitrary, rho runs to 1.5 so it is not a correlation), no posterior uncertainty is propagated (means only, despite the notebook's own line that 'the point estimate alone hides that fragility'), and the maximum swept penalty is 1.5*0.361*120 = EUR 65 against a EUR 250 gap — the sweep cannot flip by construction, so 'ROBUST' is baked in rather than demonstrated. It also stress-tests only the engagement->converted edge while ignoring activated->converted, the mediator-outcome edge that carries most of the value.
  - **Evidence.** gap = [(onb) - (eng + r*abs(c_eng)*VALUE) for r in rho] with comment '# confounding inflates apparent engagement value'; e_on posterior mean 2.150 (cell 6) means onboarding loads 2.15x on the same confounded edge. pathmc ships model.sensitivity() (pathmc/_model.py:1244, pathmc/sensitivity.py) implementing the VanderWeele & Ding gamma-x-delta grid with prob_sign_change and a contour plot — exactly the 'sensitivity RANGES/contours' the repo's four-axes bar asks for — and it is unused.
  - **Why it matters.** This is the notebook's flagship honesty move ('the honest one most mediation analyses skip') and the payoff promised in Steps 1, 3, and 6 ('show how strong it would have to be to flip'). The figure and the ROBUST verdict rest on a formula whose code contradicts its own comment; anyone who reads the cell in the lecture repo can dismantle it, and stakeholders cannot 'judge if rho=1.5 is plausible' because rho means nothing.
  - **Fix.** Replace the hand-rolled sweep with pathmc's sensitivity() contour (gamma = confounder->mediator, delta = confounder->outcome, bias = gamma*delta), applied coherently to BOTH levers' effects through the fitted graph, propagating posterior draws; report the (gamma, delta) frontier at which the onboarding-vs-engagement ranking flips and benchmark it against the strength of the observed confounder channel_quality (the standard calibration move). Cover the activated->converted edge too.
  - **Verifier.** Every factual citation checks out against the artifacts, and the statistical criticism is sound.

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 0 ('pushing posterior draws through the intervened graph'), cell 4 ('by simulating through the intervened graph'), and caveat 3 in cell 12`
  - **Issue.** The notebook repeatedly claims pathmc computes path-specific effects by simulating/propagating draws through the intervened graph, but compute_path_effect (pathmc/effects.py:280-344) literally multiplies posterior draws of the edge coefficients — product-of-coefficients, the very 'hand-multiplied coefficients' the notebook warns against. Only ate()/do() simulate through the graph. Caveat 3 then advises: for strong nonlinearities 'lean on pathmc's simulate-through-the-graph numbers, not hand-multiplied coefficients' — but the notebook's own via_act/via_eng numbers ARE coefficient products and would NOT be valid under nonlinearity.
  - **Evidence.** pathmc/effects.py:340-344: 'result_draws = edge_draws[0]; for d in edge_draws[1:]: result_draws = result_draws * d'.
  - **Why it matters.** In this linear DGP the two coincide so no number is wrong, but the methodological claim is false and the caveat gives actively wrong guidance for exactly the situation (nonlinearity) it addresses — a verifiable inaccuracy about the tool in a lecture that showcases the tool.
  - **Fix.** Correct the narration: effect(path) is the posterior product-of-coefficients (exact in linear SCMs); ate()/do() simulate interventions through the graph. Rewrite caveat 3 to say that under nonlinearity path decomposition needs mediation-formula simulation (nested do() counterfactuals), not effect(path).
  - **Verifier.** Code verification: pathmc's compute_path_effect (effects.py:306-345) extracts per-edge posterior coefficient draws and multiplies them (lines 341-343: `result_draws = result_draws * d`) — a pure product-of-coefficients with zero simulation. PathModel.effect() (_model.py:501-524) just wraps it. Conversely, do() (_model.py:912-1022) documents and implements PyMC-native graph surgery (pm.do + posterior predictive/compute_deterministics), and ate() (_model.py:1024-1059) is do(hi)-do(lo). Notebook verification: cell 0 claims pathmc "generalises" the a·b product "by pushing posterior draws through the intervened graph" and "computes path-specific effects by propagating posterior draws through the …
  - **Corrected statement.** In notebook 04, effect(path) should be described as the posterior product of edge coefficients (exact for linear SCMs), while only ate()/do() simulate interventions through the intervened graph via pm.do(); caveat 3 should say that under strong nonlinearity path-specific decomposition requires mediation-formula simulation (nested do() counterfactuals), not effect(path) coefficient products.

- **🟡 MINOR · pedagogical** — `Cell 9 (DAG panel) and cell 10 ('Left is the causal graph we fit'); Step 3 has no DAG`

The Identify step (cell 4), where the contract calls for a DAG, has no DAG at all.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 9: pos = {onboarding, engagement, activated, converted} only; PDF p.3 left panel confirms channel_quality absent.
  - **Why it matters.** The DAG is the identification device; hiding the measured confounder undercuts the adjust-for-channel-quality story and makes the 'no direct arrow' reading of the figure incomplete for the audience.

- **🟡 MINOR · pedagogical** — `Cell 6 output table (hdi_3%/hdi_97%) vs cell 8 printout (90% quantile intervals)`
  - **Issue.** Step 4 reports 94% HDIs while Step 5 reports 90% equal-tailed quantile intervals; neither convention is defined for the audience and the switch is not explained.
  - **Why it matters.** Terms-defined-on-first-use is an explicit bar for this repo; an MBA audience will not know what hdi_3%/hdi_97% means or why the interval width convention changed between consecutive tables.
  - **Fix.** Pick one convention (e.g., 90% equal-tailed credible intervals everywhere), define 'credible interval' in one sentence at first use, or add a one-line note explaining the HDI columns in the effects_summary table.

- **🟡 MINOR · code** — `Cell 8, final print statement and its output ('Proportion mediated ... 100% [99%, 101%] — most of onboarding's value is realised downstream.')`
  - **Issue.** The conclusion clause 'most of onboarding's value is realised downstream' is hard-coded inside the f-string and would print regardless of the computed proportion; and the interval's upper bound of 101% (>100%, from ratio-of-draws Monte Carlo noise around a structurally-exact 100%) is shown with no explanation.
  - **Why it matters.** A proportion above 100% is exactly the kind of detail a sharp attendee asks about, and a conclusion string that does not depend on the number is fragile if seeds/specs change.
  - **Fix.** Condition the printed conclusion on the computed value, and add one line: the fitted graph has no direct edge so the true proportion is exactly 100%; draws of the ratio scatter around 1, which is why the interval brackets 100%.

- **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `Cell 4, assumptions paragraph ('the cross-world condition that no M-Y confounder is itself affected by X')`
  - **Issue.** The condition named is VanderWeele's fourth assumption (no mediator-outcome confounder affected by treatment), which is a sufficient condition under which the cross-world independence assumption (Y(x,m) independent of M(x') given covariates) holds — labeling it 'the cross-world condition' conflates the two.
  - **Why it matters.** Minor for an MBA audience, but the repo doubles as a durable internal toolkit and a methods-savvy reader could poke at the naming; precision here is cheap.
  - **Fix.** Rename it 'no treatment-induced mediator-outcome confounding' and add a parenthetical that this is the practical stand-in for Pearl/Imai's cross-world independence assumption.

- **⚪ POLISH · pedagogical** — `PDF p.4: robustness printout and right-hand sensitivity figure`
  - **Issue.** The printed verdict wraps awkwardly mid-sentence ('confounding we / swept (rho=1.5)'), and the fragility plot shows a nearly flat line far above the zero threshold across the whole sweep — visually communicating that the stress test had no chance of flipping anything (a symptom of the sweep-design issue above, but also just a weak lecture figure).
  - **Why it matters.** Lecture-grade figures should carry the argument at a glance; this one shows a non-event.
  - **Fix.** Fix the print width; once the sensitivity is rebuilt as a (gamma, delta) contour with a flip frontier and a marker for the channel_quality-benchmark strength, the figure becomes genuinely informative.

### Notebook 05 — What to control for

**Grade: adequate** · 1 critical · 6 major · 12 findings total

| Diagnostics | Business | Narration | Validation | Watertight |
|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|
| 3 | 2 | 4 | 2 | 2 |

The notebook's skeleton is excellent — identification cleanly separated from estimation, a machine-checked backdoor step via pathmc, and a memorable five-way control-choice bar chart validated against a known €6 truth. But it has one lecture-embarrassing internal contradiction (pathmc's committed printout declares {loyalty, opened_email} safe — "OK — no collider opened" — while the very next figure shows that set is biased by −€0.55, because the declared DAG omits the simulator's hidden engagement trait; the notebook never reconciles this), and the sensitivity section is muddled: the contour promises a "black = effect crosses zero" tipping line that mathematically cannot appear on the default (0,1)×(0,1) grid (adjusted ATE never drops below ≈€5.07), the E-value bar chart plots €6.07 next to an RR-scale 3.29 on a single axis labeled "RR scale" (the effect on the RR scale is ≈1.94), and an r-hat>1.01 warning in the committed output goes unaddressed. Business (no actual euro decision in step 6) and validation (single seed, no intervals on the truth-recovery bars, mediator/M-bias never demonstrated) both sit below the four-axes bar. Fixable with targeted edits; the conceptual core is sound.

**Strengths.**
- Identification is genuinely separated from estimation and made machine-checkable: pathmc enumerates [{'loyalty'}] as the admissible set, confirms identifiability, and flags the 'responded' collider from structure alone (cell 8), with a correct statement of the backdoor criterion (cells 0, 7) — exactly the right pedagogy for 'what to control for'.
- The five-way control-choice comparison against a known €6 truth (cell 10, PDF p.3) is a crisp, memorable centerpiece: naive +3.45 (up, as confounding predicts), collider −0.42 (down, as collider bias predicts), 'everything' worst of all — every bias direction matches theory, and the 'the model can't tell you it's biased' moral (cell 11) is exactly the right takeaway for an MBA audience.
- Conceptual narration is tight and correct: all four variable roles defined on first use with the right rule for each, the M-bias panel explicitly kills the 'adjust for everything pre-treatment' heuristic, and the caveats (the graph is an assumption; colliders hide in 'obvious' engagement metrics; front-door fallback; sensitivity ≠ proof) are honest and well-chosen.

<details><summary>Axis notes</summary>

- **Diagnostics (3/5).** The right diagnostic family is present (adjustment-set enumeration, collider warnings, sensitivity contour, E-value), but the contour cannot show the promised tipping point, pathmc's test_implications()/falsification — the one diagnostic that would have caught the DAG misspecification from data — is unused, and the r-hat warning is unaddressed.
- **Business (2/5).** Biases are shown in € per customer, but step 6 'Decide, in euros' contains no decision: no campaign-scale translation (naive overstates lift by 57%), no break-even, COSTLINE=0 unexplained, and the E-value is never tied to a business threshold despite metrics.e_value supporting a cost argument.
- **Narration (4/5).** Definitions are crisp and correct on first use, the backdoor criterion is stated properly, and the 'machine doing the reasoning' narration works; loses a point because the actual mechanism biasing {loyalty, opened_email} (a hidden engagement trait) is never narrated and the E-value's RR scale is never explained for a euro outcome.
- **Validation (2/5).** Single seed, point estimates only: no error bars on the five truth-recovery bars (so +0.09 'success' vs −0.42 'bias' cannot be separated from Monte Carlo noise, per-bar SE ≈ €0.2), the available observed_ate_hdi is never shown, no multi-seed stability, and mediator/M-bias — half the intro gallery — are never validated empirically.
- **Watertight (2/5).** Core recovery numbers are correct and internally consistent, but the committed outputs contain an unreconciled contradiction (pathmc blesses a set the validation shows is biased), a figure caption asserting a zero-crossing that cannot exist on the plotted grid, a mixed-units bar chart labeled 'RR scale', a false 'E-value summarises the tipping surface' claim, and an unaddressed r-hat warning.

</details>

- **🔴 CRITICAL · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cells 8-11 (pathmc printout vs bar chart), with root cause in src/cmp/dgp.py:239-241 and the spec in cell 8`
  - **Issue.** The committed pathmc output says "control for {'opened_email', 'loyalty'}: OK — no collider opened", yet the validation two cells later shows that exact set is biased (€5.45, error −0.55). Root cause: the simulator generates opened_email = f(email, engagement_trait) and spend = f(loyalty, email, engagement_trait), making opened_email a collider between email and an UNOBSERVED engagement trait — but the DAG declared to pathmc (opened_email ~ b2*email) omits engagement_trait, so the tool cannot see the collider. Under the declared DAG, adjusting for a pure descendant of T would in fact be harmless for bias, so the notebook's own claim that {loyalty, opened} is 'another no-no' is not explained by the graph it drew. The contradiction is never acknowledged or reconciled.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 8 output: "control for {'opened_email', 'loyalty'}:  OK — no collider opened"; cell 10 output: "{loyalty,opened} ✗   € 5.45 (error -0.55)". dgp.py:240-241: opened_email = sigmoid(1.5*email + 0.7*engagement_trait); spend = 20 + 5*loyalty + 6*email + 3*engagement_trait + noise — opened_email never enters the spend equation, and engagement_trait never enters the cell-8 spec. pathmc's own docstring (identify.py:66-72) warns it "cannot detect omitted variables" and points to test_implications().
  - **Why it matters.** This is the notebook whose entire thesis is 'let the DAG decide, and the machine checks it' — and its own committed outputs show the machine green-lighting a control set that the ground truth proves is biased. A sharp audience member reading the printout against the bar chart catches it in seconds, and the lecturer has no scripted answer.
  - **Fix.** Turn the bug into the lesson: declare engagement_trait in the spec (or narrate explicitly that the drawn DAG omits it), show that pathmc's advice is only as good as the drawn graph — echoing the existing 'the graph is an assumption' caveat — and run pathmc's test_implications(), which would refute the declared DAG's testable implication opened_email ⊥ spend | email straight from the data. Also fix the dgp.py docstring (see separate finding).
  - **Verifier.** Every factual citation checks out and the statistics are sound. (a) Accuracy: cell 8's committed output does print "control for {'opened_email', 'loyalty'}: OK — no collider opened" while cell 10's committed output shows that set yields €5.45 (error −0.55); dgp.py:239-241 does generate opened_email = sigmoid(1.5*email + 0.7*engagement_trait) and spend = 20 + 5*loyalty + 6*email + 3*engagement_trait + noise, so opened_email is a collider between email and the unobserved engagement_trait (and, contra the dgp docstring, NOT a mediator — it never enters the spend equation); the cell-8 pathmc spec omits engagement_trait; and pathmc's identify.py docstrings (lines 66-72 and 263-269) say verbatim t…

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 12 (contour panel), title 'Sensitivity to a hidden confounder (black = effect crosses zero)'; PDF page 4`
  - **Issue.** The contour plot promises a black zero-crossing line, but none can exist: m.sensitivity() was called with the default gamma_range=(0,1), delta_range=(0,1), and pathmc's bias model is adjusted ATE = observed ATE − γ·δ, so the surface spans [6.07−1, 6.07] ≈ [5.07, 6.07] — confirmed by the PDF colorbar (5.04-6.00). The narrative's 'tipping surface' (γδ = 6.07) lies entirely outside the plotted grid; the figure shows at most a 17% attenuation and says nothing about overturning the conclusion.
  - **Evidence.** pathmc/_model.py:1248-1249 (defaults (0.0, 1.0)); pathmc/sensitivity.py:96-104 (tipping point = observed ATE = 6.07, since adjusted = observed − γδ); PDF p.4 colorbar range 5.04-6.00, no black contour visible.
  - **Why it matters.** The caption asserts a feature the figure does not contain; a viewer looking for the black line concludes either the plot is broken or the effect is unconditionally robust — neither is what the analysis shows. The section's stated purpose ('how strong would a confounder have to be to overturn the conclusion?') is not answered by the figure.
  - **Fix.** Pass gamma_range/delta_range wide enough to contain the tipping hyperbola (e.g. (0,3)×(0,3), since γδ must reach 6.07), draw and label the γδ = tipping_point curve (pathmc exposes .tipping_point), or plot prob_sign_change; also state what units γ and δ are in (raw additive effects on a 0/1 treatment and a € outcome).
  - **Verifier.** Every factual claim verifies against the artifacts. (a) Notebook cell 12 calls m.sensitivity("spend", "email", n_grid=12) with no ranges; installed pathmc/_model.py:1248-1249 defaults both gamma_range and delta_range to (0.0, 1.0). pathmc/sensitivity.py:264-265 computes adjusted = observed_ate − γδ, and the tipping_point property (lines 96-104) equals the observed ATE = 6.07 (printed in cell 12 output). On [0,1]² the max bias is γδ=1, so the surface spans [5.07, 6.07] and the zero contour requested by ax[0].contour(..., levels=[0], colors="k") cannot exist — yet the title hard-codes "(black = effect crosses zero)". Rendering PDF page 4 confirms: axes 0-1 × 0-1, colorbar 5.04-6.00, no black l…

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 12, right panel (ax[1].bar) and the preceding markdown in cell 11 ('the E-value summarises it as a single interpretable number')`
  - **Issue.** The bar chart plots abs(observed_ate) = €6.07 (a euro effect) next to the E-value 3.29 (a risk-ratio-scale association) on one axis labeled 'association strength (RR scale)'. €6.07 is not on the RR scale; the observed effect converted to that scale is ≈1.94 (metrics.e_value maps d = 6.07/sd(spend≈8.3) ≈ 0.73 to RR = exp(0.91·d) ≈ 1.94, whence E-value 1.94 + √(1.94·0.94) = 3.29). Relatedly, the markdown claims the E-value 'summarises' the pathmc tipping surface — it does not: it is an independent VanderWeele RR-scale computation, unconnected to the γδ grid (whose tipping product is 6.07 in raw €·probability units).
  - **Evidence.** Cell 12: ax[1].bar([...], [abs(float(sens.observed_ate)), evalue]) with ylabel 'association strength (RR scale)'; metrics.py:124-130 (RR = exp(0.91·d) with d = |estimate−cost|/sd, E = RR + √(RR(RR−1))); reproduction with sd(spend) ≈ 8.3 gives RR ≈ 1.94 and E ≈ 3.29, matching the printed output.
  - **Why it matters.** The panel invites a wrong reading ('the observed effect is bigger than what's needed to null it?!') and the taller blue bar means nothing coherent; a statistically literate audience member will ask where 3.29 lives on the contour axes, and there is no answer. This is a headline lecture figure with mismatched units.
  - **Fix.** Plot both bars on the RR scale (observed ≈ 1.94 vs E-value 3.29) — which correctly shows the confounder must be STRONGER than the observed association — and reword the markdown: the contour and the E-value are two different sensitivity parameterizations (raw additive γδ vs RR-scale), not a surface and its summary. Add one sentence defining the RR conversion for a continuous € outcome.
  - **Verifier.** Factual accuracy verified: Cell 12 of the notebook plots [abs(observed_ate)=6.07, evalue=3.29] as bars on a single axis with ylabel 'association strength (RR scale)', and Cell 11 markdown says the E-value 'summarises' the pathmc tipping surface. src/cmp/metrics.py:113-130 implements e_value as d=|estimate−cost|/sd, RR=exp(0.91·d), E=RR+√(RR(RR−1)), using only the point estimate/cost/sd — never the γδ grid. - **🟠 MAJOR · business** — `Cell 11 markdown '## 6 · Decide, in euros — with a robustness statement' and cell 12`
  - **Issue.** Step 6 is titled 'Decide, in euros' but contains no decision and no euros beyond the per-customer ATE: no campaign-scale consequence of each wrong control set (e.g. naive €9.45 vs true €6.00 overstates incremental revenue by 57% — at 100k mails that is a phantom €345k in the business case; the collider set understates by €0.42/customer, enough to wrongly kill a marginal campaign), no break-even, no go/no-go, and COSTLINE = 0.0 is set without explanation even though metrics.e_value supports a non-zero break-even threshold that would tie robustness directly to the decision.

  - **Fix.** Extend dag_control_demo (or add a small second DGP) with a true mediator (e.g. site_visit on the email→spend path) and an M-structure pre-treatment variable; add two bars to the comparison showing the mediator over-control bias (estimate collapses toward the direct effect) and the M-bias, in euros.

  - **Evidence.** dgp.py:241: spend = 20 + 5*loyalty + true_ate*email + 3*engagement_trait + noise — no opened_email term.

  - **Fix.** Rewrite the docstring: 'opened_email is a post-treatment collider between email and an unobserved engagement trait that also drives spend; it is NOT a mediator (spend does not depend on it).'

- **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `Cells 13-14 (LaLonde section) and README.md:148`
  - **Issue.** The section's interpretive strings are hardcoded in print() — '(badly biased — groups differ hugely)' and '(recovers the ~$1,800 experimental truth)' will print regardless of what naive2 and adj2 actually compute — and the committed output shows the section skipped (CMP_REAL unset), so the markdown claims ('recovers ~$1,800', 'can flip the sign') are never evidenced in the artifact. - **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `Cell 9 markdown, punchline paragraph`
  - **Issue.** 'The sign and rough size of each bias is predictable from the graph *before* you run anything' overclaims: a DAG encodes structure only; predicting the SIGN of each bias additionally requires the signs of the edge effects (e.g. loyalty raising both email propensity and spend), which the text silently assumes.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 9: 'the sign and rough size of each bias is predictable from the graph before you run anything'.
  - **Why it matters.** A sharp audience member can correctly object that the bare graph cannot give a bias direction; one clause fixes it and protects the lecturer.

  - **Why it matters.** The repo bar requires every term defined on first use and cross-links between notebooks; '3.3×' on an undefined scale is precisely the kind of number an MBA repeats without being able to defend.
  - **Fix.** Add one sentence: 'For a euro outcome we standardize the effect (d ≈ 0.73 sd) and convert to an approximate risk ratio via RR ≈ exp(0.91·d); the E-value is on that scale.' Add '(see notebook 04)' to the front-door bullet.

### Notebook 06 — Incrementality MMM

**Grade: weak** · 3 critical · 7 major · 14 findings total

| Diagnostics | Business | Narration | Validation | Watertight |
|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|
| 2 | 3 | 4 | 2 | 2 |

The notebook's pedagogical core is excellent — a seeded DGP (dgp.mmm_weekly) where seasonality confounds brand-search spend, generated with the MMM's own adstock + Michaelis-Menten form, so the naive-vs-adjusted confounding contrast (4,843 → 679 vs truth 333) is clean, decisive and truth-checked — and the honest twin-theme framing ("trust the ranking, calibrate levels with a geo experiment, nb 07") is exactly right. But the statistics are not watertight, which is the non-negotiable bar. Three claims are contradicted by the notebook's own outputs or ground truth: (1) the how-to-read cell says TV's ROI interval "sits above the break-even line (1×)" while the printed 90% CI directly above it is [0.29, 8.02], visibly straddling 1× in the lecture figure; (2) the headline decision number P(TV ROI > brand_search ROI)=0.96 — repeated in the README — is miscomputed as P(roi_bs < mean(roi_tv)), collapsing TV's huge uncertainty to a point; (3) the true TV ROI implied by the notebook's own ground truth is ~3,536/4,190 ≈ 0.84×, BELOW break-even, so the repeated claim that the MMM "gets each channel's ROI verdict right" and "TV clears it" is false against the known truth — true ROI is never computed. The committed fit also carries 16 divergences, r-hat > 1.01, ESS/chain < 100 and max-treedepth hits with no in-notebook acknowledgment; the caveat's "~2–3× the truth" understates the actual 3.3× (TV) and 6.3× (brand_search) overshoots; brand_search's true contribution (333) falls outside its ~[613, 2,272] 90% posterior interval unremarked; and the README's "recovers TV well" does not match the committed 3.3× overshoot. Diagnostics and validation are thin against the four-axes bar (no PPC, no coverage check, single seed, no parameter-recovery check despite known adstock/saturation truth, one fixed 15% reallocation scenario, no margin step in the euro decision). Fixable with targeted edits, but in its committed state a sharp MBA could break the headline decision in one question.

**Strengths.**
- The confounder-by-design DGP is flagship-grade pedagogy: dgp.mmm_weekly (src/cmp/dgp.py:259-308) makes seasonality drive both sales (35*season) and brand-search spend (25+18*season), and generates sales with the exact adstock + Michaelis-Menten form the MMM fits — so the naive-vs-adjusted OLS contrast (brand_search credit 4,843 naive vs 679 adjusted vs 333 true, Cell 9) isolates pure confounding and is fully validated against known truth. This is the strongest, most defensible result in the notebook and it is correctly led with.
- Honest framing that mirrors real practice: the twin themes (ranking robust / absolute levels unreliable, calibrate with a geo experiment in nb 07) are stated up front (Cell 0), repeated before estimation (Cell 6), in the figure read-out (Cell 10), and in the caveats (Cell 13); identification is cleanly separated from estimation, with the DAG handed to pymc-marketing and the backdoor adjustment set ['seasonality'] actually printed (Cell 5).
- Conceptual narration is MBA-ready: adstock, saturation, last-click attribution, incremental-vs-mediated, and confounder are each defined crisply on first use (Cell 0); the business hook (brand search catches demand it did not create) is compelling; the 7-step contract is followed end to end; kernel (cmp-legacy) matches the documented env split and the FAST/seed conventions are correctly implemented.

<details><summary>Axis notes</summary>

- **Diagnostics (2/5).** The naive-vs-adjusted confounding contrast and adjustment-set printout are good, but the method's signature diagnostics are missing: no posterior-predictive/fit-over-time plot, no r-hat/ESS/divergence handling despite visible warnings, no adstock/saturation parameter-recovery check against the known truth (lam=0.4/0.2), no prior sensitivity; 'saturation curves' are a same-week scatter, not fitted response curves.
- **Business (3/5).** Clear go/no-go framing, a concrete reallocation action with a probability statement, and an honest average-vs-marginal caveat — but a single fixed 15% scenario computed from posterior means, the headline probability is miscomputed, there is no shift-size sweep, budget-optimizer, or VOI, and break-even at 1× revenue/spend ignores margin entirely.
- **Narration (4/5).** Terms defined on first use, DAG explicit, why-causal-MMM section is genuinely good, cross-links to nb 05 (backdoor) and nb 07 (geo calibration) are accurate; docked one point for the muddy estimand statement (undefined 'baseline') and the vacuous 'ROI is far more stable than the absolute contribution' claim.
- **Validation (2/5).** Recover-the-truth is eyeball-only: no interval-coverage check (brand_search truth 333 falls outside its ~[613, 2,272] 90% interval), true ROI never computed so the 'ROI verdict' claim goes unchecked (and is false for TV), single seed, no multi-seed stability, no calibration/sensitivity range.
- **Watertight (2/5).** Three claims contradicted by the notebook's own outputs or ground truth (interval-above-break-even, the P=0.96 formula, TV's true ROI 0.84× vs the 'clears break-even' verdict), plus unaddressed divergences/r-hat/ESS warnings in the committed fit and a caveat that understates the overshoot the outputs show.

</details>

- **🔴 CRITICAL · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 10 (how-to-read markdown), contradicted by Cell 9 output and PDF p.3 middle panel`
  - **Issue.** The how-to-read cell states "TV's interval sits above the break-even line (1×)", but the printed output directly above it is "ROI — TV 2.81× [90% 0.29, 8.02]": the 90% credible interval straddles 1× by a wide margin, and the errorbar visibly crosses the dashed break-even line in the rendered figure.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 9 stdout: "ROI — TV 2.81× [90% 0.29,8.02] · brand_search 0.82× [90% 0.24,0.89]"; Cell 10: "TV's interval sits above the break-even line (1×) and brand_search's sits below it".
  - **Why it matters.** This is the decision-relevant panel ("the whole budget story in one picture"). Any attendee who reads the interval printed two lines above the claim sees the contradiction; it is a misread of the notebook's own diagnostic and the exact kind of interval-language error the cookbook is supposed to model correctly.
  - **Fix.** State it correctly: TV's posterior mean clears break-even but its 90% interval is wide and includes values below 1×, i.e. the data support the ranking (P(TV ROI > BS ROI)) more strongly than TV's own above-break-even verdict; or run the full (non-FAST) fit if it genuinely tightens the interval and re-commit.
  - **Verifier.** Both prongs hold. (a) Factually accurate: Cell 9 stdout reads "ROI — TV 2.81× [90% 0.29,8.02] · brand_search 0.82× [90% 0.24,0.89]" (nb_text line 218), and Cell 10 says "TV's interval sits above the break-even line (1×) and brand_search's sits below it" (lines 228-229). The forest plot is drawn from those exact 5%/95% quantiles with ref=1.0 (lines 203-205), and PDF p.3 middle panel visibly shows TV's errorbar crossing the dashed 1× line. (b) Statistically sound: a 90% CI of [0.29, 8.02] straddles 1× — only the posterior mean clears break-even; the brand_search half of the sentence ([0.24, 0.89] fully below 1×) is a genuine interval-level claim, so no alternate reading rescues the TV half. Th…
  - **Corrected statement.** Cell 10 should say: TV's posterior mean ROI (2.81×) clears break-even, but its 90% credible interval [0.29, 8.02] is wide and includes values below 1×, so TV's above-break-even verdict is not interval-decisive; brand_search's interval [0.24, 0.89] sits entirely below break-even. - **🔴 CRITICAL · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 12, line `p_gain = (roi_tv.mean() > roi_bs).mean()``
  - **Issue.** The headline probability printed as "P(TV ROI > brand_search ROI) = 0.96" is computed by comparing the scalar posterior MEAN of TV's ROI against brand_search draws, i.e. it is P(roi_bs < 2.81), not the draw-by-draw P(roi_tv > roi_bs). TV's uncertainty (90% CI [0.29, 8.02]) is discarded entirely from the comparison.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 12 code: `p_gain = (roi_tv.mean() > roi_bs).mean()   # prob TV ROI beats brand_search ROI draws` followed by `print(f"P(TV ROI > brand_search ROI) = {p_gain:.2f} ...")`; README line ~216ff quotes the reallocation result.
  - **Why it matters.** This is the number that triggers the recommendation ("→ reallocate toward TV") and is quoted in the README as a headline result. Mislabeling P(bs-draws below a point estimate) as a joint posterior probability is a wrong-stats error; the correct draw-wise probability could differ materially given TV's interval dips to 0.29 (below brand_search's mean of 0.82).
  - **Fix.** Compute `(roi_tv > roi_bs).mean()` on aligned posterior draws (they come from the same trace, so this also correctly captures the posterior correlation between the two channels' contributions), re-run, and update the printed number and the README's P=0.96 claim.
  - **Verifier.** Cell 12 of the notebook does exactly what the reviewer claims: `p_gain = (roi_tv.mean() > roi_bs).mean()` computes P(roi_bs < 2.81) — brand_search draws vs TV's scalar posterior mean — yet is printed as "P(TV ROI > brand_search ROI) = 0.96" and gates the printed recommendation via p_gain > 0.8. roi_tv/roi_bs are full posterior-draw arrays (built in cells 5 and 9 from the same MMM trace via .values.ravel() over identical (chain, draw) dims), so TV's uncertainty (90% CI [0.29, 8.02]) is genuinely discarded. The suggested fix `(roi_tv > roi_bs).mean()` is statistically correct: it is the Monte Carlo estimator of the joint-posterior probability, and since both arrays are raveled from the same tr…
  - **Corrected statement.** The finding is correct as written, with one small evidence correction: the README does not quote the P=0.96 figure — it references notebook 06's ROI/reallocation verdict qualitatively (README lines 64 and 213-219). The fix therefore applies to the notebook cell 12 and its PDF render only; no README number needs updating, though the qualitative "right budget call" framing should be re-checked after recomputing p_gain as (roi_tv > roi_bs).mean() on aligned draws.

- **🔴 CRITICAL · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 6 ("What the MMM does get right ... each channel's ROI verdict") and Cell 11 ("brand_search sits below break-even ..., TV clears it"); ground truth from Cell 3 output + dgp.mmm_weekly`
  - **Issue.** Against the notebook's own ground truth, TV's TRUE ROI is below break-even: true TV contribution 3,536 (Cell 3) over total TV spend ≈ 4,190 (= 11,775/2.81 from Cell 7/9 outputs; ≈ 40/week × 104 weeks per dgp.py:279) gives ≈ 0.84×. The MMM's 2.81× "clears break-even" verdict for TV is therefore an artifact of the very 3.3× level miscalibration the notebook warns about — yet the notebook never computes true ROI, so the repeated claim that the MMM gets "each channel's ROI verdict" right is asserted, unvalidated, and false for TV.
  - **Evidence.** true_tv = 3,536 (Cell 3); tv_post.mean() = 11,775 and roi_tv.mean() = 2.81 (Cells 7, 9) imply spend_tv ≈ 4,190; 3,536/4,190 ≈ 0.84 < 1. dgp.py:279 sets tv_spend ≈ 40/week; 40 × 104 = 4,160, consistent.
  - **Why it matters.** The notebook's entire trust hierarchy is "ranking and ROI verdict trustworthy, levels not." The ground truth supports only the ranking (0.84 > 0.13); the above/below-break-even verdict for TV flips between estimate and truth. A prepared student who divides the two printed truths by spend (spend_bs is even printed: €383 = 15% → 2,553) can derive this in one line during the lecture.
  - **Fix.** Print true ROI per channel next to the posterior ROI in the validation step. Then either (a) retune the DGP so TV's true ROI genuinely clears 1× (e.g. raise alpha in dgp.mmm_weekly) so the verdict story is truth-consistent, or (b) weaken the claim to "the ranking is trustworthy" and drop "TV clears break-even" / "ROI verdict" language.
  - **Verifier.** Both the factual accuracy and the statistical soundness of the finding hold.

(a) Factual accuracy — verified against the artifacts:
- Cell 3 output prints true_tv = 3,536, true_bs = 333 (nb_text/06_incrementality_mmm.md lines 77-78).

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 7 committed stderr outputs`
  - **Issue.** The committed fit shows 16 divergences after tuning, max-treedepth saturation in both chains, "rhat statistic is larger than 1.01", "effective sample size per chain is smaller than 100", and only 2 chains of 250 draws — and no markdown cell anywhere acknowledges or addresses these warnings.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 7 stderr: "There were 16 divergences after tuning.", "Chain 0/1 reached the maximum tree depth.", "The rhat statistic is larger than 1.01 for some parameters.", "The effective sample size per chain is smaller than 100...", "Sampling 2 chains for 300 tune and 250 draw iterations (600 + 500 draws total)".
  - **Why it matters.** Every decision quantity downstream (contributions 11,775/2,083, the ROI forest CIs, P=0.96, +€764) is computed from this posterior, whose own diagnostics say r-hat and ESS are unreliable and whose divergences can bias the estimates. It also muddies the notebook's central lesson: part of the "absolute levels run high" overshoot could be sampling artifact rather than the confounding/weak-identification story being taught. FAST mode is a documented repo tradeoff, but the review bar explicitly requires unaddressed convergence warnings in committed outputs to be flagged.
  - **Fix.** Add one honest markdown sentence ("FAST-mode fit: divergences/r-hat warnings expected; the full CMP_FAST=0 run is clean with ~identical contributions") only if that is verified true — or better, commit the notebook with the full run (4 chains, 1000 draws) since this figure and P-number are lecture headline material, and show a small az.summary r-hat/ESS table.
  - **Verifier.** Factually accurate: all five cited stderr messages appear verbatim in cell 7 of the committed notebook (extract lines 140-158; confirmed by grep on notebooks/06_incrementality_mmm.ipynb, which is clean in git) — 16 divergences after tuning, max-treedepth saturation in both chains, rhat > 1.01, ESS per chain < 100, and 2 chains x 250 draws. No markdown cell acknowledges any of it: cell 6, cell 10, and the Step-7 caveats (cell 13) attribute all imprecision to confounding/weak identification and never mention sampling diagnostics, chain count, or FAST mode (which exists only as code in cell 1); the "see note" in cell 7's stdout refers to the miscalibration note, not sampling. Aggravating detail…

- **🟠 MAJOR · consistency** — `Cell 13 first caveat; README.md lines ~216-220`
  - **Issue.** The caveat says contributions "ran ~2–3× the truth", but the committed outputs show TV at 3.33× (11,775/3,536) and brand_search at 6.25× (2,083/333). The README goes further and claims the causal MMM "recovers TV well", which the committed 3.3× TV overshoot flatly contradicts.

  - **Why it matters.** Narrative numbers inconsistent with cell outputs are a top-priority defect for this cookbook, and the README sells a design decision ("honest about MMM weakness ... recovers TV well") that the artifact does not deliver: TV's level is not recovered well; only the ranking and the confounding contrast are.

  - **Evidence.** Cell 9 stdout "brand_search credit — naive 4,843 | adjusted 679 | true 333" plus Cell 7 "brand_search 2,083"; the four bars are all in the left panel of the PDF p.3 figure.
  - **Why it matters.** A sharp audience member will ask the obvious question the figure begs: "why does the fancy causal MMM do 3× worse than plain OLS with a season control?"   - **Fix.** Rewrite the sentence honestly: the MMM cuts the naive credit by ~57% and preserves the go/no-go, but lands above the simple OLS adjustment on levels — then explain why in one sentence (flexible adstock/saturation soak up seasonal variance) and tie it to the calibrate-with-geo theme.

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cells 7-10 (Step 5, Validate) as a whole`
  - **Issue.** The recover-the-truth step is eyeball-only and would fail a strict check: brand_search's 90% contribution interval, derived from the printed ROI CI [0.24, 0.89] × spend 2,553, is ≈ [613, 2,272], which EXCLUDES the truth of 333 — never computed or remarked. There is also no interval-coverage statement for TV, no multi-seed stability run, no posterior predictive check, and no recovery check of the adstock/saturation parameters even though the DGP truth (lam=0.4/0.2, alpha, kappa) is known and the caveat asserts they are "weakly identified" without showing it.
  - **Evidence.** roi_bs 90% CI [0.24, 0.89] (Cell 9) × spend_bs 2,553 (= 383/0.15, Cell 12) = [613, 2,272]; true_bs = 333 (Cell 3). No coverage, PPC, seed-loop, or parameter-recovery code exists in the notebook.
  - **Why it matters.** The cookbook's stated bar requires rigorous validation (coverage, multi-seed stability, sensitivity ranges). Here the posterior is not just biased high, it is confidently wrong for brand_search (truth outside the 90% interval) — a much stronger and more teachable statement than "levels run high", and currently hidden.
  - **Fix.** Add an explicit truth-in-interval check per channel (and per-parameter recovery table for adstock/saturation), a 3-5 seed stability loop on the ROI ranking and P(roi_tv > roi_bs), and one PPC/fit-over-time panel. Turning the brand_search coverage failure into the explicit lesson ("the posterior is overconfident as well as biased — another reason to calibrate with a geo test") would strengthen, not weaken, the narrative.
  - **Verifier.** (a) Factually accurate. Every cited number is in the committed outputs: Cell 3 prints true_bs = 333; Cell 9 prints roi_bs 90% CI [0.24, 0.89]; Cell 12's printed moved=€383 at SHIFT=0.15 implies spend_bs ≈ 2,553 (matches the DGP mean 25/week × 104 weeks). Because roi_bs = bs_post/spend_bs is a deterministic linear rescale of the same draws (Cell 9), the brand_search contribution 90% CI is exactly [613, 2,272], which excludes the truth 333 (true ROI ≈ 0.13 < 0.24; cross-check: 0.82×2,553 ≈ 2,094 ≈ printed mean 2,083). The notebook only says levels "run high" (Cells 7, 10, 13) and never notes truth-outside-interval. Grep over the full extract confirms no coverage check, no PPC, no multi-seed lo…

- **🟠 MAJOR · business** — `Cells 9-12: ROI definition ("ROI = contribution ÷ spend") and break-even at 1×`
  - **Issue.** What is computed is revenue-per-euro (ROAS: incremental sales / spend), but it is called ROI with a break-even line at 1×, which implicitly assumes 100% gross margin. Margin is never mentioned; "projected +€764 sales" is likewise revenue, not profit.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 4: "ROI = contribution ÷ spend"; Cell 9 forest ref=1.0 titled "Channel ROI (× spend), 90% CI"; Cell 12 prints "+€764 sales". The word "margin" appears nowhere in the notebook.
  - **Why it matters.** For a business-first cookbook aimed at MBAs this is the first question from the room: "ROI of revenue or profit?" At a realistic 30% margin the break-even ROAS is 3.3×, and TV's 2.81× mean fails it — the go/no-go can flip on an assumption the notebook never states. Other notebooks in the series convert posteriors to euros with explicit margins; this one skips the step.
  - **Fix.** Introduce a margin parameter m, define break-even as ROAS = 1/m (or report incremental profit = m × contribution − spend), and show the verdict at 2-3 margin values as a one-line break-even table — this also adds the multi-parameter-sweep depth the business axis currently lacks.

- **🟠 MAJOR · business** — `Cells 11-12 (Step 6, Decide in euros)`
  - **Issue.** The decision step is a single fixed scenario: one 15% shift, delta computed from posterior means only (moved × (mean ROI difference)), with the miscomputed p_gain as its only uncertainty statement. No sweep over shift size, no marginal-ROI (saturation-aware) version despite the saturation panel motivating exactly that, no posterior distribution of delta_sales / P(delta > 0), no comparison of allocation policies, no value-of-information — and no truth-check of the decision quantity (true delta = 383 × (0.84 − 0.13) ≈ €272, vs the projected +€764, ~2.8× optimistic).
  - **Evidence.** Cell 12: `delta_sales = moved * (roi_tv.mean() - roi_bs.mean())`; printed "+€764". True delta from Cell 3 truths and spends: 383 × (3,536/4,190 − 333/2,553) ≈ 272.
  - **Why it matters.** The four-axes bar explicitly requires business-decision richness (sweeps, policy comparisons, VOI), and this notebook is the README's named example of "budget reallocation (06)". As committed, the euro decision inherits the untrusted absolute levels the notebook itself disclaims, with no sensitivity shown, and the projected gain is ~3× the true gain without comment.
  - **Fix.** Push delta_sales through the posterior (draw-wise), report its 90% interval and P(delta > 0); sweep SHIFT over e.g. 5-30% using marginal ROI from the fitted saturation curves (or pymc-marketing's budget optimizer); and print the true delta from true_contrib as the recover-the-truth check on the decision itself.

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical** — `Cell 8, view 2: "it's far more stable than the absolute contribution"`
  - **Issue.** The claim that posterior ROI is "far more stable than the absolute contribution" is mathematically empty as stated: ROI is the contribution divided by a fixed, observed spend total, so the ROI posterior inherits exactly the same relative miscalibration (TV ROI 2.81 vs true 0.84 is the same 3.3× factor as contribution 11,775 vs 3,536).
  - **Evidence.** roi_tv = tv_post/spend_tv (Cell 9) with spend_tv a scalar; 2.81/0.84 = 11,775/3,536 = 3.3.
  - **Why it matters.** It is a hand-wavy statistical assertion a sharp attendee can demolish in one line ("you divided by a constant"). What is actually stable is the cross-channel RANKING and (for brand_search only) the below-1 verdict — conflating that with ROI-level stability muddies the notebook's most important message.
  - **Fix.** Replace with the precise claim: "the ROI RANKING (and brand_search's below-break-even verdict) is robust to the level miscalibration; the ROI levels are biased by exactly the same factor as the contributions."

- **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `Cell 4 (Identify)`
  - **Issue.** The estimand is stated as "E[sales | do(x_c)] − baseline" with "baseline" undefined and the do-argument left generic; the quantity actually computed is the sum over weeks of the model's channel contribution, i.e. E[sales | do(spend_c = observed path)] − E[sales | do(spend_c = 0)] holding other channels at their observed paths.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 4: "The estimand for channel c is the interventional contribution E[sales | do(x_c)] − baseline".
  - **Why it matters.** The cookbook's contract requires the estimand stated precisely; as written, "baseline" could mean the model intercept, zero-all-channels, or zero-this-channel, which differ. Small fix, but this is the identification step of the flagship causal-MMM notebook.
  - **Fix.** Write the contrast explicitly (observed-spend path vs zero-spend path for channel c, other channels fixed, summed over weeks) and note it is identified via the backdoor set {seasonality}.

- **🟡 MINOR · pedagogical** — `Cell 9 panel 3 and Cell 10 ("saturation curves"); README "saturation/diminishing-returns curves"`
  - **Issue.** The "saturation curves" panel is a scatter of posterior-mean weekly contribution against SAME-WEEK spend; with adstock, each week's contribution also depends on prior weeks' spend, so the points do not lie on the saturation function, and no fitted curve (e.g. pymc-marketing's direct contribution / saturation curves with uncertainty) is drawn. The README's plural "curves" promises more than the delivered scatter.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 9: `ax[2].scatter(df["tv"], cw.sel(channel="tv").values, ...)` on raw weekly spend; dgp.py:282-294 shows contribution = saturate(adstock(spend)), so same-week spend is not the curve's argument.
  - **Why it matters.** The panel is used to justify the marginal-vs-average-ROI argument ("the next euro is worth the curve's slope"), but no curve or slope is actually shown, and the adstock-induced scatter can visually flatten or distort the diminishing-returns story on the projector.
  - **Fix.** Plot the fitted Michaelis-Menten saturation curve per channel (with a credible band) over the adstocked-spend axis, optionally overlaying the DGP's true curve (alpha, kappa known) — which would double as the missing parameter-recovery diagnostic.

- **🟡 MINOR · pedagogical** — `PDF p.3 middle panel (ROI forest, Cell 9)`
  - **Issue.** On the shared x-axis (0 to ~8) forced by TV's wide interval, brand_search's entire interval [0.24, 0.89] collapses to a dot touching the break-even dashed line — the below-break-even story the narration calls "the whole budget story in one picture" is essentially invisible at lecture scale.
  - **Evidence.** PDF page 3, middle panel: brand_search marker and error bar are visually indistinguishable from the 1× reference line; interval width 0.65 on an 8-unit axis.
  - **Why it matters.** This is the decision figure for the notebook; from the back of a lecture hall the audience cannot verify the claim being made about it.
  - **Fix.** Use a log-scaled x-axis or an inset/zoom for brand_search, and annotate each channel with its P(ROI > 1) so the verdict is readable regardless of scale.

- **⚪ POLISH · code** — `Cell 7 output; PDF p.2 ("Output()")`

### Notebook 07 — Geo-lift synthetic control (Anchor B ⭐)

**Grade: good** · 1 critical · 6 major · 13 findings total

| Diagnostics | Business | Narration | Validation | Watertight |
|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|:--:|
| 4 | 4 | 4 | 3 | 3 |

Anchor B is conceptually the strongest-narrated kind of notebook the repo aims for: the simplex/convex-hull story, the Dirichlet-prior framing, the assumption-by-check table, and the genuinely borderline TEST FURTHER decision are flagship-grade, and the README's claims (naive bake-off, simplex SC, RMSE-ratio placebo, LOO robustness, spaghetti + permutation p, P(lift>cost)~0.6) are all delivered. But the statistics are not yet watertight at the level the repo demands. The headline problem: the planted truth (EUR 339k) falls OUTSIDE the committed 90% credible interval [EUR 279k, 333k] and the notebook never says so — because the interval carries only donor-weight uncertainty (no predictive-noise term in cmp.estimators.synthetic_control), it systematically under-covers, which directly undermines the notebook's own thesis that "the interval, not the point estimate, drives the call". Around that sit several narrative-vs-output contradictions (Depth A calls treated-minus-average "closer" when the output shows it is farther; the decision paragraph claims "a handful of interpretable donors" against a printed eff_donors=14.7), a mislabeled "expected_roi" (actually net profit) in the decision JSON, an inline placebo RMSE-ratio loop that leaves the lifted treated series inside placebo donor pools (unlike the correct packaged placebo_in_space), and MCMC convergence checks hard-disabled with no r-hat/ESS reported anywhere. All are fixable without changing the story; the permutation logic itself and the rank-based p-value are otherwise correctly implemented and explained.

**Strengths.**
- Conceptual narration is genuinely flagship: every term defined on first use (DMA, donor pool, simplex, convex hull, Dirichlet, inverse-HHI effective donors), the why-simplex/anti-extrapolation intuition is exactly right, the assumption table maps each assumption to the cell that checks it, and the Prop 99 pointer bridges cleanly to real data.
- Depth B implements the real Abadie machinery, not a toy: pre-fit-filtered placebo spaghetti with a correct add-one permutation p (1/21), plus the scale-free post/pre RMSE-ratio rank test correctly defined ('fraction of markets, placebos + treated, at least as extreme') and matching the output (rank 1/30 = 0.033, treated ratio 6.7 vs median 1.3).
- The decision architecture is honest and pedagogically brave: a deliberately borderline TEST FURTHER (P(lift>cost)=0.62) with a break-even cost sweep and ROI posterior, rather than a manufactured GO — exactly the interval-driven lesson the README promises (even if the interval itself needs the fix in finding 1).

<details><summary>Axis notes</summary>

- **Diagnostics (4/5).** All signature SC diagnostics present (pre-fit gate, LOO donors, placebo-in-space and -in-time, scale-free RMSE-ratio rank test) and mostly well interpreted, but zero MCMC diagnostics (convergence checks hard-disabled in the estimator) and the inline ratio loop contaminates placebo donor pools with the treated series.
- **Business (4/5).** Go/no-go via P(lift>cost), a break-even cost sweep (100-600k), ROI posterior and launch-timing sensitivity are strong; but the decision IS 'test further' and no value-of-information / second-geo-test sizing is computed, and the decision JSON prints a mislabeled expected_roi.
- **Narration (4/5).** Genuinely flagship prose — simplex/convex-hull, Dirichlet, inverse-HHI, assumption-to-check table, Prop 99 bridge — docked for conflating estimand with estimator in the Identify step and for a Depth A failure-mechanism explanation that does not match the estimator as coded.
- **Validation (3/5).** Recovery plot, pre-fit gate and LOO exist, but the committed 90% interval misses the planted truth unacknowledged, and there is no multi-seed recovery stability or coverage/calibration quantification, which the repo's own four-axes bar requires.
- **Watertight (3/5).** Permutation and RMSE-ratio inference are correctly defined and the rank p-value math checks out, but truth-outside-interval unremarked, an interval that omits predictive noise, two narrative claims contradicted by committed outputs, and suppressed convergence checks fall short of 'watertight'.

</details>

- **🔴 CRITICAL · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cells 6, 8, 10, 21 outputs; src/cmp/estimators.py:287-288; PDF p.5 decision histogram`
  - **Issue.** The planted truth (EUR 339.5k total lift) lies OUTSIDE the committed 90% credible interval [EUR 279.2k, 333.0k], and the notebook never acknowledges the non-coverage. Root cause: synthetic_control builds effect_samples as target - W_post @ donors (estimators.py:287-288), so the band carries ONLY donor-weight uncertainty — the residual noise (pre-RMSE ~2.9k/week, i.e. ~13k sd over 20 post weeks, comparable to the interval's entire half-width of ~27k) is excluded. The band is a band on the mean blend, not on the counterfactual outcome.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 6 prints 'estimated total lift EUR 305k (true EUR 339k) · 90% CI [EUR 279k, EUR 333k]'; cell 20 JSON: true_total 339.48, ci90 [279.23, 332.97]. estimators.py:287-288: cf = W_post @ donors; effect = target[None, :] - cf — no observation-noise draw added, although sd is sampled in the model.
  - **Why it matters.** This is the flagship whose one-paragraph decision says 'the interval, not the point estimate, drives the decision' — yet the committed run demonstrates the interval failing its own validation criterion ('the true per-week path should sit inside the posterior band', cell 7). The decision histogram (PDF p.5) even draws the 'true' dashed line visibly outside the posterior mass. P(lift>cost)=0.62 is computed from this over-narrow posterior. A sharp audience member who reads 'true EUR 339k' next to 'CI [279, 333]' will call it out in the lecture.
  - **Fix.** Add the posterior predictive noise to the counterfactual samples (draw Normal(0, sd) per week per posterior sample) or explicitly state the band is for the mean blend and widen the decision interval accordingly; quantify and explain the ~10% downward bias instead of the unexamined 'mildly conservative' label; add a small multi-seed loop reporting recovery bias and 90%-interval coverage so non-coverage cannot pass silently (the four-axes bar explicitly requires multi-seed recovery + calibration, and this notebook has neither).
  - **Verifier.** Factual accuracy: verified against the notebook extract and source. - **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `Cell 16, line `others = np.delete(np.arange(sales.shape[0]), j)`; contrast src/cmp/estimators.py:311`
  - **Issue.** In the inline RMSE-ratio loop, each placebo unit's synthetic control is fitted from ALL other units including the treated market — whose post-period contains the real +12% lift. The packaged placebo_in_space (estimators.py:311) correctly excludes the treated unit from placebo donor pools (np.delete(..., [treated_idx, j])), and Abadie's placebo studies do the same. The two tests printed side by side in the same cell therefore use different donor-pool conventions.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 16: for j in range(sales.shape[0]): others = np.delete(np.arange(sales.shape[0]), j) — no exclusion of treated_idx for j != treated. estimators.py:311 uses others = np.delete(np.arange(n), [treated_idx, j]).
  - **Why it matters.** This is the artifact's signature inference test. Any placebo whose SLSQP weights load on the lifted treated series gets a distorted post-period gap (here biased toward inflating placebo ratios, i.e. conservative, so p=1/30 likely survives — but the mechanics are wrong, and a methods-literate attendee comparing the notebook loop to cmp.estimators would spot the inconsistency).
  - **Fix.** Exclude treated_idx from `others` whenever j != treated_idx (mirroring placebo_in_space), or refactor the ratio test into cmp.estimators next to placebo_in_space so both tests share one donor-pool convention; note in the markdown that placebo pools exclude the treated unit.
  - **Verifier.** Factually accurate: notebook 07 cell 16 fits each placebo's synthetic control with `others = np.delete(np.arange(sales.shape[0]), j)`, which leaves treated_idx (dma_00, carrying the true +12% post-launch lift) in the donor pool for every placebo j != treated; src/cmp/estimators.py:311 (placebo_in_space) instead uses `np.delete(np.arange(n), [treated_idx, j])`, excluding the treated unit, and both tests' p-values are printed side by side in the same cell (p_space=0.048 vs p_ratio=0.033). Statistically sound: Abadie-style placebo studies fit placebos from control units only — the treated unit's post-period is treatment-contaminated. - **🟠 MAJOR · business** — `Cell 10 output JSON; src/cmp/policy.py:171-175`
  - **Issue.** go_no_go labels expected net profit as ROI: roi = total_effect_samples - cost, so the printed '"expected_roi": 4.991' is EUR 4.99k of expected net value, not a return ratio. Cell 20 then defines ROI correctly as lift/cost (~1.02, 'P(ROI>1)=0.62'), so the notebook prints two irreconcilable 'ROI' numbers.

  - **Issue.** The recommendation is literally 'confirm with a second geo test', yet the notebook never prices that test: no value-of-information calculation, no sizing (how many weeks / how many treated markets would move P(lift>cost) past the 0.9 GO line), no cost of delay.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 21 ends at 'promising, confirm with a second geo test'; cells 10/20 contain only the cost sweep, ROI histogram and launch-date sensitivity. README line ~62: 'value-of-information test-sizing' listed under business decision richness.
  - **Why it matters.** The four-axes bar names value-of-information as part of business-decision richness, Anchor A (01) delivers it, and here VOI is not an optional extra — 'TEST FURTHER' is precisely a decision to buy information, so a VP's first question ('what will the second test cost vs what it resolves?') goes unanswered in the flagship program-evaluation notebook.
  - **Fix.** Add a short Depth C block: expected value of perfect information at cost 300k from the current posterior, and a simulated second-geo-test power/sizing sweep (weeks of post-period vs resulting P(lift>cost) resolution), ending in a concrete 'run X markets for Y weeks (~EUR Z) to reach a 0.9 GO/no-GO'.

- **🟠 MAJOR · consistency** — `Cell 21 (one-paragraph decision) vs cell 20 output (eff_donors 14.68) and cell 5 markdown`
  - **Issue.** The decision paragraph claims the synthetic 'leans on a handful of interpretable donors' — contradicted by the notebook's own printed metric (eff_donors = 14.68 of 29, chart titled 'Synthetic leans on ~14.7 effective donors') and by cell 5's own caveat that the Dirichlet blend is 'less individually interpretable' than classical sparse SC. It also says the estimate 'barely moves' when the launch date is nudged +/-3 weeks, while the sensitivity plot moves from 15.9 to 13.0 (~18%), a mechanical dilution the text never explains.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 20 JSON: eff_donors 14.680734; cell 6 figure title '~14.7 effective donors'; cell 5: 'more stable out-of-sample but less individually interpretable'; PDF p.9 left panel: points range ~13.0-15.9 across weeks 37-43.
  - **Why it matters.** This is the summary paragraph a lecturer would read aloud; two of its supporting claims are contradicted by the committed outputs two cells above, exactly the 'narrative numbers inconsistent with actual cell outputs' failure the repo treats as top priority.
  - **Fix.** Rewrite to match the fit actually obtained ('a regularized blend of ~15 effective donors — stable, at the cost of donor-level interpretability') and explain the launch-date sensitivity shape (mis-dating dilutes the post window with no-effect weeks, so the peak at the true launch week is itself a diagnostic).

- **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `Cell 4 ('The estimand (the precise thing we estimate)')`
  - **Issue.** The quantity displayed as 'the estimand' — tau-hat_t = Y_1t - sum_j w_j Y_jt — is the estimator. The estimand is tau_t = Y_1t(1) - Y_1t(0); the synthetic sum is the estimate of the unobserved Y_1t(0).
  - **Evidence.** Cell 4: 'The estimand (the precise thing we estimate). For each post-launch week t, the treatment effect on the treated market is tau-hat_t = Y_1t - sum_j w_j Y_jt'.
  - **Why it matters.** The 7-step contract deliberately separates identification from estimation, and the section title promises precision; a stats-literate attendee can poke 'that's your estimator, what's the estimand?' at the flagship's Identify step.
  - **Fix.** Define tau_t = Y_1t(1) - Y_1t(0) (weekly effect on the treated, t > T0) as the estimand, then introduce the synthetic sum explicitly as the estimator of Y_1t(0).

- **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `Cell 4 assumptions table`
  - **Issue.** The table omits the assumption the intro itself leans on — 'assuming those markets keep moving together' (donor blend matches the treated unit's factor loadings, which pre-fit only guarantees with a long, low-noise pre-period) — and omits 'no other shock hits the treated market at launch' (a concurrent local event would be indistinguishable from campaign lift).
  - **Evidence.** Cell 4 table rows: convex hull, good pre-fit, no anticipation, no spillover — nothing on factor-loading match or concurrent shocks; cell 0: 'assuming those markets keep moving together'.
  - **Why it matters.** For real geo-lift work the concurrent-local-shock assumption is usually the one that breaks (competitor entry, local promo, weather), and no placebo in this notebook can test it; an honest assumptions table should name it as untestable-by-design.
  - **Fix.** Add two rows: 'donors and treated keep co-moving post-launch (factor loadings matched via long pre-period)' checked by pre-period length/placebo-in-time, and 'no concurrent treated-market shock' checked only by institutional knowledge (state it as the residual leap of faith).

- **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `Cells 15-18 (Depth B reporting)`
  - **Issue.** Three reporting gaps: (a) the number of discarded placebos is never shown (p_space = 1/21 implies 9 of 29 placebos were dropped at the 5x pre-RMSE threshold — a 31% discard rate worth surfacing); (b) the two p-values use different conventions side by side — p_space is add-one permutation ((count+1)/(n+1) = 1/21 = 0.048, treated excluded from the placebo set) while p_ratio is the Abadie rank (rank/N = 1/30 = 0.033, treated included) — with no note on why the forms differ; (c) the placebo-in-time verdict 'EUR 0.9k, should be ~0' has no reference scale (vs pre-RMSE 2.86k it is fine, but the notebook doesn't say so).
  - **Evidence.** Cell 16 output: p (gap) = 0.048 = 1/21 vs estimators.py:318 add-one formula; p_ratio = 1/30 from np.sum(ratios >= treated_ratio)/len(ratios); cell 18: 'avg gap EUR 0.9k (should be ~ 0)'.
  - **Why it matters.** Depth B is the inferential heart of the notebook; a careful reader comparing 0.048 and 0.033 will wonder whether the difference is substance or convention, and 'approximately 0' claims without a yardstick are the kind of hand-waving the watertight bar excludes.
  - **Fix.** Print kept/discarded placebo counts; add one sentence noting the two p-value conventions (add-one permutation vs Abadie rank) and that both put the treated at rank 1; benchmark the in-time gap against the pre-fit RMSE (0.9k vs 2.86k, well within noise).

- **🟡 MINOR · code** — `Cell 8 (leave-one-out block)`
  - **Issue.** The LOO bars are SLSQP point refits while the 'all donors' baseline line is the Bayesian posterior-mean total (EUR 305k); all six LOO totals (309-337k) sit above the baseline, so part of the displayed 'range' is fitter mismatch (sparse SLSQP vs Dirichlet-regularized blend), not donor sensitivity. The full-pool SLSQP total is never computed for an apples-to-apples baseline.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 8: loo uses est.sc_effect_slsqp while full_total = eff_mean[post].sum() from the Bayesian fit; output: 'LOO total range EUR 309-337k around EUR 305k'.
  - **Why it matters.** The robustness claim 'no single donor drives it' is probably right, but the 28k LOO spread against a baseline from a different fitter muddies the one figure meant to demonstrate stability; note also that dropping one donor lands at 337k, essentially the truth (339k) — another unexplored hint of the main fit's downward bias.
  - **Fix.** Add the full-donor SLSQP total as the baseline for the LOO bars (keep the Bayesian line as a second reference), so lurches are measured against the same fitter.

- **⚪ POLISH · pedagogical** — `src/cmp/plots.py:118 and :131; PDF p.4 and p.7 figures`
  - **Issue.** The flagship counterfactual plot and the placebo spaghetti use generic axis labels ('outcome'/'period', 'gap vs synthetic'/'period') while every notebook-local figure is labeled in weeks and EUR 000.
  - **Evidence.** plots.py:118: ax.set_xlabel("period"); ax.set_ylabel("gap vs synthetic"); plots.py:131: ax.set_xlabel("period"); ax.set_ylabel("outcome").
  - **Why it matters.** Lecture-grade figures should carry the business units; the two most projected figures in the notebook are the only ones with placeholder labels.
  - **Fix.** Add xlabel/ylabel parameters (defaulting to current strings) and pass 'week' / 'sales (EUR 000)' from the notebook.

- **⚪ POLISH · consistency** — `PDF page 1 title; README.md:84`
  - **Issue.** Two cosmetic drifts: the PDF title renders the star emoji as '[ANCHOR] ANCHOR B' (duplicated word) on the flagship report's title page; and the README index row for 07 says 'CausalPy / manual SC' but the notebook is manual-SC only — CausalPy cannot even import on the cmp-core kernel this notebook declares (estimators.py routes causalpy to the legacy env).
  - **Evidence.** PDF p.1: '07 · Did the regional campaign work? — synthetic control [ANCHOR] ANCHOR B'; README.md:84: '| 07 | ... | CausalPy / manual SC | core |'; estimators.py _require_causalpy docstring: causalpy only in legacy env.
  - **Why it matters.** The title-page glitch is the first thing a reader of the distributed PDF sees; the README library column sets an expectation ('CausalPy') the notebook deliberately does not meet.
  - **Fix.** Strip or map the star emoji in the PDF pipeline; change the README cell to 'manual Bayesian SC (PyMC)' or add a note that the CausalPy variant lives in the legacy-env wrapper/app.
