  - **Fix.** Either implement what is promised (propagate posterior draws: for each draw s, mask_s = cate_samples[s] > cost, giving a genuine profit posterior for the model rules, plus a treat-none row) — the machinery is one line away since profit_of already accepts (S,n) masks — or trim the docstring and the nb01 bullet list to match reality.

- **🟠 MAJOR · consistency** — `src/cmp/plots.py:75,84,98,99,140,141,229 (and dgp.py:38,348 docstrings)`
  - **Issue.** Mojibake is baked into rendered figure strings: 'cumulative profit (â‚¬)' and 'â†’ â‚¬... profit' in profit_plot, 'true effect Ï„(x)' in recovery_scatter, 'low â†’ high' in calibration_by_decile, 'true ATE â‚¬..' / 'cost â‚¬..' in sensitivity_plot, ' cost â‚¬..' in decision_hist. These are double-encoded UTF-8 literals in the source (confirmed by grep), while other lines in the same file use clean '€', so every notebook that calls these helpers ships lecture figures with garbage characters on axes, titles and legends.
  - **Evidence.** grep output: plots.py:75 'ax.set_xlabel("true effect  Ï„(x)")'; plots.py:98-99 'cumulative profit (â‚¬)' and title 'â†’ â‚¬{...} profit'; plots.py:189 uses a correct '€', proving mixed encodings.
  - **Why it matters.** These helpers draw the headline figures of the anchor notebooks (profit curve, recovery scatter, sensitivity, go/no-go histogram). Projected at SDA Bocconi, axis labels reading 'â‚¬' and 'Ï„' are immediately visible and undercut the polish the business-first framing depends on.
  - **Fix.** Replace the corrupted literals with '€', 'τ', '→' (or ASCII 'EUR'/'tau'/'->'), re-render all notebooks/PDFs, and add a simple CI grep (e.g. rg 'â‚¬|Ï„|â†' src notebooks) to prevent regression.

- **🟠 MAJOR · pedagogical** — `src/cmp/dgp.py:394-408 (iv_ad_exposure) with notebooks/11 (extract 11 lines 36-44, 101-102, 139, 249-254)`
  - **Issue.** Notebook 11 makes 'What IV recovers: a LATE ... the effect for compliers, not everyone' its central concept, but the simulator plants a homogeneous effect (sales = 50 + 15*ad_exposure + ...): LATE = ATE = 15 by construction. The validation then compares the IV estimate to a truth labeled generically 'TRUE exposure→sales effect', so the recovery check cannot exhibit — and quietly papers over — the very estimand distinction the notebook teaches; a student can fairly ask 'if IV only speaks for compliers, why do you grade it against the population effect?'
  - **Evidence.** dgp.py:405 'sales = 50 + true_effect * ad_exposure + 12 * engagement + ...' (constant true_effect); extract 11 line 38: 'IV does not give the average effect over everyone. It gives the LATE'; line 139 validates against 'true €15'.
  - **Why it matters.** The task's own estimand-match test (ATE vs LATE): as built, the notebook asserts LATE-not-ATE as a caveat but demonstrates a world where the distinction is vacuous, weakening the strongest conceptual point of the IV lecture and inviting the exact hole-poke the bar warns about.
  - **Fix.** Give compliers a different effect (e.g. draw a complier/always/never type from engagement, with tau=20 for compliers and 8 for always-takers), return both true_ate and true_late from the DGP, and have the notebook show IV landing on true_late while missing true_ate — turning the caveat into a demonstrated result.

- **🟡 MINOR · consistency** — `notebooks/01_uplift_targeting.ipynb cell 19 (extract 01 lines 585, 591-599)`
  - **Issue.** print(comp.round(0)) destroys the frac_contacted column of the policy table: the committed output shows random-50% contacting '1.0' (rounded from ~0.51) and both model rules and the oracle contacting '0.0' (rounded from ~0.26), directly contradicting the very next printed sentence 'targeting 236 of 900 customers'.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 19 output: 'model (P>conf)  2681.0  0.0' followed by '... targeting 236 of 900 customers.'
  - **Why it matters.** A decision table asserting the chosen policy contacts 0% of the base while earning €2,681 is self-contradictory on a lecture slide, even though the underlying numbers are right.
  - **Fix.** Format columns separately (profit round(0), frac_contacted round(2) or as percent), or have policy_comparison return frac_contacted as a percentage string; re-commit the output.

- **🟡 MINOR · code** — `src/cmp/policy.py:23 (profit_curve) and :44-47 (cost_sweep)`
  - **Issue.** stop = argmax(cumsum) forces at least one contact: when every increment is negative (cost above the top CATE), cumsum is monotone decreasing, argmax returns index 0, and the 'optimal' policy is reported as contacting 1/n of the base at a negative profit instead of the true optimum of contacting nobody at 0. cost_sweep inherits this, so its opt_profit curve can never touch the 0 floor and opt_frac never reaches 0.
  - **Evidence.** policy.py:22-24: 'cum_profit = np.cumsum(...); stop = int(np.argmax(cum_profit))' — no comparison against the empty policy. In nb01's sweep (costs 2-20) the peak stays positive so the committed figures are unaffected, but the boundary behavior is wrong.
  - **Why it matters.** The functions' contract is 'the optimal stopping point'; for high-cost scenarios (exactly the region a cost sweep is meant to stress) they report a strictly dominated policy, which would misteach the 'when do we stop mailing entirely' boundary.
  - **Fix.** Prepend 0 to the cumulative profit (cum = np.concatenate([[0.0], np.cumsum(...)])), take argmax over that, and map stop=0 to frac=0 / profit=0; same in cost_sweep.

- **🟡 MINOR · consistency** — `notebooks/02_segment_effects.ipynb cells 2 and 8 (extract 02 lines 56-59, 167) vs dgp.py:142-152`
  - **Issue.** nb02's narrative says the email 'lifts low-value customers by €3 and high-value by €12 at average engagement, plus a smooth +€8 x engagement slope on top' and later 'Segment CATEs vs the planted €3 / €12' — but €3/€12 are the effects at engagement = 0; at average engagement (0.5) the truths are €7/€16, which is exactly what the code prints ('TRUE segment-average effects (at mean engagement): {low: 7.0, high: 16.0}') and validates against (cell 9: 'true 7.0', 'true 16.0').
  - **Evidence.** tau = 3 + 9*is_high + 8*engagement (dgp.py:144); extract 02 line 78 prints 7.0/16.0 two lines below the €3/€12-at-average-engagement claim.
  - **Why it matters.** Stating the same quantity two ways within one screen ('€3/€12 at average engagement' vs 'true 7.0/16.0 at mean engagement') double-counts the engagement slope in the prose and will trip a careful reader in the moderation notebook whose whole point is getting the conditioning right.
  - **Fix.** Reword cells 2 and 8: '€3 (low) / €12 (high) at zero engagement, plus +€8 x engagement — i.e. €7 / €16 for the average (engagement = 0.5) customer.' The dgp code and returned true_effect dict are already correct.

- **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `notebooks/07_geo_lift_synthetic_control.ipynb cells 6-8 (extract 07 lines 196-259)`
  - **Issue.** The committed 90% credible interval for total lift, [€279k, €333k], excludes the planted truth (€339k), yet Step 5's narrative frames recovery as successful ('the estimated total near the planted truth', 'pre-launch gap ~0 = good fit') and never remarks that the interval misses. The SC posterior here reflects only weight uncertainty around a conservative simplex fit (point estimate 305 vs truth 339, ~10% low), under FAST sampling.
  - **Evidence.** Cell 6 output: 'estimated total lift €305k (true €339k) · 90% CI [€279k, €333k]'.
  - **Why it matters.** Anchor B's validation step is supposed to model honest calibration; a 90% interval that excludes the notebook's own planted truth, praised as good recovery, is exactly the miscalibration the four-axes bar says must be surfaced, and a sharp attendee will read the two numbers off the same line.
  - **Fix.** Add one honest sentence quantifying it (point estimate ~10% low, interval misses the truth — the simplex constraint is conservative and the band conditions on the fitted model), ideally paired with a multi-seed coverage check of the SC interval; or re-commit a non-FAST run if coverage recovers there.

- **🟡 MINOR · code** — `src/cmp/data.py:16,75-76 and notebooks/05 cell 14 (extract 05 lines 286-292)`
  - **Issue.** Three small loader-layer gaps: (a) LALONDE_NSW_URL (the Dehejia .dta experimental file) is defined but used by nothing, implying an experimental-benchmark path that does not exist; (b) the Hillstrom fetch is plain http:// (no TLS); (c) nb05's real-data cell hard-codes the annotation '(recovers the ~$1,800 experimental truth)' into the f-string, so it will print regardless of what adj2 actually is — on the robjellis/MatchIt sample (185 NSW treated vs 429 PSID controls, verified live) OLS adjustment typically lands nearer $1,300-1,600, and the committed repo has never executed this gated cell to check.
  - **Evidence.** data.py defines LALONDE_NSW_URL at :75, never referenced; verified CSV header 'ID,treat,age,educ,black,hispan,married,nodegree,re74,re75,re78' matches nb05's covariate list; nb05 cell 14 f-string embeds the claim as static text.
  - **Why it matters.** If the lecturer flips CMP_REAL=1 live, the cell may print e.g. '$1,485 (recovers the ~$1,800 experimental truth)' — a self-refuting line in front of the audience; and the dead URL suggests an unfinished experimental-vs-observational comparison.
  - **Fix.** Run the gated cell once and soften the annotation to a computed comparison (print the number and separately 'experimental benchmark ~ $1,800'), make the claim conditional on the value, either wire up load_nsw_experimental() using LALONDE_NSW_URL or delete the constant, and switch Hillstrom to an https mirror or note why http is unavoidable.

- **⚪ POLISH · code** — `src/cmp/plots.py:72-74 (recovery_scatter)`
  - **Issue.** Axis limits are computed from tau_true only ([min-3, max+3]) and applied to both axes, so estimated CATEs outside the truth's range are silently cropped out of the recovery plot — the one diagnostic whose job is to expose exactly such estimator failures (e.g. a T-learner extrapolating wildly in thin-overlap regions).
  - **Evidence.** plots.py:72-74: 'lim = [tau_true.min() - 3, tau_true.max() + 3]; ax.plot(lim, lim, ...); ax.set_xlim(lim); ax.set_ylim(lim)'.
  - **Why it matters.** A recovery scatter that clips outliers can make a badly-behaved estimator look acceptable; in the committed FAST outputs nothing is visibly cropped, but the default is unsafe for the toolkit's reuse promise.
  - **Fix.** Set y-limits from the union of truth and all estimate arrays (with the 45-degree line still spanning the truth range), or at least annotate 'k points outside view' when clipping occurs.

---

### Tests, CI, build & reports infrastructure

**Grade: adequate** · 1 critical · 6 major · 10 findings total

The test/build design is genuinely well-conceived — a single pytest process routes each notebook to its declared kernel across two environments with CMP_FAST forced, and test_package.py contains a thoughtful statistical gotcha-guard suite — but the automated safety net does not actually exist: the GitHub Actions workflow can never run (it sits in a subfolder of the sda_projects monorepo, not the git root; it triggers on 'main' while the default branch is 'master'; and even relocated it would fail because 'uv sync' never installs the dev extra containing pytest). Every green result to date is a local, hand-patched-venv run. Around that dead CI sit several silent-pass paths: missing kernels skip instead of fail, there is no kernelspec-drift regression guard despite a documented past incident, notebooks contain zero assertions so FAST runs test only executability, the legacy stack (5 of 12 notebooks) has no unit tests and no lockfile, and the lecture PDFs are generated from committed FAST-mode outputs while the report pipeline strips the very arviz warnings that would disclose under-sampling.

**Strengths.**
- Dual-kernel routing in tests/test_notebooks.py is elegant and correct: nbclient launches each notebook's declared kernel as a subprocess, so one pytest process really does drive both pymc>=6 and pymc<6 environments; CMP_FAST=1 is forced at module import (line 18) so spawned kernels inherit it, and ci.yml sets it again explicitly (belt and braces).
- tests/test_package.py is unusually thoughtful for a smoke suite: the BART frozen-CATE 'gotcha guard' (lines 49-61) asserts a known-nonzero effect is actually recovered, protecting the repo's #1 silent-failure mode (all-zero CATEs if sample_vars regresses); BCF, synthetic control, AIPW, first-stage F, McCrary, coverage, AUUC and policy-oracle tests give real statistical coverage of the core env on tiny sampling budgets.
- All 12 notebooks currently declare the correct kernelspec per the documented env split (00-05, 07 -> cmp-core; 06, 08-11 -> cmp-legacy) — verified by direct inspection of every notebook's metadata.
- scripts/make_reports.py can never silently drop figures or tracebacks: execute_result, display_data and error outputs are kept unconditionally (only stream outputs are filtered), and the xelatex glyph-drop problem is handled with a documented replacement map that correctly orders multi-codepoint keys before single ones.
- The core environment is properly locked (uv.lock committed) and pyproject.toml documents the pymc 5/6 ecosystem split rationale inline, including why requirements-legacy.txt is deliberately kept out of the resolver.

- **🔴 CRITICAL · code — ✅ verified** — `.github/workflows/ci.yml:1-7 (file location + trigger), relative to git root /Users/fmuia/.../sda_projects`
  - **Issue.** The CI workflow can never execute, for three independent reasons: (1) the git repository root is the parent monorepo sda_projects (confirmed via git rev-parse --show-toplevel), and GitHub Actions only reads workflows from the repo root's .github/workflows/ — there is none there; this file sits in the causal-marketing-pymc/ subfolder where GitHub ignores it. (2) The push trigger is 'branches: [main]' but the repo's only branch is 'master' (recent commits, including the lecture-content ones, went straight to master), so even a relocated workflow would not fire on push. (3) All steps assume the project is at the repo root ('uv sync', 'pytest tests/...') with no working-directory: causal-marketing-pymc, so a relocated workflow would fail immediately.
  - **Evidence.** git rev-parse --show-toplevel returns .../sda_projects; ls sda_projects/.github/workflows -> does not exist; git branch -a shows only master / origin/master; ci.yml lines 3-5 read 'on: push: branches: [main]'; commit 2b8c172 'Flatten causal-marketing-pymc from accidental submodule into monorepo folder' is when the workflow became unreachable.
  - **Why it matters.** The entire premise that 'CI executes every notebook headless across both environments' is currently fiction — no automation has ever run this suite. The only thing standing between a broken notebook and the SDA Bocconi lecture is remembering to run 'make test' locally. The 'Full suite 30/30 green' claims in commit messages are all local runs with no independent verification.
  - **Fix.** Move the workflow to sda_projects/.github/workflows/ci.yml, change the push trigger to [master] (and add paths: ['causal-marketing-pymc/**'] so unrelated monorepo pushes don't run it), and set 'defaults: run: working-directory: causal-marketing-pymc' on both jobs. Then confirm one green run on GitHub before the lecture.
  - **Verifier.** All three factual legs verified by direct inspection. (1) git rev-parse --show-toplevel returns .../sda_projects; no .github directory exists at that root; the only ci.yml is at causal-marketing-pymc/.github/workflows/ci.yml, which GitHub Actions ignores (workflows are only discovered at the repo root). Independently confirmed via `gh workflow list` and `gh run list` on fmuia/sda_projects: both empty — zero workflows registered, zero runs ever. The flatten commit 2b8c172 even states the folder was previously a submodule pointer to an UNPUSHED commit, so CI could not have run pre-flatten either. (2) ci.yml lines 3-5 read `on: push: branches: [main]` while the only branch is master (git branch…

- **🟠 MAJOR · code — ✅ verified** — `.github/workflows/ci.yml:20-22 and 37/54; pyproject.toml:33-37; Makefile:48-52; README Quickstart`
  - **Issue.** pytest and nbmake live in [project.optional-dependencies].dev, which plain 'uv sync' does NOT install (uv only auto-installs [dependency-groups], not optional extras). Both CI jobs run 'uv sync' then 'uv run pytest', so even once the workflow is relocated, both jobs fail with pytest missing. The same gap breaks the documented onboarding path: README Quickstart says 'uv sync' then 'make test', but 'make test' calls .venv/bin/python -m pytest, which a fresh clone would not have. The local .venv does contain pytest (verified: .venv/bin/pytest exists), which means it was installed by an undocumented manual step — the local 30/30-green result is not reproducible from the documented commands.
  - **Evidence.** pyproject.toml lines 33-37 put pytest/nbmake under [project.optional-dependencies].dev; uv.lock lines 305/312 carry marker "extra == 'dev'" for both, confirming they are not part of a default sync; ci.yml line 21 runs bare 'uv sync' and lines 22/54 then invoke pytest; Makefile:49 runs $(CORE)/python -m pytest.
  - **Why it matters.** A fresh machine (a colleague, the lecture laptop, or the CI runner) following the README exactly cannot run the test suite at all. The reproducibility story ('uv.lock + make test') silently depends on an off-book install.
  - **Fix.** Move pytest/nbmake (and the test-critical nbclient/nbformat/jupyter_client, currently only transitive via the 'jupyter' metapackage) into [dependency-groups].dev, which 'uv sync' installs by default — or add '--extra dev' to the uv sync calls in ci.yml, 'make env', and the README Quickstart.
  - **Verifier.** Every cited fact verifies: pyproject.toml:33-37 puts pytest/nbmake under [project.optional-dependencies].dev with no [dependency-groups] table; uv.lock lines 305/312 gate both behind marker "extra == 'dev'"; ci.yml lines 20/37 run bare 'uv sync' and lines 22/54 then invoke pytest via 'uv run'; Makefile 'test' target (line 49) calls .venv/bin/python -m pytest while 'make env' is a bare 'uv sync'; README Quickstart documents uv sync → make test with no dev-extra step. The uv semantics claim is correct and I confirmed it empirically read-only: 'uv sync --python 3.12 --dry-run' in the repo reports "Would uninstall 4 packages: nbmake==1.5.5, pytest==9.1.1" — plain uv sync would not only skip thes…
  - **Corrected statement.** The finding is accurate as written; if anything it understates the problem: plain 'uv sync' would actively uninstall the ad-hoc pytest 9.1.1/nbmake 1.5.5 from the existing local .venv (verified via 'uv sync --dry-run': "Would uninstall ... nbmake==1.5.5, pytest==9.1.1"), and the locally installed pytest 9.1.1 violates the pyproject dev constraint pytest>=8.3,<9, confirming it was installed outside the locked, documented path.

- **🟠 MAJOR · code — ✅ verified** — `tests/test_notebooks.py:29-33`
  - **Issue.** If a notebook's kernel is not registered, the test calls pytest.skip rather than fail. There is no guard — in CI or in 'make test' — asserting that zero notebook tests were skipped. If cmp-legacy registration is missing or misnamed, the 5 legacy notebooks (06, 08-11) silently skip and the suite exits 0; with 'pytest -q' the only trace is a lowercase 's' in the progress line. A 'green' run is therefore indistinguishable from a run that never executed 40% of the lecture notebooks.
  - **Evidence.** test_notebooks.py lines 29-33: 'if kernel not in AVAILABLE_KERNELS: pytest.skip(...)'. ci.yml line 54 runs 'pytest tests/test_notebooks.py -q' with no --strict skip policy, no skip-count check; the Makefile test target likewise.
  - **Why it matters.** Skip-on-missing-kernel is the right ergonomics for a laptop but the wrong default for the gate that decides 'the lecture material runs'. This is precisely the path by which a broken legacy notebook (the CausalPy DiD/RDD/ITS/IV set) reaches the lecture with a green checkmark.
  - **Fix.** Gate the skip on an env var: in CI (and in 'make test'), set e.g. CMP_REQUIRE_KERNELS=1 and turn the skip into pytest.fail; alternatively add a session-scoped fixture that asserts {'cmp-core','cmp-legacy'} <= AVAILABLE_KERNELS when the var is set.
  - **Verifier.** Factual claims verified against the artifacts: tests/test_notebooks.py:29-33 contains exactly the cited pytest.skip on missing kernel; there is no conftest.py, pytest.ini, or [tool.pytest.ini_options] anywhere in the repo, so no skip-count guard exists; ci.yml:54 runs 'pytest tests/test_notebooks.py -q' with no skip policy; the Makefile 'test' target runs 'pytest tests/ -v' and does not even depend on 'make kernels', so a fresh clone would skip ALL 12 notebooks locally and still exit green — the finding is understated for the local path. Legacy notebooks 06, 08-11 = 5/12 ≈ 42%, matching the '40%' claim. The CI kernel-registration step (ci.yml:46-49) fails hard if ipykernel install errors, wh…
  - **Corrected statement.** Minor correction only: with 'pytest -q' the skips are visible both as 's' characters in the progress line and in the final summary line (e.g. '7 passed, 5 skipped'), but neither affects the exit code, so the core claim — a green run is indistinguishable by exit status from one that never executed the 5 legacy notebooks — is correct. Additionally, the local 'make test' path is worse than stated: it does not depend on 'make kernels', so on a machine where kernels were never registered all 12 notebook tests skip and the suite still passes.

- **🟠 MAJOR · consistency** — `tests/ (missing test); incident: commit 152524c; test_notebooks.py:27-34`
  - **Issue.** There is no regression guard for kernelspec drift, despite a documented past incident (commit 152524c: 'nbclient had rewritten it to python3/.venv, breaking cmp import'). Nothing asserts that each notebook's declared kernelspec matches the env-split contract (00-05,07 -> cmp-core; 06,08-11 -> cmp-legacy). If a tool rewrites a kernelspec to 'python3' again, test_notebooks.py will happily route it there: a 'python3' kernel exists both inside .venv/share/jupyter/kernels and at user level (~/Library/Jupyter/kernels/python3 — verified present), so AVAILABLE_KERNELS contains it and a drifted core notebook executes and passes silently. Worse, KernelSpecManager gives user-level kernels precedence, so the drifted notebook could run against whatever unrelated environment the user-level 'python3' kernel points to.
  - **Evidence.** Commit 152524c message describes the exact incident; test_notebooks.py line 28 falls back to whatever name the notebook declares ('python3' default); ls .venv/share/jupyter/kernels -> python3; ls ~/Library/Jupyter/kernels -> includes python3 plus six unrelated project kernels.
  - **Why it matters.** This is a known, already-materialized failure mode with zero protection. The failure is silent in tests but loud at the lecture: the notebook opens in Jupyter asking for a kernel that doesn't exist on the presentation machine, or runs against the wrong pymc major.
  - **Fix.** Add a ~10-line test (no kernel launch, pure metadata) that hard-codes the mapping {00-05,07: 'cmp-core', 06,08-11: 'cmp-legacy'} and fails on any mismatch, including a drift to 'python3'. This also documents the env split in executable form.

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `tests/test_notebooks.py:34-35; all 12 notebooks (0 assert statements); src/cmp/estimators.py:329-407 untested`
  - **Issue.** FAST-mode notebook runs test executability only, not statistical content: NotebookClient.execute() surfaces exceptions, and a scan of all 12 notebooks finds exactly zero 'assert' statements in code cells — every recover-the-truth and calibration result is printed, never enforced. A regression that flips an estimator's sign, freezes an effect at zero (outside the two BART learners covered by test_package.py), or breaks calibration would still be '30/30 green'. Compounding this, the entire legacy stack has no unit tests at all: the CausalPy wrappers in src/cmp/estimators.py lines 329-407 (synthetic_control_cp, did, rdd, its, iv) are never imported by tests/test_package.py (which runs only in the core env), so notebooks 06 and 08-11 — five of twelve lecture notebooks — are validated solely by 'the notebook did not raise'.
  - **Evidence.** grep for '^\s*assert' across all notebook code cells returns 0 hits in all 12 notebooks; test_notebooks.py line 35 comment: 'raises CellExecutionError on any cell failure' (the only check); tests/ contains no legacy-env test file and no causalpy import (grep confirms); test_package.py docstring says core env, pymc>=6.
  - **Why it matters.** The repo's stated bar is watertight statistics with recover-the-truth validation, but the test suite cannot detect a statistically wrong answer, only a crash. For the legacy half of the toolkit even the estimator layer is unguarded — e.g. a formula or argument-passing bug in the did/rdd/iv wrappers that still returns a fitted object would sail through.
  - **Fix.** Two cheap additions: (1) put wide-tolerance sanity asserts in each notebook's validation step (e.g. 'assert sign(ate_hat) == sign(true_ate)' and truth-within-3-posterior-SD), tolerant enough for FAST budgets but fatal to sign flips and frozen-zero regressions; (2) add tests/test_package_legacy.py exercising the five CausalPy wrappers on tiny seeded DGPs, run in CI with .venv-legacy/bin/python -m pytest.
  - **Verifier.** Every factual claim verifies against the artifacts. (1) Programmatic parse of all 12 notebooks' code cells finds 0 assert statements, and no alternative enforcement (np.testing, raise-on-value, sys.exit) exists in validation cells — recover-the-truth results are printed/plotted only. (2) tests/test_notebooks.py:34-35 is exactly as cited: NotebookClient.execute() with the comment 'raises CellExecutionError on any cell failure' is the only check; no output inspection. (3) src/cmp/estimators.py:329-407 are precisely the five CausalPy wrappers (synthetic_control_cp, did, rdd, its, iv); tests/ has no legacy test file, no causalpy call (only a docstring mention in test_notebooks.py), and the lazy …
  - **Corrected statement.** The finding stands as written, with one refinement: frozen-zero/sign regressions at the estimator level are guarded in the core env not only for the two BART learners but also for bcf, the core-env synthetic_control, and aipw_ate (test_package.py lines 64-83, 147-151). The unguarded surface is exactly (a) all 12 notebooks' statistical outputs (0 asserts; execute-only testing) and (b) the entire legacy stack — the five CausalPy wrappers in src/cmp/estimators.py:329-407 have zero unit tests in any environment, so notebooks 06 and 08-11 are validated solely by absence of exceptions.

- **🟠 MAJOR · consistency** — `notebooks/01_uplift_targeting.ipynb committed outputs (cells ~11-24); scripts/make_reports.py:34-36 and 66-68; README 'FAST vs full' (~line 121); Makefile:54-55`
  - **Issue.** The committed 'reference' outputs are FAST-mode runs, the PDFs are rendered from those committed outputs, and the report pipeline strips exactly the warnings that would disclose it. Notebook 01's committed outputs show "FAST=True ... {'draws': 140, 'tune': 140, 'chains': 2, 'm': 30}" and a dozen arviz warnings 'Only 80 samples per chain. Reliable r-hat and ESS diagnostics require longer chains for accurate estimate'; notebook 07 shows FAST=True with draws=600. make_reports.py drops all stderr streams (line 67) and its NOISE regex additionally matches 'Only', 'The rhat', 'The effective', 'There were' (lines 34-36), so the lecture PDF presents under-sampled numbers — including 01's validation line '90% coverage 76%' for a nominal 90% interval — with every disclosing warning removed. This contradicts the README's claim that CMP_FAST=0 'reproduce[s] the reference figures' (the committed reference outputs are themselves FAST). There is also no staleness gate: 'make reports' never executes notebooks and has no dependency tracking, and right now reports/02_segment_effects.pdf (mtime 1783376235) is older than the modified notebooks/02_segment_effects.ipynb (mtime 1783377064).
  - **Evidence.** Committed stream output in 01: "FAST=True  N=900  sampling={'draws': 140, 'tune': 140, 'chains': 2, 'm': 30}" and repeated 'Only 80/90 samples per chain...' stderr lines (cells 17, 24); 01 cell 15 output 'PEHE €6.34 · ... 90% coverage 76%'; make_reports.py line 67 skips all stderr, NOISE regex line 34-36 matches the warning prefixes; mtime comparison shows 02 PDF predates the notebook edit.
  - **Why it matters.** The PDFs are the lecture-facing artifact. Shipping a calibration table where a 90% interval covers 76% — an artifact of 140-draw FAST sampling, not of the method — with the small-sample warnings scrubbed, is exactly the kind of thing a sharp MBA quant will poke at; and the stale-02 case shows edited narrative can silently coexist with old numbers in the PDF.
  - **Fix.** Make 'make reports' (or a 'make reports-full' variant) re-execute each notebook with CMP_FAST=0 on its declared kernel before rendering — or at minimum have make_reports.py refuse (or loudly watermark 'FAST DRAFT') when any committed output contains the FAST=True banner or an 'Only N samples per chain' warning, and fail when a notebook's mtime is newer than its PDF.

- **🟠 MAJOR · code — ✅ verified** — `requirements-legacy.txt:7-9; .github/workflows/ci.yml:39-44 vs Makefile:23-26`
  - **Issue.** The legacy environment — which powers 5 of 12 notebooks — has no lockfile and its ranges span known API-breaking releases: 'pymc-marketing>=0.15,<0.20' covers five minor versions of a fast-moving library and 'causalpy>=0.8,<0.9' any 0.8.x, while the README documents the specific working versions (causalpy 0.8.1, pymc-marketing 0.19.4) that nothing actually records. A lecture-morning rebuild on a new machine can resolve different versions than every committed output was produced with. Separately, CI's legacy build diverges from the local one: ci.yml line 43 additionally installs a completely unpinned 'pymc-marketing[dag]' (no version bound at all — if pymc-marketing's latest ever moves to pymc>=6, this step corrupts the legacy env), and installs graphviz system deps; the Makefile env-legacy target installs neither, so 'works in CI' and 'works locally' are not the same environment.
  - **Evidence.** requirements-legacy.txt lines 7-9 (ranges only, no ==); no lock/constraints file for .venv-legacy exists in the repo; ci.yml line 43: uv pip install "pymc-marketing[dag]" with no specifier; Makefile env-legacy (lines 23-26) has no [dag] extra and no graphviz; README Environment split section names 0.8.1 / 0.19.4 as the working versions.
  - **Why it matters.** The core env has uv.lock discipline; the legacy env has none. Reproducibility of nearly half the lecture notebooks rests on PyPI not having published anything new — the exact risk lockfiles exist to eliminate. The CI/Makefile divergence means the (currently dead) CI wouldn't even validate the environment a presenter builds with 'make env-legacy'.
  - **Fix.** Freeze the known-good legacy env: 'uv pip compile requirements-legacy.txt -o requirements-legacy.lock' (or pin == versions directly: pymc==5.x.y, causalpy==0.8.1, pymc-marketing==0.19.4) and install from the lock in both Makefile and CI; make the two install paths identical, moving the [dag] extra (pinned) into requirements-legacy.txt if any notebook needs it, or deleting it from CI if none does.
  - **Verifier.** Every factual citation verified: requirements-legacy.txt:7-9 contains only ranges (pymc>=5.15.1,<6; causalpy>=0.8,<0.9; pymc-marketing>=0.15,<0.20) with no lockfile — the repo's uv.lock covers only the core env since the legacy requirements are deliberately kept out of pyproject.toml (per the file's own header). README line 178 documents causalpy 0.8.1 / pymc-marketing 0.19.4 as the working versions, and the local .venv-legacy indeed contains exactly those dist-infos, but nothing machine-readable records them. ci.yml line 43 installs an unpinned "pymc-marketing[dag]" plus system graphviz (lines 29-30), while Makefile env-legacy (lines 23-26) installs neither — and this divergence is MORE sev…
  - **Corrected statement.** The legacy env (5 of 12 notebooks) has no lockfile: requirements-legacy.txt:7-9 gives only ranges spanning API-breaking releases (pymc-marketing>=0.15,<0.20 even predates the dag= MMM API notebook 06 uses; causalpy>=0.8,<0.9), while the known-good versions (causalpy 0.8.1, pymc-marketing 0.19.4) live only in README prose. CI (ci.yml:39-44) and Makefile env-legacy (lines 23-26) diverge: CI additionally installs "pymc-marketing[dag]" (unpinned, though uv would keep the already-installed <0.20 version rather than upgrade it, so outright env corruption is unlikely — the extra's own deps do resolve unbounded) plus system graphviz; the Makefile installs neither, yet notebook 06 requires the [dag] extra (dowhy/pygraphviz — present in the author's actual .venv-legacy but not installed by any committed target). A fresh `make env-legacy` therefore builds an environment in which notebook 06 fails today. Fix: compile a legacy lockfile or pin ==, add the pinned [dag] extra to requirements-legacy.txt, and make CI and Makefile install identically.

- **🟡 MINOR · code** — `scripts/make_reports.py:34-36 (NOISE regex)`
  - **Issue.** The stream-output noise filter matches overly generic line-start tokens — bare '>', 'Only', 'Chain', 'Computing', 'took', 'Sampling' — via NOISE.match(). Any future legitimate printed result line beginning with one of these (e.g. 'Only 12% of customers have positive uplift', 'Computing break-even at cost=...') would be silently deleted from the lecture PDF with no warning. A scan of current committed outputs confirms only sampler noise is affected today, but the pipeline's whole job is faithfulness and it fails open.
  - **Evidence.** make_reports.py lines 34-36: alternation includes '>', 'Only', 'Chain', 'Computing', 'took'; scan of all 12 notebooks' stdout streams found 59 lines matching NOISE, all currently sampler-related (e.g. '>CompoundStep', '>>PGBART: [prog]').
  - **Why it matters.** Silent content loss in the report generator is the one failure mode a narrative-PDF pipeline must not have; the failure would only be caught by a human diffing PDF against notebook.
  - **Fix.** Anchor the patterns to what they actually target (e.g. r'^>+\s*(CompoundStep|NUTS|PGBART)', r'^Only \d+ samples per chain', r'^Chain \d', r'^Sampling(\s|:)', r'took \d+ seconds') and log a per-notebook count of dropped lines so unexpected drops are visible in the make output.

- **🟡 MINOR · code** — `Makefile:57-58 (clean target)`
  - **Issue.** 'rm -rf .pytest_cache **/__pycache__ ...' relies on globstar, but make runs recipes under /bin/sh where '**' behaves like '*'; nested __pycache__ directories (e.g. src/cmp/__pycache__, tests/__pycache__) are never removed.
  - **Evidence.** Makefile line 58; make's default SHELL is /bin/sh (no globstar).
  - **Why it matters.** Stale bytecode across the pymc5/pymc6 env boundary is exactly the kind of thing that produces confusing import behavior when switching kernels; a clean target that doesn't clean invites it.
  - **Fix.** Use 'find . -name __pycache__ -type d -prune -exec rm -rf {} +' (and consider adding .venv exclusions), or set 'SHELL := /bin/bash' plus 'shopt -s globstar' — the find form is simpler.

- **⚪ POLISH · code** — `pyproject.toml:35 (nbmake); tests/test_notebooks.py:13-16 (undeclared direct imports)`
  - **Issue.** nbmake is declared in the dev extra but unused — tests drive nbclient directly. Meanwhile the packages the test suite actually imports (nbformat, nbclient, jupyter_client) are not declared anywhere and arrive only transitively via the heavyweight 'jupyter' metapackage in the runtime dependencies.
  - **Evidence.** pyproject.toml line 35 'nbmake>=1.5,<2'; grep shows no nbmake usage in tests/, Makefile, or ci.yml; test_notebooks.py imports nbformat, nbclient, jupyter_client.kernelspec directly.
  - **Why it matters.** If 'jupyter' is ever slimmed (it's only needed for interactive use) the test suite breaks for a non-obvious reason; the vestigial nbmake suggests an abandoned approach and confuses readers about how notebooks are tested.
  - **Fix.** Drop nbmake; declare nbformat/nbclient/jupyter-client explicitly in the dev group so the test suite's dependencies are self-documenting.

---

### marimo apps (3)

**Grade: adequate** · 2 critical · 4 major · 12 findings total

The three marimo apps are architecturally sound — the reactive DAG genuinely guarantees the expensive step runs once in the uplift and confounding apps, the VOI math is a correct per-customer EVPI, and the placebo permutation p is proper Abadie inference with the +1 correction and RMSE filter. But as committed they are not lecture-ready: the confounding and synthetic-control apps never display their figures (their plot cells end on fig.tight_layout(), which returns None, and no cell outputs fig — confirmed by the committed marimo session snapshots, where the plot cell rendered empty), so two of three demos show only text. The third app's headline decision table glues together numbers from two different policies (confidence-rule count 243 vs ranking-policy stop 28%=280, plus a profit figure realised on the simulation truth with an oracle-chosen stop, unlabelled). Several deeper statistical wrinkles — a seed artifact inflating the confounding app's tipping-point story, the treated market left in the SC donor/placebo pools, and a hard-coded coarse BCF posterior that inflates the straddler count to 619/1000 — are each the kind of hole a sharp MBA audience member could poke. All are fixable in hours; the underlying cmp machinery is largely watertight.

**Strengths.**
- Reactive dependency structure verified: in uplift_policy_explorer.py the BCF cell (lines 42-53) and in confounding_sensitivity.py the drift-curve cell (lines 44-64) depend only on imports, never on sliders, so marimo's DAG guarantees the expensive step runs exactly once — the README's 'posterior once, sliders re-derive the decision' claim holds structurally for these two apps.
- Value-of-information is a correct per-customer EVPI: E[max(tau-c,0)] - max(E[tau]-c, 0) (src/cmp/policy.py:64-88), and the committed snapshot confirms the claimed concentration on straddlers (EUR 337 of EUR 345 total) — a genuinely good decision-theoretic demo.
- Placebo inference is done properly: placebo_in_space (src/cmp/estimators.py:299-322) uses the Abadie 3x pre-RMSE filter, excludes the treated unit from placebo donor pools, and computes p = (#{|placebo| >= |real|}+1)/(n+1) with the correct +1 permutation adjustment; measured specificity holds (p=0.150 and 0.550 for two non-treated market selections, p=0.053 for the real one).
- App-notebook consistency is strong: same DGPs and seeds (uplift seed=7, geo seed=3), same EUR 8 cost, same 0-12 confounder-strength range and identical adjusted_ate OLS as notebook 01 cell 28; the SC app explicitly labels the SLSQP fitter as the fast stand-in for notebook 07's Bayesian version.
- Live-demo robustness of inputs is good: the heaviest interaction (SC fit + 29 placebo refits) measured 0.22 s; the market dropdown cannot be cleared to None (value provided, so allow_select_none is False); slider edge values (c=20, conf=0.95, base=200, launch=50) degrade gracefully with no crash paths found.

  - **Verifier.** Factual claims verified by direct reading. (1) apps/uplift_policy_explorer.py line 77 computes `mask` via policy.target_set(cate_s, c, confidence=conf) — the P(tau>c)>conf rule — while line 78 computes `frac, cum, stop` via policy.profit_curve(point_s, tau_s, c), whose signature (src/cmp/policy.py:13-24) takes no confidence argument: stop = argmax of cumulative realised profit under rank-by-posterior-mean, so frac[stop] and cum[stop] are provably independent of the confidence slider. - **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `apps/uplift_policy_explorer.py:78,103 with src/cmp/policy.py:13-24`
  - **Issue.** 'Profit at optimal stop EUR 2,902' is doubly oracle-informed but presented as the decision output: profit_curve realises profit on the true simulated tau (tau_true - cost per contact) AND chooses the stop as argmax of that realised curve — a stopping point only knowable with ground truth. The app never says this number is a validation-against-known-truth quantity rather than an achievable forecast.
  - **Evidence.** policy.profit_curve: cum_profit = np.cumsum(tau_true[order] - cost); stop = int(np.argmax(cum_profit)) — both use tau_true. App passes tau_s (the simulator's true effects) at line 78 and reports cum[stop] at line 103 under 'Decision at cost EUR 8'.
  - **Why it matters.** In the notebooks, truth-realised evaluation lives in the explicit 'validate' step; in the app it sits in a table headed 'Decision at cost EUR 8'. It also inflates the model policy relative to what deployment would deliver (deployment must pick the stop from predicted profit).
  - **Fix.** Label the row 'realised profit vs simulated ground truth (validation)' and add the deployable counterpart: choose the stop from the predicted curve cumsum(sorted_cate_point - c) and report realised profit at that stop, so the audience sees model-chosen stop vs oracle stop.
  - **Verifier.** Factually accurate: policy.py:21,23 shows cum_profit = np.cumsum(tau_true[order] - cost) and stop = int(np.argmax(cum_profit)) — realised profit and stop selection both use tau_true. No app text discloses that this is truth-realised validation; the intro cell (lines 29-37) frames everything as 'the decision'. Worse, the plot legend (plots.py:91-93) labels the blue curve 'model policy' vs green 'oracle (knows truth)', implying the blue curve does not use truth when its y-values and stop …

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `apps/confounding_sensitivity.py:54-63 (drift precompute), with src/cmp/dgp.py:58-63`
  - **Issue.** The tipping-point headline ('flips at s ~ 1.0') rests on a single-seed drift curve whose first step is an RNG-stream artifact, with no Monte Carlo band. dgp.uplift_customers draws U = rng.normal(n) only when confounder_strength > 0, so the s=0 point uses a different treatment-assignment and noise realisation than every s>0 point; the drift jumps EUR 6.33 -> EUR 7.53 between s=0 and s=0.25 even though the actual confounding bias at s=0.25 is roughly EUR 0.1.
  - **Evidence.** Recomputed the app's exact loop: true ATE 5.76; drift[0]=6.33 (s=0), drift[1]=7.53 (s=0.25); first crossing of the EUR 8 cost at s=1.0 — matching the committed snapshot ('tipping point is strength ~ 1.0', 'estimate EUR 6.3', 'True ATE EUR 5.8'). dgp.py lines 58-63: the else-branch (s=0) skips the rng.normal(size=n) draw for U, shifting all subsequent T-uniform and noise draws.
  - **Why it matters.** The app's one takeaway number — 'the tipping point is strength ~ 1.0' — is mostly a seed artifact plus sampling noise (single-realisation OLS ATE SE ~ EUR 0.5 at n=1000, and the true margin to the cost line is only EUR 2.2). The repo's own quality bar demands sensitivity RANGES, not single points; here the flagship sensitivity demo violates it, and an audience member watching the first slider step sees the estimate leap with almost no hidden confounding.
  - **Fix.** In the DGP, always draw U (multiply by strength afterwards) so the stream is identical across strengths; in the app, average the drift curve over ~10 seeds and shade the min-max or 90% band, quoting the tipping point as a range (e.g. 's ~ 0.8-1.6').
  - **Verifier.** Attempted refutation failed on every point; I reproduced the reviewer's numbers exactly and ran the two counterfactual checks that would have falsified the claim.

(a) Factual accuracy — confirmed by reading and exact reproduction:
- src/cmp/dgp.py lines 58-63: `U = rng.normal(size=n)` is drawn only in the `confounder_strength > 0` branch; the else-branch sets `U = np.zeros(n)` without consuming the stream, so the subsequent `rng.uniform(size=n)` treatment draw (line 64) and `rng.normal(0, 8, n)` outcome noise (line 68) come from a shifted stream at s=0 versus every s>0. Exactly as the reviewer described.
- apps/confounding_sensitivity.py lines 43-64: single seed=7, n=1000, strengths linspac…
  - **Corrected statement.** The finding stands as written. One refinement from verification: over 20 seeds the tipping point ranges roughly 1.0-2.5 with median 2.0, so the committed headline "≈1.0" is not just noisy but sits at the extreme fragile end of the seed distribution — the finding, if anything, understates the distortion.

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `apps/synthetic_control_placebo.py:73-79 (donor construction and placebo call)`
  - **Issue.** When the user selects a non-treated market — which the intro text explicitly invites ('pick any other market') — the truly treated dma_00 remains (a) in the donor pool used to build the selected market's synthetic counterfactual, and (b) in the placebo set. Its planted +12% post-launch lift (~ +17 EUR 000/week) contaminates both. Standard synthetic-control practice excludes known-treated units from the donor pool. Additionally, setting the launch slider above week 40 while dma_00 is selected silently mixes 40+ treated weeks into the pre-fit window, with no on-screen explanation.
  - **Evidence.** Measured with the app's exact code path: treated=dma_05 -> weight on dma_00 = 0.084, post-gap mean -5.53, p=0.150; dma_00's true post effect averages +16.97. placebo_in_space (estimators.py:299-322) iterates j over all units including dma_00 when treated_idx != 0.
  - **Why it matters.** The app's own pedagogical claim for this exploration is 'the test's specificity in action'. But the counterfactual for a placebo market can be biased upward by the treated donor (measured: dma_05's synthetic puts weight 0.084 on dma_00, contributing ~ -1.4/week to a post-gap of -5.5), so the audience may see a spurious negative 'effect', and dma_00's real-effect gap sits inside the placebo spaghetti inflating the null spread (conservative for p, but muddies the 'is the treated gap an outlier?' read). A methods-aware attendee will spot the treated unit in the donor pool immediately.
  - **Fix.** When the selected market is not dma_00, drop dma_00 from both the donor pool and the placebo set (the app knows the ground truth), or add an on-screen toggle 'exclude the truly treated market from donors' and a one-line note; also add a caption warning when launch > 40 with dma_00 selected that the pre-fit window now contains treated weeks (or cap the slider at 40 for dma_00).
  - **Verifier.** Factual claims all verified by reading and by reproducing the app's exact code path: (1) dgp.geo_panel (src/cmp/dgp.py:114-117) writes the +12% lift into sales[0] (dma_00), true post effect mean +16.97 €000/week; (2) apps/synthetic_control_placebo.py:72 builds donors as np.delete(sales, treated_idx, 0), so with treated=dma_05 the truly treated dma_00 stays in the donor pool — reproduced weight on dma_00 = 0.0836, post-gap mean -5.53, with dma_00 contributing ~-1.42/week of that spurious negative gap; (3) placebo_in_space (src/cmp/estimators.py:308-310) skips only treated_idx, so dma_00 enters the placebo set when another market is selected — reproduced p = 0.150 with 19 placebos kept, exactl…

- **🟠 MAJOR · statistical — ✅ verified** — `apps/uplift_policy_explorer.py:51 (bcf call), with src/cmp/estimators.py:132-135`
  - **Issue.** The app hard-codes a coarse BCF posterior (draws=200, tune=200, chains=2, m=40 - i.e. ~400 short-tuned, autocorrelated BART draws), ignores the repo's CMP_FAST/full-profile convention (notebook 01 uses PROF with 600/600/4chains/m=100 in full mode), and bcf() itself sets compute_convergence_checks=False, so no r-hat/ESS warning can ever surface. There is no on-screen caveat that this is a fast approximate posterior.
  - **Evidence.** Line 51: est.bcf(X, T, y, _phat, seed=60, draws=200, tune=200, chains=2, m=40); estimators.py:134: compute_convergence_checks=False. Snapshot: 'on the 619 straddlers EUR 337'. Notebook 01 cell 1: PROF = dict(draws=600, tune=600, chains=4, m=100) if not FAST.
  - **Why it matters.** Every headline the sliders re-derive is a posterior tail functional: P(tau>c) against a confidence bar up to 0.95, 5th/95th CATE quantiles for the straddler set, and the EVPI. With ~400 correlated draws these are coarse, and the visible symptom is already in the committed snapshot: 619 of 1000 customers are 'straddlers', so the app's closing advice ('put the straddlers into an A/B test') means testing 62% of the base — partly genuine uncertainty, but partly an under-sampled-posterior artifact, and there is no diagnostic or note to separate the two. This is exactly the flagged risk of FAST-profile outputs undermining a lecture-grade figure.
  - **Fix.** Respect CMP_FAST (fast profile for rehearsal, full for the lecture build), add a one-line md note 'posterior: S draws, fast profile — straddler counts shrink with the full run', and surface a minimal ESS/r-hat check (e.g. az.ess on tau) so the app can state the tail probabilities are resolved at the chosen confidence bar.
  - **Verifier.** Factually accurate on every citation: apps/uplift_policy_explorer.py:51 hard-codes est.bcf(..., draws=200, tune=200, chains=2, m=40) with no CMP_FAST reference anywhere in apps/ (grep: zero hits); src/cmp/estimators.py:134 hard-codes compute_convergence_checks=False inside bcf() and the **kw passthrough cannot re-enable it, so no r-hat/ESS warning can ever surface; notebook 01 (nb_text line 85) defines PROF = 600/600/4 chains/m=100 in full mode gated on CMP_FAST, confirming the repo convention the app ignores; the committed snapshot apps/__marimo__/session/uplift_policy_explorer.py.json:87 renders "on the 619 'straddlers' … €337" out of 1000; and the app's markdown cells contain no fast-post…

- **🟡 MINOR · statistical** — `apps/confounding_sensitivity.py:49-52 (adjusted_ate) and on-screen labels`
  - **Issue.** 'Estimated ATE (adjusting for observed X only)' is the OLS coefficient on T in a constant-effect linear model. Under the DGP's heterogeneous tau and selection-on-observables, that coefficient is a conditional-variance-weighted effect plus functional-form bias, not the ATE — it misses the truth even with zero hidden confounding (6.33 vs true 5.76; the same OLS under the randomized regime gives 5.52).
  - **Evidence.** Recomputed with the app's exact code: true ATE 5.76, drift[0]=6.33 at s=0 (matches snapshot 'estimate EUR 6.3 ... True ATE EUR 5.8'); randomized-regime OLS 5.52.
  - **Why it matters.** The curve visibly starts EUR 0.5 above the dashed 'true ATE' line at s=0, and the narrative attributes all deviation to the hidden confounder. After a session devoted to heterogeneous effects, a sharp attendee will ask why the estimate is already wrong at zero confounding — and the app has no answer on screen.
  - **Fix.** One added sentence: 'even at zero hidden confounding the OLS coefficient is not exactly the ATE — it is a variance-weighted average under heterogeneous effects; the drift beyond that baseline is what the hidden confounder adds'; or subtract the s=0 baseline and plot the drift relative to it.

- **🟡 MINOR · pedagogical** — `apps/synthetic_control_placebo.py:94-105 (verdict md cell)`
  - **Issue.** The verdict reports 'p = 0.053 -> significant at the 0.1 level' without showing how many placebos survived the 3x pre-RMSE filter. Only 18 of 29 were kept, so 0.053 = 1/19 is the minimum attainable p — the real effect sits exactly at the resolution floor of the test, and the audience cannot see the denominator that gives p its meaning.
  - **Evidence.** Snapshot: p = 0.053; measured with the app's code path: 18 placebos kept of 29, so (0+1)/(18+1) = 0.0526. placebo_in_space returns only (gaps, real_gap, p) — kept-count not surfaced.
  - **Why it matters.** Permutation p-values are only interpretable relative to the number of permutations; 'p = 0.053' looks like a continuous quantity when it is the best possible outcome of a 19-point null. If someone asks 'what would a stronger effect show?' the honest answer is 'exactly the same p', which the app should pre-empt.
  - **Fix.** Report 'p = 0.053 (rank 1 of 19 after the 3x RMSE filter; smallest attainable p = 0.053)' — placebo_gaps.shape[0] is already available in the cell.

- **🟡 MINOR · consistency** — `README.md:158-159 ('Interactive apps' section)`
  - **Issue.** The blanket claim 'the expensive posterior is computed once, and the sliders only re-derive the decision' is verified true for the uplift and confounding apps (their heavy cells depend only on imports), but false for app-sc: it has no posterior at all (SLSQP point fit) and the full fit plus 29 placebo refits re-run on every dropdown/slider interaction.
  - **Evidence.** apps/synthetic_control_placebo.py:65-79: the analysis cell takes launch and market as inputs and calls sc_effect_slsqp + placebo_in_space inside it. Timed at 0.22 s per interaction with the app's exact parameters.
  - **Why it matters.** The README is the pitch for the demo architecture; anyone opening synthetic_control_placebo.py expecting the fit-once pattern will find a recompute-everything pattern. (Latency is fine — measured 0.22 s per interaction — and the app's own docstring is honest about SLSQP.)
  - **Fix.** Reword the README to 'the expensive step is computed once where there is one (BCF posterior, drift curve); the synthetic-control app instead uses a fast point fitter so each refit is ~0.2 s' .

- **🟡 MINOR · code** — `apps/uplift_policy_explorer.py:71-72`
  - **Issue.** The comment 'top-ranked mailable customers are the ones we score' mislabels idx = np.arange(n): it takes the first n rows in simulation order (an arbitrary, effectively random subset), not customers ranked by anything. Also the app simulates n=1000 while notebook 01 uses N=900 (fast) / 1600 (full), so app and notebook headline numbers will not match.
  - **Evidence.** Line 72: idx = np.arange(n) with n from base_slider; dgp.uplift_customers rows are generated iid with no ordering. Notebook 01 cell 1: N = 900 if FAST else 1600.
  - **Why it matters.** The behaviour is statistically fine (iid rows, so a random subset is a legitimate 'mailable base'), but the comment invites a future editor — or a code-reading attendee — to believe the base slider selects the best customers, which would make the profit-curve intercept meaningless.
  - **Fix.** Change the comment to 'first n rows = a random subset standing in for the mailable base', and align n with the notebook (or state the difference in the intro md).

- **🟡 MINOR · code** — `apps/confounding_sensitivity.py:109 (verdict md)`
  - **Issue.** If the drift curve never crossed the cost line, tip would be NaN and the verdict would render 'The tipping point is strength ~ nan' — the plot helper guards NaN (plots.py:142) but the markdown f-string f'{tip:.1f}' does not. Latent today (drift crosses at 1.0 with the committed seed), but any change to seed, n, or cost could trigger it live.
  - **Evidence.** Line 63: tip = ... if np.any(drift > COST) else float('nan'); line 109 formats tip unconditionally.
  - **Why it matters.** A 'nan' in the on-screen verdict of a lecture demo is exactly the class of edge that robustness review is for; the fix is one conditional.
  - **Fix.** Guard the sentence: 'The estimate never crosses the cost line over this range' when np.isnan(tip).

- **⚪ POLISH · code** — `apps/synthetic_control_placebo.py:90 and apps/uplift_policy_explorer.py:53`
  - **Issue.** Hand-edited, stale generated cell stubs: the SC analysis cell's return lists market, which the cell does not define (it is an input), and the uplift BCF cell defines X, T, y but omits them from its return. marimo 0.23 re-derives defs/refs from the AST so this is harmless at runtime, but the file no longer round-trips cleanly with what marimo would generate.
  - **Evidence.** Line 90: return L, fig, p_space, market, pre_rmse — market is only read (line 66); line 53: return cate, cate_point, tau while X, T, y are assigned without underscore prefix at lines 46-48.
  - **Why it matters.** Signature/return lines that disagree with the cell body mislead anyone reading the apps as plain Python and will produce noisy diffs the next time marimo rewrites the files on save.
  - **Fix.** Open each app once in marimo edit and save (regenerating stubs), or underscore-prefix the genuinely cell-local names (X, T, y) to make locality explicit.

---

### README & repo claims

**Grade: good** · 0 critical · 1 major · 4 findings total

Claim-by-claim cross-check of README.md and reports/README.md against the notebooks, Makefile, src/cmp, tests, and docs/causal_marketing_cookbook.pdf. The README is unusually honest overall: the technique-index library mappings for 01-06 and 08-11 are real (02's pathmc m.ate/m.cate calls are literal do()-contrasts, so the 'do-operator' claim holds), every design-decision bullet checks out against code (BART gotcha test exists at tests/test_package.py:50; Anchor B really lands on P(lift>cost)=0.62 TEST FURTHER; CausalPy 0.8.x pins are documented in src/cmp/estimators.py:341-346), all quickstart commands match real Makefile targets, notebook numbering matches the cookbook PDF 1:1, CMP_REAL gates exactly the three claimed notebooks (00, 01, 05 - Hillstrom in 01's section 6b, LaLonde in 00 and 05), and reports/ contains one PDF per notebook. Four claims are overstated: (1) the technique index and the 'verbatim cookbook mapping' claim say notebook 07 uses CausalPy, but the anchor notebook is a fully manual Dirichlet-simplex SC on the core env where CausalPy cannot even install, and this deviation - unlike nb03's analogous one - is not recorded in the design-decisions section (the cmp.estimators CausalPy SC wrapper exists but is dead code); (2) posterior predictive checks are attributed to '(00, 01)' but notebook 00 contains none; (3) the IHDP row in the real-data table implies a runnable CATE benchmark, but load_ihdp is used by no notebook or test; (4) 'multi-seed recovery stability' and 'E-values, 2-D contours' are listed under 'Every notebook is deep on four axes' but exist only in 01 (and 05 for E-values).

**Strengths.**
- Nearly all named diagnostics genuinely exist where claimed: Qini/AUUC and uplift-by-decile in 01, AIPW cross-checks in both 00 and 01, the live staggered-adoption/TWFE-bias demo and pre-trends in 08, McCrary + bandwidth + placebo-cutoff (€70/€130) + polynomial-order robustness in 09, placebo-in-time + residual autocorrelation in 10, first-stage F + Wald + exclusion stress in 11, Abadie RMSE-ratio and leave-one-out donors in 07.
- Design-decision bullets are verifiably true against code, not marketing: tests/test_package.py:50 test_bart_cate_is_nonzero exists; the S-learner flattening demo is explicit in 01's bake-off (cells around lines 654-885 of the extract); nb03's hierarchical deviation and toward-zero simultaneity demo are both present; nb06 leads with the naive-vs-adjusted contrast and repeatedly defers absolute levels to a geo experiment; the CausalPy 0.8.x API workarounds (post_treatment bool, dummy treated, numeric seasonality, cores=1) are documented verbatim in src/cmp/estimators.py:341-346.
- The Anchor B honesty claim is exactly right: notebook 07 outputs P_lift_gt_cost = 0.6208 with decision TEST FURTHER, matching the README's 'P(lift>cost)≈0.6' promise of a genuinely borderline call.
- Operational claims all reproduce: every Makefile target named in the README exists (env-legacy, kernels, test, test-fast, app-uplift/confounding/sc, reports); make test really executes notebooks headless via tests/test_notebooks.py with per-notebook kernel routing; all 12 notebooks declare the kernel (cmp-core for 00-05+07, cmp-legacy for 06, 08-11) exactly as the environment-split table states; reports/ has one PDF per notebook.
- The '02 uses pathmc's do-operator' claim survives scrutiny at the source level: pathmc's ate()/cate() are documented shorthands for do(set={treatment: hi}) - do(set={treatment: lo}) contrasts (pathmc/_model.py:1055-1103), and 02 also derives its estimand in do-notation in the markdown.
- The real-data section's fine print is accurate: exactly three notebooks (00, 01, 05) are gated on CMP_REAL, fetching what the table says, and every non-gated notebook does carry a real-data pointer in its intro as promised.

- **🟠 MAJOR · consistency** — `README.md:84 (technique-index row 07), README.md:199-201 (cookbook 'verbatim' mapping claim), README.md:221-226 (CausalPy design bullet), src/cmp/estimators.py:360 (unused synthetic_control_cp)`
  - **Issue.** The technique index lists notebook 07 (Anchor B) as 'CausalPy / manual SC', and the design-decisions section claims the repo follows the cookbook's technique-to-library mapping 'verbatim' - but notebook 07 contains zero references to CausalPy (grep of both the extract and the .ipynb returns 0). It uses only the hand-rolled est.synthetic_control (Dirichlet-simplex PyMC model) and est.sc_effect_slsqp from cmp.estimators, and it runs on the core (pymc>=6) env where causalpy 0.8.1 (pinned pymc<6, per the README's own environment-split section) cannot be installed. docs/causal_marketing_cookbook.pdf section 7 explicitly maps this technique to CausalPy's SyntheticControl + WeightedSumFitter. The CausalPy SC wrapper cmp.estimators.synthetic_control_cp exists but is dead code - no notebook, app, or test calls it. Unlike notebook 03's analogous library deviation, which gets its own design-decision bullet, this deviation on an anchor notebook is recorded nowhere.
  - **Evidence.** grep -ci causalpy notebooks/07_geo_lift_synthetic_control.ipynb -> 0. 07 extract imports only 'from cmp import dgp, estimators as est, policy, plots' and calls est.synthetic_control / est.sc_effect_slsqp / est.placebo_in_space (extract lines 60, 184, 246, 388-458). Kernelspec of 07 is cmp-core. grep -rl synthetic_control_cp over src/tests/notebooks matches only src/cmp/estimators.py itself. Cookbook PDF p.6, section 7: 'CausalPy - Synthetic Control ... cp.SyntheticControl(... model=cp.pymc_models.WeightedSumFitter...)'.
  - **Why it matters.** This is the flagship program-evaluation notebook of the lecture. A student or colleague who opens 07 expecting the CausalPy API from the index (or from the cookbook PDF the README says is followed verbatim) finds a different library and a different environment, and the README's promise that deviations are 'recorded as made, per the brief' is visibly broken for the most prominent case. It also leaves an untested code path (synthetic_control_cp) implicitly advertised by the 'CausalPy wrappers' phrase in the src/cmp description.
  - **Fix.** Change the 07 row's library cell to 'manual Bayesian SC (Dirichlet-simplex, PyMC)' and add a design-decision bullet recording the deviation and its reason (Anchor B kept on the core env / CausalPy's pymc<6 pin; manual model exposes the weights and placebo machinery the lecture needs). Either wire synthetic_control_cp into a short legacy-env appendix cell or a test, or delete it.

- **🟡 MINOR · consistency** — `README.md:57-58 (four-axes bullet: 'AIPW doubly-robust cross-checks & posterior predictive checks (00, 01)')`
  - **Issue.** Posterior predictive checks are claimed for notebooks 00 and 01, but notebook 00 contains no PPC at all: grep for 'predictive'/'ppc'/'sample_posterior_predictive' returns 0 matches in both the extract and notebooks/00_foundations.ipynb. The PPC exists only in 01 (extract line 334 'Model criticism - the posterior predictive check (PPC)' and line 347 plots.ppc_plot). The AIPW half of the claim is correct for both notebooks.
  - **Evidence.** grep -c -e ppc -e posterior_predictive -e predictive notebooks/00_foundations.ipynb -> 0; same greps on the 00 extract -> 0. 01 extract lines 334-347 show the PPC section and plots.ppc_plot call.
  - **Why it matters.** This is a named-diagnostic claim in the repo's headline quality statement ('Every notebook is deep on four axes'); a reader who checks it against 00 finds it false, which cheapens the adjacent claims that are actually true. It also flags a small real gap: 00 fits a PyMC model whose fit quality is never criticised.
  - **Fix.** Either change the bullet to '...posterior predictive checks (01)' or add a small PPC (plots.ppc_plot already exists in cmp.plots) to notebook 00's estimation step - the latter is a few lines and closes the gap rather than the claim.

- **🟡 MINOR · consistency** — `README.md:149 (real-data table, IHDP row) and src/cmp/data.py:100 (load_ihdp)`
  - **Issue.** The real-data table's third row - '(CATE benchmark) | IHDP - semi-synthetic, known true effects (cmp.data.load_ihdp) | real covariates with a known truth, for grading CATE recovery' - describes a capability nothing in the repo exercises: load_ihdp is defined in src/cmp/data.py:100 but is imported or called by no notebook, no app, and no test (repo-wide grep for 'ihdp' matches only data.py). Unlike the Hillstrom and LaLonde rows, there is no gated cell a reader can run.
  - **Evidence.** grep -rli ihdp across src/, tests/, notebooks/, apps/ matches only src/cmp/data.py. The section intro says 'three notebooks also fetch a real public dataset' and exactly three (00, 01, 05) are CMP_REAL-gated - the IHDP row is the odd one out with no notebook.
  - **Why it matters.** The row sits in a table whose other rows map to runnable CMP_REAL-gated notebook cells, so it reads as 'this benchmark exists in a notebook'. A reader looking for the IHDP CATE-recovery grading (the natural real-data complement to Anchor A's simulated PEHE checks) finds nothing to run, and the loader itself is untested dead code.
  - **Fix.** Either add a CMP_REAL-gated IHDP cell to notebook 01 (fit T-learner/BCF on IHDP covariates, report PEHE against the known effects - a natural Depth-D addendum), or annotate the row as 'loader provided for your own benchmarking; not wired into a notebook' and add a smoke test for load_ihdp.

- **🟡 MINOR · consistency** — `README.md:54 and README.md:66-69 ('Every notebook is deep on four axes' -> 'Rigorous validation - ... multi-seed recovery stability, and sensitivity ranges (E-values, 2-D contours)')`
  - **Issue.** The validation bullet sits under the explicit claim 'Every notebook is deep on four axes, not just the anchors', but two of its three named items are anchor/near-anchor-only: multi-seed recovery stability appears solely in notebook 01 (grep for multi-seed/across-seeds/seed-stability phrasing returns 0 hits in all of 00, 02-11), and E-values / 2-D sensitivity contours appear only in 01 and 05. Unlike the technical-diagnostics bullet, this bullet gives no per-notebook attribution, so it reads as a repo-wide guarantee.
  - **Evidence.** grep -ci for 'multi-seed|seed stability|across seeds|seeds' per extract: 01 -> 4 hits, all other eleven notebooks -> 0. grep -li 'e-value' -> only 01 and 05; grep -li 'contour' -> only 01 and 05.
  - **Why it matters.** A sharp reader (or MBA student told 'every notebook validates this rigorously') who opens, say, 08 or 10 looking for multi-seed stability or a sensitivity range will not find one, and the header's 'not just the anchors' framing makes the overstatement explicit rather than incidental. The per-notebook attributions in the neighbouring diagnostics bullet show the authors know how to scope claims - this bullet should be scoped the same way.
  - **Fix.** Scope the bullet like the diagnostics one - e.g. 'multi-seed recovery stability (01), sensitivity ranges: E-values & 2-D contours (01, 05)' - or add a cheap 3-seed recovery loop to the remaining notebooks (each already has a seeded DGP, so it is a small addition) to make the universal claim true.
